# Breton


The Direnni left a significant mark on the Bretons: the race's obsession with nobility, status, and lineage can be traced back to their days as vassals of Clan Direnni.<sup>[[13]](#cite_note-ONBS-15)</sup> Bretons possess an inborn and instinctive bond for the [magical arts](Lore_Magic.md), often attributed to their elven blood,<sup>[[14]](#cite_note-16)</sup><sup>[[15]](#cite_note-TCCAG-17)</sup><sup>[[16]](#cite_note-MWGDB-18)</sup> and they are known for their intelligence and quick, perceptive grasp of [spellcraft](Lore_Magic.md), [enchantment](Lore_Enchanting.md), and [alchemy](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Alchemy).<sup>[[17]](#cite_note-TS-19)</sup><sup>[[18]](#cite_note-HOTIB-20)</sup><sup>[[19]](#cite_note-KE9-21)</sup><sup>[[16]](#cite_note-MWGDB-18)</sup>

Bretons are also noted for having some natural resistance to destructive and magical energies, a trait associated with their race but not tied to their elven lineage.<sup>[[20]](#cite_note-Altmer Stats-22)</sup><sup>[[16]](#cite_note-MWGDB-18)</sup><sup>[[21]](#cite_note-23)</sup><sup>[[22]](#cite_note-24)</sup> However, their shorter [human lifespans](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Lifespan) place them at a disadvantage compared to their elven counterparts, whose naturally long lives grant them far more time to study, refine their craft, and establish lasting reputations.<sup>[[23]](#cite_note-IWADE-25)</sup><sup>[[24]](#cite_note-26)</sup><sup>[[25]](#cite_note-LAHT-27)</sup><sup>[[26]](#cite_note-28)</sup> Even so, their potential has not gone unrecognized. The Assistant [Sapiarch](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Sapiarch) of Culinary Arts once remarked that Bretons were the second-best sorcerers after the [Altmer](Lore_Altmer.md), believing they had the potential to achieve more than they have demonstrated so far if given equal opportunity.<sup>[[27]](#cite_note-Cookbook2-29)</sup> While it is often difficult for an individual Breton to leave a lasting mark on the greater magical community—since the widespread mystical aptitude among their people makes it harder for any one mage to stand out<sup>[[25]](#cite_note-LAHT-27)</sup> —Bretons have nonetheless produced mages considered among the greatest in Tamriel,<sup>[[UOL 3]](#cite_note-ESOLI-30)</sup> with notable figures such as [Voernet](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Voernet), [Druid King Kasorayn](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Kasorayn), and [Gyron Vardengroet](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Gyron_Vardengroet).<sup>[[25]](#cite_note-LAHT-27)</sup>

Bretons have also retained a connection to their human [druidic](Lore_Druid.md) forebears, and are believed to be the reason for their "shrewd resourcefulness".<sup>[[28]](#cite_note-BOTSEAB-31)</sup><sup>:28</sup> Druidic spellcraft (which differs from the arcane) is said to be the first truly Breton creation.<sup>[[29]](#cite_note-ONLOTB-32)</sup> Bretons have a natural affinity for environmental manipulation,<sup>[[30]](#cite_note-ONILES-33)</sup> which druids believe should be utilized to enhance or perfect nature, reshaping it just as their god [Y'ffre](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Y%27ffre) once did.<sup>[[31]](#cite_note-ONHIDS-34)</sup><sup>[[32]](#cite_note-ONWD-35)</sup> What it means to be a Breton is considered an age-old quandary by their people.<sup>[[33]](#cite_note-MTCSSM-36)</sup> To make sense of it all, some may focus on a specific aspect of their culture, or seek to blend it all together.<sup>[[29]](#cite_note-ONLOTB-32)</sup><sup>[[34]](#cite_note-ESOSSM-37)</sup><sup>[[35]](#cite_note-ONCDD-38)</sup> Some Bretons hold their elven heritage in high esteem, which may influence them to worship [Phynaster](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Phynaster), the patron deity and "teacher" of the Direnni.<sup>[[36]](#cite_note-VOFB-39)</sup> Others attempt to seek out the druidic roots of their Nedic ancestors and reconnect with nature.<sup>[[33]](#cite_note-MTCSSM-36)</sup><sup>[[29]](#cite_note-ONLOTB-32)</sup>

High Rock is fractious and divided politically,<sup>[[37]](#cite_note-PGE1High-40)</sup> which is seemingly encouraged by the layout of the land itself.<sup>[[38]](#cite_note-POT-41)</sup> Warfare between [kingdoms](Lore_Kingdoms_of_High_Rock.md) accounts for much of Breton history.<sup>[[15]](#cite_note-TCCAG-17)</sup> Despite this, Bretons across the province share many facets of culture, including [language](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Bretic), bardic traditions, and heroic tales.<sup>[[37]](#cite_note-PGE1High-40)</sup><sup>[[38]](#cite_note-POT-41)</sup> Bretons make up the peasantry, soldiery, magical elite, and ruling families of the feudal kingdoms competing for power within High Rock,<sup>[[37]](#cite_note-PGE1High-40)</sup><sup>[[39]](#cite_note-TIEGTT-42)</sup><sup>[[38]](#cite_note-POT-41)</sup> but they are found across [Tamriel](Lore_Tamriel.md), often as merchants or mercenaries.<sup>[[12]](#cite_note-Adventure Game-14)</sup> [Knighthood](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Knights) is pivotal to the Breton identity; its earliest practitioners served under Clan Direnni,<sup>[[40]](#cite_note-ONARCP-43)</sup><sup>[[41]](#cite_note-ONTNS-44)</sup> but knights are credited with kickstarting High Rock's modern cultural history through tales of liberating the race from their elven oppressors.<sup>[[42]](#cite_note-ONTKOHR-45)</sup> These knights of old set the example for those that followed by going on grand quests for adventure and glory.<sup>[[UOL 1]](#cite_note-ON2022-9)</sup> In their free time, Breton youths of all walks of life imitate knights through chivalric pursuits in their thoughts or by their actions.<sup>[[37]](#cite_note-PGE1High-40)</sup> Indeed, the profession encapsulates the traditional chivalric principles of Breton society,<sup>[[42]](#cite_note-ONTKOHR-45)</sup><sup>[[43]](#cite_note-TL-46)</sup><sup>[[44]](#cite_note-ONDHQ-47)</sup> and the "quest-obsession" that has become a national identity for High Rock.<sup>[[37]](#cite_note-PGE1High-40)</sup>

## Appearance
[![](https://images.uesp.net/thumb/2/22/ON-misc-Breton_Pointed_Ear.png/200px-ON-misc-Breton_Pointed_Ear.png)](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:ON-misc-Breton_Pointed_Ear.png) [](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:ON-misc-Breton_Pointed_Ear.png) A male Breton displaying a remnant of elven blood: pointed ears (ESO) Whether Bretons are humans or elves is a topic of debate,<sup>[[7]](#cite_note-MDBMM-7)</sup> with most people believing that they are the former.<sup>[[6]](#cite_note-PGE3A-6)</sup> The earliest Bretons were referred to as **Manmeri**,<sup>[[37]](#cite_note-PGE1High-40)</sup> **Half-Elves**,<sup>[[1]](#cite_note-TBMOP-1)</sup> and possibly **[Chimera](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Chimera)** (from the Altmeri word for "change"),<sup>[[45]](#cite_note-TBOG-48)</sup> and were more elven in appearance.<sup>[[1]](#cite_note-TBMOP-1)</sup> These elf-like physical features included pointed ears, angled faces, slender bodies, and distinctive eyes.<sup>[[7]](#cite_note-MDBMM-7)</sup> Although the terms are archaic, some modern Bretons such as druids embrace this heritage and still refer to themselves as Manmer or Half-Elves.<sup>[[32]](#cite_note-ONWD-35)</sup><sup>[[31]](#cite_note-ONHIDS-34)</sup><sup>[[34]](#cite_note-ESOSSM-37)</sup> Due to their mixed heritage, Bretons have been described disparagingly as "degraded hybrids" or a "mongrel race".<sup>[[1]](#cite_note-TBMOP-1)</sup><sup>[[2]](#cite_note-Cot DC-2)</sup>

When the Manmer fully transitioned to modern Bretons is unknown, though by the fourth century of the [First Era](Lore_First_Era.md), the ethnicity of the Druids of Galen was already "Breton-y".<sup>[[8]](#cite_note-LATD-8)</sup> Modern Bretons, by and large, are pale-skinned<sup>[[46]](#cite_note-DFRB-49)</sup> and slightly built, less muscular than [Nords](Lore_Nord.md) and [Redguards](Lore_Redguard.md).<sup>[[39]](#cite_note-TIEGTT-42)</sup> Compared to the other human races, Bretons have more rounded and softer features.<sup>[[47]](#cite_note-50)</sup><sup>:126</sup> Bretons also typically have straight or wavy hair,<sup>[[46]](#cite_note-DFRB-49)</sup> and possess more defined features such as high and delicate cheekbones, sensuous lips,<sup>[[48]](#cite_note-t IC173-51)</sup><sup>:173</sup> and have been depicted with pronounced brow ridges.<sup>[[49]](#cite_note-PGDrawing-52)</sup> Some Bretons even display pointed ears much like elves.<sup>[[50]](#cite_note-53)</sup><sup>[[28]](#cite_note-BOTSEAB-31)</sup><sup>:28</sup> The Bretons' elvish physical features have waned and become more human over time, but have not vanished.<sup>[[7]](#cite_note-MDBMM-7)</sup>

## History

### Origin
[![](https://images.uesp.net/thumb/2/22/LO-map-High_Rock_%28Anthology%29.jpg/200px-LO-map-High_Rock_%28Anthology%29.jpg)](File_LO-map-High_Rock_(Anthology).jpg.md) [](File_LO-map-High_Rock_(Anthology).jpg.md) [High Rock](Lore_High_Rock.md), home of the Bretons The province of High Rock is the ancestral home to the modern day Breton people, and by tradition the name High Rock originates from humanity.<sup>[[51]](#cite_note-TVS-54)</sup><sup>[[52]](#cite_note-ONSHV4-55)</sup> Before them, there's evidence that a [beastfolk](Lore_Beastfolk.md) population were High Rock's original inhabitants, though they did not build permanent communities, and what interactions they had with men or mer are unknown.<sup>[[53]](#cite_note-PGE3High-56)</sup> Considered a cursed and hostile race in the modern day, the [dreugh](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Dreugh) are thought to have once had a great civilization that flourished around the [Iliac Bay](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Iliac_Bay) before the First Era.<sup>[[54]](#cite_note-DUG-57)</sup> Legends abound of the hill giants, a race of [giants](Lore_Giant.md) from [Skyrim](Lore_Skyrim.md) that migrated to the present day region of [Rivenspire](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Rivenspire), bringing along their massive mammoths. Though they are no longer around, giant remains found within a cavern system in the region gives credence to this theory.<sup>[[55]](#cite_note-58)</sup><sup>[[56]](#cite_note-ONBF-59)</sup><sup>[[nb 3]](#intnote_Hill_Giants)</sup>

Bretons themselves originated from Nedes and Aldmer interbreeding<sup>[[6]](#cite_note-PGE3A-6)</sup> for centuries as far back as the Merethic Era.<sup>[[7]](#cite_note-MDBMM-7)</sup><sup>[[8]](#cite_note-LATD-8)</sup> Who first arrived in High Rock is debated in scholarly circles: some believe that Nedic civilization and their [Druid King](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Druid_King) were already established in the province when the Aldmer arrived,<sup>[[7]](#cite_note-MDBMM-7)</sup> while others claim that the Nedes arrived in High Rock after, encountering the elves gradually with a variety of reactions and outcomes.<sup>[[57]](#cite_note-FC-60)</sup><sup>[[53]](#cite_note-PGE3High-56)</sup><sup>[[UOL 4]](#cite_note-LSP:OAC-61)</sup>

The Nedic ancestors of the Bretons were a people that survived in ancient High Rock by tapping into and nurturing nature.<sup>[[9]](#cite_note-LADCG-11)</sup><sup>[[32]](#cite_note-ONWD-35)</sup> They followed Y'ffre's True Way (later known as Druidism),<sup>[[33]](#cite_note-MTCSSM-36)</sup> in which the eponymous god took the forefront of their faith. Under it, one is to lead a life connecting with and valuing the natural world.<sup>[[58]](#cite_note-ESODA-62)</sup> Some reverence was also shown to the stars, especially the [Ritual constellation](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:The_Ritual).<sup>[[32]](#cite_note-ONWD-35)</sup> These Nedes are known by the retroactive nomenclature, the Druids of Galen,<sup>[[7]](#cite_note-MDBMM-7)</sup><sup>[[8]](#cite_note-LATD-8)</sup><sup>[[10]](#cite_note-RDBA-12)</sup><sup>[[4]](#cite_note-ONHIPTZ-4)</sup> (or proto-Bretons)<sup>[[UOL 2]](#cite_note-LTP2022-10)</sup><sup>[[9]](#cite_note-LADCG-11)</sup> and what would become their moniker is derived from a mythical "Galen", an entity or place which druids first came about.<sup>[[9]](#cite_note-LADCG-11)</sup> Regardless of the origin, it is agreed that the True Way was born in High Rock.<sup>[[59]](#cite_note-EOTD-63)</sup>

There is evidence of human settlements in High Rock dating back at least a thousand years before recorded history.<sup>[[60]](#cite_note-AHOD-64)</sup> Archaeological excavations have dated the ruins of Nedic habitation to as early as [ME 1000](Lore_Merethic_Era.md#ME_1000), predating [Ysgramor](Lore_Ysgramor.md) by centuries.<sup>[[57]](#cite_note-FC-60)</sup> The Nedes of [Stormhaven](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Stormhaven) had strained relations with the neighboring [Orc](Lore_Orc.md) clans, which regularly clashed with other Orc clans and their Nedic neighbors.<sup>[[61]](#cite_note-65)</sup>

Error creating thumbnail: File missing [](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:BT-concept-Breton_Female_2.png) Female Breton with Elvish ears The Aldmer that settled High Rock did so sparsely and in very specific locations,<sup>[[UOL 4]](#cite_note-LSP:OAC-61)</sup> and it is speculated that there was internal strife between the various Aldmer clans of High Rock.<sup>[[UOL 5]](#cite_note-66)</sup><sup>[[62]](#cite_note-ESODruid King-67)</sup> The most successful of these settlers were from Clan Direnni,<sup>[[53]](#cite_note-PGE3High-56)</sup> who came from the [Summerset Isles](Lore_Summerset_Isle.md) in the Middle Merethic Era and captured the [Adamantine Tower](Lore_Adamantine_Tower.md).<sup>[[63]](#cite_note-BTAOM-68)</sup><sup>[[64]](#cite_note-Once-69)</sup> Some believe the Direnni were following their destiny to rule from [Balfiera](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Balfiera), while others believed that they were exiled.<sup>[[65]](#cite_note-ESOBE-70)</sup> The Direnni didn't enslave the Nedes as the [Ayleids](Lore_Ayleid.md) of [Cyrodiil](Lore_Cyrodiil.md) did; instead, they ruled them as a noble caste. The elves established a system of feudal vassalage over their new subjects and took Nedic concubines.<sup>[[1]](#cite_note-TBMOP-1)</sup><sup>[[64]](#cite_note-Once-69)</sup> They inevitably interbred with their human subjects, producing Half-Elven children (also known as Manmer).<sup>[[1]](#cite_note-TBMOP-1)</sup><sup>[[37]](#cite_note-PGE1High-40)</sup>

#### The Direnni, Druids, and the Wyrd
[![](https://images.uesp.net/thumb/c/c8/ON-misc-Druid_King_Wyrd_and_Frii.png/200px-ON-misc-Druid_King_Wyrd_and_Frii.png)](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:ON-misc-Druid_King_Wyrd_and_Frii.png) [](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:ON-misc-Druid_King_Wyrd_and_Frii.png) Symbols for the Druid King (top), the Beldama Wyrd (left), the Glenmoril Wyrd (right), and later Frii (center) The Druids of Galen led the new race when it first emerged,<sup>[[UOL 6]](#cite_note-ESOLive Firesong-71)</sup> as children begat from Elf-Nede relations were considered sub-mer and not accepted by their Direnni parents. Instead, they were given privileged positions among the Nedes, which eventually led to a recognizable mixed-blood human caste dubbed "Bretons", from the Ehlnofex "beratu", meaning "half".<sup>[[7]](#cite_note-MDBMM-7)</sup><sup>[[1]](#cite_note-TBMOP-1)</sup> These Bretons were only allowed to marry humans, and over time, the Bretons' human features became more prominent than their elven traits.<sup>[[1]](#cite_note-TBMOP-1)</sup> Shortly after the Breton race emerged, Druidic spellcraft became the first truly Breton creation, and "druid" as a distinct identity was fully realized.<sup>[[32]](#cite_note-ONWD-35)</sup><sup>[[29]](#cite_note-ONLOTB-32)</sup> Though the term Manmer is archaic in the modern day, Breton druids embrace this heritage by still referring to themselves as such,<sup>[[32]](#cite_note-ONWD-35)</sup><sup>[[31]](#cite_note-ONHIDS-34)</sup> and believe in Breton's ability to enhance or perfect nature.<sup>[[31]](#cite_note-ONHIDS-34)</sup> Indeed, the modern Breton has a natural affinity for environmental manipulation.<sup>[[30]](#cite_note-ONILES-33)</sup>

Eventually, the witches of [the Wyrd](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:The_Wyrd) diverged from the True Way in a religious schism, ultimately driven away by what they called the "excesses of the Elves".<sup>[[32]](#cite_note-ONWD-35)</sup> In druidic belief, mortals<sup>[[32]](#cite_note-ONWD-35)</sup> were not meant to separate themselves from nature, as one can rejuvenate and enjoy Y'ffre's bounty through it.<sup>[[66]](#cite_note-72)</sup><sup>[[67]](#cite_note-ESODR-73)</sup> While the druids revere nature, they were not keen to isolate themselves and worship the untamed wilds.<sup>[[32]](#cite_note-ONWD-35)</sup><sup>[[68]](#cite_note-LABHI-74)</sup> Therein lies the primary difference in culture between druids and the Wyrd: the Wyrd abandoned civilization in favor of living in the wilds.<sup>[[32]](#cite_note-ONWD-35)</sup> They believe that they are nature itself: the forest, the plants and beasts within it, even the weather.<sup>[[69]](#cite_note-75)</sup><sup>[[32]](#cite_note-ONWD-35)</sup> In contrast, druids accepted what they interpreted as their "proper place" as people, and embraced the idea that civilization can coexist alongside nature.<sup>[[32]](#cite_note-ONWD-35)</sup><sup>[[68]](#cite_note-LABHI-74)</sup><sup>[[67]](#cite_note-ESODR-73)</sup><sup>[[70]](#cite_note-ESOWM-76)</sup> The Druids of Galen and the Wyrd disapproved of each other's lifestyles: the druids found the ways of the Wyrd unsavory, and the Wyrd thought the druids were no better than city-dwellers.<sup>[[70]](#cite_note-ESOWM-76)</sup> Druids would much later practice self-isolation to varying degrees<sup>[[34]](#cite_note-ESOSSM-37)</sup><sup>[[67]](#cite_note-ESODR-73)</sup><sup>[[71]](#cite_note-DP-77)</sup> as a response to historical encroachments and deprivations.<sup>[[32]](#cite_note-ONWD-35)</sup><sup>[[68]](#cite_note-LABHI-74)</sup>

While the Aldmer maintained control of Tamriel, Clan Direnni coexisted peacefully alongside their Nedic and Half-Elven subjects.<sup>[[57]](#cite_note-FC-60)</sup> The Direnni ruled largely through their Nedic clients,<sup>[[UOL 4]](#cite_note-LSP:OAC-61)</sup> while the "Meriphilic"<sup>[[72]](#cite_note-ONSHV1-78)</sup> Druids of Galen used their fearsome magic to enforce their influence over early Bretons, and the Wyrd avoided politics altogether.<sup>[[73]](#cite_note-ESOEFS-79)</sup> Some Manmeri devotional idols from this period depict [Mara](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Mara) as an elven woman in a lover's embrace with a man, suggesting Aldmeri culture may have been welcomed with relatively open arms.<sup>[[74]](#cite_note-Manmer-80)</sup> However, their comity would not last: localized groups of Bretons displeased with mer butted heads with their elven overlords long before they officially came to blows.<sup>[[8]](#cite_note-LATD-8)</sup>

### First Era
[![](https://images.uesp.net/thumb/c/cf/ON-crown_store-Chrysamere.jpg/200px-ON-crown_store-Chrysamere.jpg)](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:ON-crown_store-Chrysamere.jpg) [](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:ON-crown_store-Chrysamere.jpg) Chrysamere (ESO) The earliest written account of the existence of a Breton is from the late Merethic Era, which is the blacksmith [Asterie Bedel](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Asterie_Bedel), who is credited with the creation of the legendary artifact [Chrysamere](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Chrysamere).<sup>[[75]](#cite_note-LAIA-81)</sup> The history that followed would see the Breton peoples venturing out of High Rock and into other provinces. In [1E 20](Lore_First_Era.md#1E_20), the sage and author Voernet traveled to [Artaeum](Lore_Artaeum.md) to meet with [Iachesis](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Iachesis), the Ritemaster of the [Psijic Order](Lore_Psijic_Order.md).<sup>[[76]](#cite_note-FOA-82)</sup>

Written in [1E 200](Lore_First_Era.md#1E_200), the [Tamrilean Tractates](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Tamrilean_Tractates) speak of an early encounter between a Nord hunting party and the Bretons. The Bretons were scarcely recognizable as men, and the Nords attacked them thinking they were Aldmeri. The Nords ceased their assault when one of the Bretons spoke in broken Nordic, and the hunting party brought news of this race back to [Windhelm](Lore_Windhelm.md). The Nords believed the Manmeri from beyond [the Reach](Lore_The_Reach.md) were descended from human slaves taken during the [Night of Tears](Lore_Night_of_Tears.md).<sup>[[37]](#cite_note-PGE1High-40)</sup> The Breton [Archmage Gauldur](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Gauldur), who was contemporary with [High King Harald](Lore_Harald.md), became cemented in Nordic oral traditions despite an age-long campaign to erase his legacy.<sup>[[77]](#cite_note-83)</sup><sup>[[78]](#cite_note-84)</sup> Upon forming the [First Empire of the Nords](Lore_First_Empire_of_the_Nords.md), [High King Vrage](Lore_Vrage.md) made the liberation the Bretons from their elven masters his first priority.<sup>[[37]](#cite_note-PGE1High-40)</sup> Vrage's initial campaign brought him as far as the [Bjoulsae](Lore_Bjoulsae_River.md), but progress was impeded by elven magic, and the elves were also aided in battle by many of their Breton vassals.<sup>[[37]](#cite_note-PGE1High-40)</sup> Though the Aldmer kept hold of their lands for most of the era,<sup>[[53]](#cite_note-PGE3High-56)</sup> some sources claim that all of High Rock was conquered by [1E 240](Lore_First_Era.md#1E_240).<sup>[[79]](#cite_note-TDCP11-85)</sup> To support their pillaging parties, the Nords founded many fortified towns along the coasts around this time, such as [Daggerfall](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Daggerfall), [Camlorn](Lore_Camlorn.md), and [Reich Gradkeep](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Reich_Gradkeep).<sup>[[53]](#cite_note-PGE3High-56)</sup>

During the [Alessian Slave Rebellion](Lore_Alessian_Slave_Rebellion.md), [Alessia](Lore_Alessia.md) hired many Breton and Nordic warbands as mercenaries with promises of land and trade concessions. After the Alessian Cyrodiils achieved victory, the mercenaries that participated were assimilated into the Nibenese culture.<sup>[[80]](#cite_note-86)</sup>

Tired of outside influence, the Druids of Galen advocated for druidic rule of High Rock, making them a target of virtually every faction vying for control.<sup>[[72]](#cite_note-ONSHV1-78)</sup> The rising [Direnni Hegemony](Lore_Direnni_Hegemony.md) saw them as a threat, and the [Alessian Order](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Alessian_Order) was intolerant of their religion.<sup>[[32]](#cite_note-ONWD-35)</sup> Ultimately, the druids split from Bretondom around [1E 330](Lore_First_Era.md#1E_330). Following the guidance of Y'ffre's visions,<sup>[[59]](#cite_note-EOTD-63)</sup> a song, or an [Elder Scroll](Lore_Elder_Scroll.md),<sup>[[72]](#cite_note-ONSHV1-78)</sup> Druid King Kasorayn led somewhere between a few thousand to a million druids on an exodus to the Systres.<sup>[[59]](#cite_note-EOTD-63)</sup><sup>[[72]](#cite_note-ONSHV1-78)</sup> A few remained on the mainland.<sup>[[67]](#cite_note-ESODR-73)</sup>

[![](https://images.uesp.net/thumb/1/14/ON-misc-Druidic_Knotwork_Face_Tattoos.png/200px-ON-misc-Druidic_Knotwork_Face_Tattoos.png)](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:ON-misc-Druidic_Knotwork_Face_Tattoos.png) [](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:ON-misc-Druidic_Knotwork_Face_Tattoos.png) Triquetra Tattoo (around forehead) When the Druids of Galen arrived in the Systres, the Draoife terraformed a barren volcanic island into a lush and verdant volcanic paradise and named it [Y'ffelon](Lore_Y%27ffelon.md). The druids then swiftly expanded across the archipelago into the three other islands,<sup>[[81]](#cite_note-So A-87)</sup> sprouting life where it was once barren.<sup>[[72]](#cite_note-ONSHV1-78)</sup> The dissolution of the Druids of Galen was brought about with the event known as the "three mornings of sail", where priest-navigators set out to sea on enchanted vessels outside the archipelago. Their outside experiences and their interactions with different races resulted in three sects developing, each with their own interpretation of Y'ffre's will; the Stonelore, Eldertide, and Firesong Circles.<sup>[[67]](#cite_note-ESODR-73)</sup><sup>[[72]](#cite_note-ONSHV1-78)</sup> Despite their separation, to symbolize their unity matters more and that they share the same goals, the druidic circles came to shaping knot-work into a [triquetra](Lore_Triquetra.md),<sup>[[82]](#cite_note-88)</sup> a symbol that would become adopted by civilized Bretons.<sup>[[83]](#cite_note-89)</sup> Kasorayn himself took on the role of an observer after he helped establish the druids on the isle, and only intervened when necessary. The druidic monarchy ended after heretics from the Allwither Order murdered Kasarayn. The heretics are speculated as wanting to seize the Ivy Throne<sup>[[62]](#cite_note-ESODruid King-67)</sup> to enact revenge on their former elven oppressors back in High Rock.<sup>[[84]](#cite_note-ONSHADG-90)</sup> Though the Allwither heretics were defeated,<sup>[[62]](#cite_note-ESODruid King-67)</sup> prophecy would deem that the title of Druid King remain vacant for thousands of years.<sup>[[85]](#cite_note-91)</sup> The Druid King's symbology would disappear almost overnight.<sup>[[68]](#cite_note-LABHI-74)</sup><sup>[[86]](#cite_note-92)</sup>

#### The Rise and Fall of the Direnni Hegemony
[![](https://images.uesp.net/thumb/0/02/ON-misc-Direnni.png/200px-ON-misc-Direnni.png)](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:ON-misc-Direnni.png) [](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:ON-misc-Direnni.png) Symbol of Clan Direnni (ESO) After much infighting between the mer of High Rock over who would rule the province,<sup>[[62]](#cite_note-ESODruid King-67)</sup> circa [1E 355](Lore_First_Era.md#1E_355), Clan Direnni established their Hegemony after they emerged victorious through political maneuvering and devious machinations.<sup>[[79]](#cite_note-TDCP11-85)</sup> However, some consider the Direnni's rule in the years leading up to its establishment as part of the Direnni Hegemony as well.<sup>[[72]](#cite_note-ONSHV1-78)</sup><sup>[[59]](#cite_note-EOTD-63)</sup><sup>[[67]](#cite_note-ESODR-73)</sup> The Nord's holdings in High Rock were threatened and ultimately lost as a result of the [War of Succession](Lore_War_of_Succession.md) erupting in [1E 369](Lore_First_Era.md#1E_369),<sup>[[60]](#cite_note-AHOD-64)</sup> which ended in [1E 420](Lore_First_Era.md#1E_420).<sup>[[87]](#cite_note-PGE1S-93)</sup>

After gaining influence and purchasing the Isle of Balfiera in [1E 461](Lore_First_Era.md#1E_461),<sup>[[88]](#cite_note-94)</sup><sup>[[89]](#cite_note-ALOSAS-95)</sup><sup>[[90]](#cite_note-96)</sup> [Ryain Direnni](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Ryain_Direnni) led Clan Direnni to conquer all of High Rock by [1E 477](Lore_First_Era.md#1E_477).<sup>[[79]](#cite_note-TDCP11-85)</sup><sup>[[89]](#cite_note-ALOSAS-95)</sup><sup>[[91]](#cite_note-RTR-97)</sup> His Breton legions were supposedly the first to sack the Orc hold of [Orsinium](Lore_Orsinium.md),<sup>[[89]](#cite_note-ALOSAS-95)</sup> though what's known as the "First Orsinium" is usually dated much later to the ninth or tenth century of the First Era.<sup>[[92]](#cite_note-PGE3O-98)</sup><sup>[[93]](#cite_note-BSOHR-99)</sup><sup>[[94]](#cite_note-WJOTB-100)</sup> As the Direnni Hegemony expanded geographically, the elves, who were few in number, passed increasing powers of administration to the Breton caste.<sup>[[1]](#cite_note-TBMOP-1)</sup> Clan Direnni was inspired to outlaw the religion of the Alessian Reform by [Rislav Larich](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Rislav_Larich)'s victory against Emperor [Gorieus](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Gorieus), and began pushing into Imperial territory.<sup>[[91]](#cite_note-RTR-97)</sup> The timeframe between [1E 480](Lore_First_Era.md#1E_480) and [1E 482](Lore_First_Era.md#1E_482) would see a coming conflict with the Alessian Order. Seeing the threat the Order posed, [Aiden Direnni](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Aiden_Direnni) signed the [Rights Charter](Lore_Rights_Charter.md) in an effort to muster much-needed troops for the coming conflict.<sup>[[89]](#cite_note-ALOSAS-95)</sup> With the aid of Breton knights, Aiden's army defeated the Alessians at the [Battle of Glenumbria Moors](Lore_Battle_of_Glenumbria_Moors.md) on the 8th of Sun's Dawn in [1E 482](Lore_First_Era.md#1E_482). <sup>[[40]](#cite_note-ONARCP-43)</sup><sup>[[95]](#cite_note-TLKOTA-101)</sup> The Bretons of the Glenumbra Moors celebrate the [Day of Release](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Day_of_Release) to commemorate this victory.<sup>[[96]](#cite_note-102)</sup> A popular [song](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:The_Battle_of_Glenumbria_Moors) from the Second Era memorializes the Bretons' role in turning the tide against the Alessian generals, and commemorated the Direnni clansmen who were instrumental in defending High Rock.<sup>[[97]](#cite_note-TBo GM-103)</sup>

Thoroughly spent, the Direnni withdrew to Balfiera, and their hegemony fractured circa [1E 498](Lore_First_Era.md#1E_498).<sup>[[1]](#cite_note-TBMOP-1)</sup><sup>[[79]](#cite_note-TDCP11-85)</sup><sup>[[UOL 7]](#cite_note-Xan Timeline-104)</sup> With most of High Rock free from elven control by [1E 500](Lore_First_Era.md#1E_500),<sup>[[37]](#cite_note-PGE1High-40)</sup> the Breton kingdoms began establishing themselves around this time.<sup>[[98]](#cite_note-Horse Folk-105)</sup> The Bretons' rise to prominence in High Rock initially started through villages being founded in tactical locations, such as [Wayrest](Lore_Wayrest.md), which started as a fishing hamlet possibly as early as [1E 800](Lore_First_Era.md#1E_800).<sup>[[94]](#cite_note-WJOTB-100)</sup> As the emerging Bretons absorbed the remaining Nordic population, Nordic cities such as Camlorn were assimilated rather than conquered, and High Rock would be definitively Breton by the end of the First Era.<sup>[[53]](#cite_note-PGE3High-56)</sup>

[![](https://images.uesp.net/thumb/3/36/ON-place-Isle_of_Balfiera.jpg/200px-ON-place-Isle_of_Balfiera.jpg)](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:ON-place-Isle_of_Balfiera.jpg) [](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:ON-place-Isle_of_Balfiera.jpg) Balfiera, home of Clan Direnni Though the province was in Breton hands, it was by no means a cohesive nation. Clan Direnni's retreat to Balfiera left no united government, and High Rock fractured into a hundred squabbling fiefdoms.<sup>[[53]](#cite_note-PGE3High-56)</sup> The elf-blooded nobility of [Greater Bretony](Lore_Greater_Bretony.md) took up the mantle Clan Direnni left behind, maintaining the feudal hierarchy their elven predecessors forged and placing their noble families, the oldest of whom the elven blood flowed strongest within, in the position of aristocracy. The new noble class, consisting of highborn Bretons, justified their ascension to aristocracy and the preservation of the peasant class by disassociating themselves from their elven heritage. The Bretons vilified the Direnni, and redefined themselves around the notion that they were not elves. The Breton nobility fabricated a history of noble resistance to Direnni rule to suit the narrative that Breton cultural identity had no elven roots. In time, a merchant class sprouted and thrived, trading around Tamriel's coasts.<sup>[[1]](#cite_note-TBMOP-1)</sup> In addition to the conflicts over borders and crowns, the Bretons were left to deal with the encroachment of the wilds upon their settlements: the Direnni renounced their covenant with the Earthbones after their retreat, which legends claim they did out of spite. This pact protected Direnni roads and townships from the forest and the beasts that inhabited it.<sup>[[51]](#cite_note-TVS-54)</sup>

According to one source, the Bretons permitted the Direnni to retreat to Balfiera without resistance.<sup>[[1]](#cite_note-TBMOP-1)</sup><sup>[[99]](#cite_note-106)</sup> Another account claims that the Direnni had already completed their withdrawal to Balfiera by the time the Redguards arrived in Tamriel.<sup>[[100]](#cite_note-Website Lore-107)</sup> A third, contradictory source places the final stages of the Direnni’s flight from High Rock sometime around or after the ninth century of the First Era.<sup>[[nb 7]](#intnote_Pale)</sup> During this later period, violence against the Direnni escalated under the reign of King Festrien Spenard I. Backed by vassals from [House Aurmine](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:House_Aurmine), the despot king’s Knights of the Pale Order slaughtered the Direnni wholesale during the latter years of their flight from High Rock, reportedly maintaining lists of Direnni warriors and magisters they killed.<sup>[[101]](#cite_note-ROTPO-108)</sup> Yet another source claims that the Direnni remained dominant in High Rock until the middle of the First Era.<sup>[[53]](#cite_note-PGE3High-56)</sup> In spite of the vilification of the Direnni and disassociation from their elven heritage, at least some Bretons would continue to emphasize their elven blood.<sup>[[102]](#cite_note-VOF-109)</sup>

The earliest known [Yokudans](Lore_Yokudan.md) encountered by Bretons were the [Silverhoof Horsemen](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Silverhoof_Horsemen), who came to Tamriel centuries before the [Ra Gada](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Ra_Gada), while the Direnni Hegemony was dissolving and the Breton kingdoms were forming. This opportune moment in history allowed the Horsemen to firmly establish themselves in Rivenspire without significant organized resistance from the locals. They would become "Bretonized" by their neighbors over the centuries, but retained significant elements of their original culture.<sup>[[98]](#cite_note-Horse Folk-105)</sup>

#### Bretons on the World Stage
By the time the Druids of Galen fled the mainland circa 1E 330, the Breton peoples had already encountered the [Dwemer](Lore_Dwemer.md), though such occurrences with them were minimal.<sup>[[103]](#cite_note-LDA-110)</sup> Circa [1E 420](Lore_First_Era.md#1E_420), when the self-exiled [Clan Rourken](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Clan_Rourken) relocated to [Volenfell](Lore_Volenfell.md) in Hammerfell, south of High Rock, it opened up new trade opportunities for the Bretons.<sup>[[104]](#cite_note-PGE3Hammerfell-111)</sup>

[![](https://images.uesp.net/thumb/5/5d/ON-map-Systres_Archipelago.jpg/200px-ON-map-Systres_Archipelago.jpg)](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:ON-map-Systres_Archipelago.jpg) [](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:ON-map-Systres_Archipelago.jpg) The Systres Archipelago Eventually, the differences in the beliefs of the three major Systrean drudic circles nearly led to conflict. This was avoided thanks to the appearance of a common enemy, the [Sinistral Elves](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Sinistral_Mer), who fled to the Systres circa [1E 660](Lore_First_Era.md#1E_660) to escape the Yokudans. Their invasion was temporarily halted when Y'ffelon's volcano of [Mount Firesong](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Mount_Firesong) erupted sometime around [1E 668](Lore_First_Era.md#1E_668). Regardless, the Sinistral Elves took over the archipelago, and the druidic circles were forced into hiding. With the coming of the Ra Gada in [1E 785](Lore_First_Era.md#1E_785), what remained of the elves were purged, and the Yokudans quickly left to sail eastward. In the end, only the druids remained.<sup>[[105]](#cite_note-ONSHV2-112)</sup>

This was only the first Yokudan "warrior wave".<sup>[[106]](#cite_note-RTHATH-113)</sup><sup>[[105]](#cite_note-ONSHV2-112)</sup> The next wave, known as the Tavan wave,<sup>[[107]](#cite_note-CM28-114)</sup> came after the time of [Yokuda](Lore_Yokuda.md)'s sinking in [1E 792](Lore_First_Era.md#1E_792), making landfall in [1E 808](Lore_First_Era.md#1E_808).<sup>[[108]](#cite_note-PGE3OL-115)</sup> The Tavans captured a harborage from the beastfolk, which they named [Hegathe](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Hegathe) (the Aldmeri name for Hammerfell), and used it as a staging ground for conquest.<sup>[[104]](#cite_note-PGE3Hammerfell-111)</sup><sup>[[109]](#cite_note-STJOA-116)</sup> Long before the arrival of the Ra Gada, the elves and later Bretons established an outpost at what is now [Sentinel](Lore_Sentinel_(kingdom).md) in order to protect fisherfolk and seafaring merchants from inland [desert Orc](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Desert_Orcs) marauders, [giant Goblin](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Giant_Goblin) raiders, and other dangers of the desert.<sup>[[104]](#cite_note-PGE3Hammerfell-111)</sup><sup>[[110]](#cite_note-EGTHammerfell-117)</sup> The next warrior wave, led by [Grandee Yaghoub](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Grandee_Yaghoub), quickly discovered and established control over this port with little resistance. Yaghoub conscripted the locals to serve as masons and servants in the building of his new palace, [Samaruik](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Samaruik), and the rest of the city.<sup>[[109]](#cite_note-STJOA-116)</sup> The kings of the Ra Gada continued to raid Breton coastal cities and trading vessels,<sup>[[111]](#cite_note-ONYokudan-118)</sup> and the Cyro-Nords from Colovia who plundered the Iliac Bay annually were pushed out by them.<sup>[[112]](#cite_note-PGE1C-119)</sup> The descendants of the Yokudans, the Redguards, would later become established as historical enemies to the Bretons.<sup>[[30]](#cite_note-ONILES-33)</sup>

[![](https://images.uesp.net/thumb/d/d6/ON-interior-Honor%27s_Rest_03.jpg/200px-ON-interior-Honor%27s_Rest_03.jpg)](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:ON-interior-Honor%27s_Rest_03.jpg) [](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:ON-interior-Honor%27s_Rest_03.jpg) Baloth Bloodtusk and Gaiden Shinji, assassinated by King Joile's general during the Siege of Orsinium Orsinium was built on the boundary between western [Wrothgar](Lore_Wrothgar.md) and Rivenspire in the ninth or tenth century of the First Era.<sup>[[92]](#cite_note-PGE3O-98)</sup><sup>[[93]](#cite_note-BSOHR-99)</sup><sup>[[94]](#cite_note-WJOTB-100)</sup> King [Golkarr](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Golkarr) of the Orcs amassed an army and was determined to seize control of the Bjoulsae River,<sup>[[113]](#cite_note-120)</sup><sup>[[114]](#cite_note-PGE1WR-121)</sup> upon which the nomadic Breton [Bjoulsae River Tribes](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Bjoulsae_River_Tribes) lived.<sup>[[115]](#cite_note-122)</sup> They intended to force Wayrest to pay to make use of the river.<sup>[[114]](#cite_note-PGE1WR-121)</sup> In [1E 874](Lore_First_Era.md#1E_874), Warlord [Thulgeg](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Thulgeg)'s army of Orcs and [Goblins](Lore_Goblin.md) attempted to flee Hammerfell for Orsinium in High Rock, but were blocked at [Bangkorai Pass](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Bangkorai_Pass) by the [Bangkorai Garrison](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Bangkorai_Garrison).<sup>[[93]](#cite_note-BSOHR-99)</sup><sup>[[116]](#cite_note-SC-123)</sup>

In [1E 948](Lore_First_Era.md#1E_948), [King Joile](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Joile) of Daggerfall sent a letter to [Gaiden Shinji](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Gaiden_Shinji) of the [Order of Diagna](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Order_of_Diagna) proposing a joint attack on Orsinium. Joile cited that the Orcs were raiding along the Bjoulsae and impeding traffic to the heart of the land as reason enough to make war against the Orcs. Agreeing to provide aid, an alliance was formed between the Order of Diagna, [Daggerfall](Lore_Daggerfall_(kingdom).md), and Sentinel. The armies amassed and began a 30-year long campaign known as the [Siege of Orsinium](Lore_Siege_of_Orsinium.md).<sup>[[94]](#cite_note-WJOTB-100)</sup><sup>[[92]](#cite_note-PGE3O-98)</sup> In that time, King Joile plotted to betray the Redguards and invade Hammerfell. Joile and his Reachman general [Mercedene](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Mercedene) assassinated Gaiden Shinji and Orcish hero [Baloth Bloodtusk](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Baloth_Bloodtusk). Daggerfall's own [Knights of the Dragon](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Knights_of_the_Dragon), though they failed to stop the assassination, defeated General Mercedene.<sup>[[117]](#cite_note-124)</sup> In [1E 973](Lore_First_Era.md#1E_973), Joile's invasion of Hammerfell proceeded, but he was stopped by the [Ansei](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Ansei) warrior [Makela Leki](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Makela_Leki) at Bangkorai Pass.<sup>[[118]](#cite_note-125)</sup> The Siege of Orsinium finally ended in [1E 980](Lore_First_Era.md#1E_980) when the allied forces breached the city's defenses, overran it, and razed it to the ground.<sup>[[92]](#cite_note-PGE3O-98)</sup>

With the Bjoulsae River region opened up for trade after the siege, the Bretons experienced an economic boom. The kingdom of [Evermore](Lore_Evermore.md) was founded by the Bjoulsae River Tribes,<sup>[[119]](#cite_note-TRHOKE-126)</sup> and Wayrest also established a presence on both banks of the river. The Masconian Trade Way was formed by the hard-working traders and merchants of the Bjoulsae, greatly expanding commerce and marginalizing [piracy](Lore_Piracy.md).<sup>[[94]](#cite_note-WJOTB-100)</sup> Daggerfall developed a burgeoning [ivory](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Ivory) trade, which originated with ivory plundered from Orsinium following its sacking.<sup>[[120]](#cite_note-ESOIvory-127)</sup> The uneasy truce between the Bretons and Redguards over Orsinium transitioned into economic relations between the two races.<sup>[[110]](#cite_note-EGTHammerfell-117)</sup>

#### Relations with Morrowind
[![](https://images.uesp.net/thumb/d/d3/ON-place-Ebonheart.jpg/200px-ON-place-Ebonheart.jpg)](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:ON-place-Ebonheart.jpg) [](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:ON-place-Ebonheart.jpg) Ebonheart in Morrowind Historically, the Bretons maintained ties with the [Dunmer](Lore_Dunmer.md) (and possibly the [Chimer](Lore_Chimer.md))<sup>[[nb 4]](#intnote_Chimer)</sup> through a trade agreement between [Clan R'aathim](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Ra%27athim) of [Morrowind](Lore_Morrowind.md) and the Kings of High Rock. Under this pact, [King Moraelyn](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Moraelyn) of [Ebonheart](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Ebonheart) 's retainers were granted rights to mine ebony in the [Wrothgarian Mountains](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Wrothgarian_Mountains) and establish a colony in High Rock. In return, they supplied the Breton lords with ebony weapons and taught them how to smith ebony themselves.<sup>[[121]](#cite_note-KEII-128)</sup> [House Mora](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:House_Mora) of [Ebonheart](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Ebonheart) and its Clan R'aathim notably had human blood in its family tree, before that house fell and was adopted into the [House Hlaalu](Lore_House_Hlaalu.md).<sup>[[122]](#cite_note-TRB5-129)</sup> There are some sources that suggest [King Edward](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Edward) of Daggerfall was the son of the Breton [Queen Aliera](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Aliera) of Wayrest and [King Moraelyn](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Moraelyn) of Ebonheart.<sup>[[UOL 8]](#cite_note-Jindra-130)</sup> Stories tell of King Edward and King Moraelyn wielding the [Horn of Summoning](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Horn_of_Summoning) to banish the Nords from High Rock.<sup>[[123]](#cite_note-TRB4-131)</sup> But in the historical fiction *[King Edward](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:King_Edward)*, Edward was born after Wayrest was founded, which is after the Nords were expelled from High Rock.<sup>[[124]](#cite_note-KE10-132)</sup>

Some of the people of High Rock held negative attitudes the elves of Morrowind before the time of King Edward, many who believed them to be thieves and kidnappers, with myths claiming that they sprouted from the ground.<sup>[[124]](#cite_note-KE10-132)</sup> This led to them being banned from Daggerfall for a time.<sup>[[125]](#cite_note-KEIV-133)</sup> Around the second millennium (circa [1E 1000](Lore_First_Era.md#1E_1000)), a noble family of Bretons called the [Imbels](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Imbel) inhabited the island of [Vvardenfell](Lore_Vvardenfell.md), living near the village of [Suran](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Suran).<sup>[[126]](#cite_note-IG-134)</sup> [House Telvanni](Lore_House_Telvanni.md) in Morrowind often prefers to hire [Bosmer](Lore_Bosmer.md) and Bretons as mercenaries to ensure they are left in peace.<sup>[[127]](#cite_note-Dialogue Races-135)</sup>

#### Alessian Empire and the Camorian Empire
In [1E 1029](Lore_First_Era.md#1E_1029), Empress [Hestra](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Hestra) pursued the [Gray Host](Lore_Gray_Host.md) from [Verkarth](Lore_Verkarth_(Hammerfell).md) to Bangkorai Pass, where the Bretons held the line and fractured the undead forces, easing the Empire's hunt. Hestra was impressed, and offered High Rock admission into the [First Empire](Lore_Alessian_Empire.md), which they accepted.<sup>[[93]](#cite_note-BSOHR-99)</sup> Thus, the Bretons joined the Empire of Men and accepted Alessia's [Eight Divines](Lore_Eight_Divines.md).<sup>[[1]](#cite_note-TBMOP-1)</sup> In [1E 1100](Lore_First_Era.md#1E_1100), ambassadors of the [Camorian Empire](Lore_Camorian_Empire.md) were accepted into [Wayrest](Lore_Wayrest.md) and granted them the right to call themselves a kingdom under the newly crowned [King Farangel Gardner](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Farangel).<sup>[[128]](#cite_note-WJot B-136)</sup>

At an unknown time period during the First Era, an alliance known as the [League of Unrest](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:League_of_Unrest) was created between Daggerfall, Wayrest, and Balfiera against the [Cyrodiils](Lore_Imperial.md).<sup>[[129]](#cite_note-RGMaiko-137)</sup>

[![](https://images.uesp.net/thumb/6/64/ON-trailer-All Flags Navy.jpg/200px-ON-trailer-All Flags Navy.jpg)](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:ON-trailer-All Flags Navy.jpg) [](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:ON-trailer-All Flags Navy.jpg) The All Flags Navy The [Thrassian Plague](Lore_Thrassian_Plague.md) circa [2200](Lore_Second_Era.md#2200), which spread outward from cities like Daggerfall and Hegathe, cut the population of the Iliac Bay, and Tamriel as a whole, in half.<sup>[[60]](#cite_note-AHOD-64)</sup><sup>[[130]](#cite_note-TTP-138)</sup> After several years, widespread belief emerged that the [Sload](Lore_Sload.md) were responsible for maliciously inflicting the disease on Tamriel.<sup>[[130]](#cite_note-TTP-138)</sup> To hold them accountable, the Alessian Emperor granted command of an Imperial fleet to the [Colovian](Lore_Colovian_Highlands.md) King of [Anvil](Lore_Anvil.md), [Bendu Olo](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Bendu_Olo).<sup>[[131]](#cite_note-ONSHV3-139)</sup> Bendu sought out allies to bolster his forces, and many Breton sailors and warships helped form what would become known as the [All Flags Navy](Lore_All_Flags_Navy.md).<sup>[[132]](#cite_note-JOTE-140)</sup> Some Bretons among the initial fourteen ships which formed the basis of the All Flags Navy were Captain Isara Davaux of the King's Jest, Renwic Moorcroft of the Pristine Halberd, and [Coin-Baron](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Coin-barons) Nemic Santerre of the Silver Lantern.<sup>[[133]](#cite_note-141)</sup> Bendo's call also attracted knightly figures such as [Lady Joslin Garick](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Joslin_Garick) and Baroness [Belene Chatillon](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Belene_Chatillon).<sup>[[134]](#cite_note-ONCG-142)</sup><sup>[[135]](#cite_note-ONSKO-143)</sup> The local Stonelore Circle also lent a ship and druids for the coming conflict.<sup>[[136]](#cite_note-TSS-144)</sup> Sometime around [1E 2243](Lore_First_Era.md#1E_2243), the Navy arrived in the Systres Archipelago, where they established the Navy's largest base and shipyard within High Isle's Gonfalon Bay.<sup>[[131]](#cite_note-ONSHV3-139)</sup> After various skirmishes, the Navy launched a final assault on [Thras](Lore_Thras.md) in [1E 2260](Lore_First_Era.md#1E_2260). The entire landmass was sunk into the ocean, catching half the fleet in a giant whirlpool. The remaining influential figures returned to the Systres, where these representatives of each race signed the Concordat of Fraternity on All Flags Islet, in hopes to bring about peace and cooperation.<sup>[[131]](#cite_note-ONSHV3-139)</sup>

[![](https://images.uesp.net/thumb/d/d2/ON-trailer-Skingrad.png/200px-ON-trailer-Skingrad.png)](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:ON-trailer-Skingrad.png) [](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:ON-trailer-Skingrad.png) Skingrad in Cyrodiil Angry merchants from Wayrest called their fellow Bretons to secede from the Alessian Empire circa [1E 2300](Lore_First_Era.md#1E_2300), citing prejudice against elven heritage and increasing Imperial tithes to support their position.<sup>[[137]](#cite_note-145)</sup> High Rock formally reasserted its independence in [1E 2305](Lore_First_Era.md#1E_2305).<sup>[[93]](#cite_note-BSOHR-99)</sup> Despite resenting this secession, the Alessian Order did not intervene until King Desynan of [Skingrad](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Skingrad) and Queen Margert Gardner of Wayrest arranged a marriage between their children. Fearing a dynastic alliance between High Rock and Colovia, Arch-Prelate Zirnius forbid the union, and when Desynan appointed an official to approve the marriage anyway, Zirnius dispatched his legions to punish the Colovians. This conflict was initially "anarchy, local uprisings, and shifting alliances" that were contained within the Colovian Estates, but later shifted to Breton lands within the Iliac Bay.<sup>[[138]](#cite_note-ONOWR-146)</sup> The Legions of Piety and Grace were sent under Abbot-General [Priscus Mactator](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Priscus_Mactator) to reconquer the Bretons, but could not break through the Bangkorai Garrison.<sup>[[93]](#cite_note-BSOHR-99)</sup> This loss would embolden the rebelling Colovians, officially kickstarting the [War of Righteousness](Lore_War_of_Righteousness.md) in [1E 2321](Lore_First_Era.md#1E_2321).<sup>[[52]](#cite_note-ONSHV4-55)</sup><sup>[[nb 5]](#intnote_Desynan)</sup> The Alessian Order's heavy losses in the west forced them to tax and conscript people from eastern Cyrodiil, causing angry Nibeneans to rebel and slay the Arch-Prelate and destroy the Order's great cathedral at [Lake Canulus](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Lake_Canulus). With no leadership or income, the Alessians in High Rock abandoned their invasion.<sup>[[138]](#cite_note-ONOWR-146)</sup>

[![](https://images.uesp.net/thumb/4/44/ON-concept-Martinne_Guimard.png/200px-ON-concept-Martinne_Guimard.png)](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:ON-concept-Martinne_Guimard.png) [](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:ON-concept-Martinne_Guimard.png) Statue of Martinne Guimard Although the Systres had been claimed by Colovia after the All Flags Navy's victory over the Sload, the financial costs of the war led them to sell the archipelago to High Rock Coin-barons circa [1E 2327](Lore_First_Era.md#1E_2327). [Duchess Martinne Guimard](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Martinne_Guimard) became the archipelago's new ruler, and in [1E 2328](Lore_First_Era.md#1E_2328), named the largest island High Isle in honor of High Rock. To the delight of the Systreans, their archipelago was not only untouched by the War of Righteousness, but remained "an untouched cradle of Breton history". Druidism was alive and well, and Breton culture was at the forefront thanks to the Bretons who stayed behind after the assault on Thras.<sup>[[52]](#cite_note-ONSHV4-55)</sup>

High Rock was independent once more, but the secession came at great cost. The War of Righteousness halved the population of the Iliac Bay a second time.<sup>[[60]](#cite_note-AHOD-64)</sup> The Alessian collapse struck the stubborn Bretons harder than the other races, as they had no unified governing structure. Warring fiefs would rage across the peninsula in the coming centuries as various rulers attempted to assume control.<sup>[[139]](#cite_note-147)</sup> The Systres remained in Breton hands, despite later transferring from [House Guimard](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Guimard) to [House Mantel](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:House_Mantel), but in [1E 2484](Lore_First_Era.md#1E_2484), Mount Firesong erupted once more, devastating the archipelago and killing many of its inhabitants. Starvation and illnesses among the lower classes led to political unrest. The Stonelore Circle managed to pull the city folk back from the brink of death by developing sprawling pastoral and agricultural operations, leading to a renaissance of Druidism. This time period was referred to as the Green Years.<sup>[[140]](#cite_note-ONSHV5-148)</sup>

#### The Second Empire
The first appearances of the [Akaviri](Lore_Akaviri.md) in Tamriel were pirates (later assumed to have been scouts for an invasion force).<sup>[[108]](#cite_note-PGE3OL-115)</sup> These raiders established themselves on the islands to the west of Wayrest around [1E 800](Lore_First_Era.md#1E_800), antagonizing the Bretons of the region.<sup>[[94]](#cite_note-WJOTB-100)</sup> Finally, around [2700](Lore_Second_Era.md#2700), Akaviri legions invaded northern Tamriel,<sup>[[141]](#cite_note-LOTD-149)</sup> which prompt the people of Wayrest to move within the walled estate of the Gardners for protection in [1E 2702](Lore_First_Era.md#1E_2702).<sup>[[94]](#cite_note-WJOTB-100)</sup> With the Akaviri invasion, the population of the Iliac Bay was halved a third time. It is said that if Daggerfall had not been hardened and fortified through wars in its first thousand years of existence, the Akaviri may have dominated the Iliac Bay into modernity.<sup>[[60]](#cite_note-AHOD-64)</sup>

The [Second Empire](Lore_Second_Empire.md) was established in [1E 2703](Lore_First_Era.md#1E_2703) after [Reman Cyrodiil](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Reman_I) suppressed the Akaviri invasion of Tamriel at the battle of [Pale Pass](Lore_Pale_Pass.md).<sup>[[112]](#cite_note-PGE1C-119)</sup> With the Akaviri's numbers and tactics boosting his power, Reman went on to pacify most of Tamriel.<sup>[[141]](#cite_note-LOTD-149)</sup><sup>[[112]](#cite_note-PGE1C-119)</sup> In an effort to make Cyrodiil more cosmopolitan, Reman I incorporated many elements of High Rock society into his own.<sup>[[142]](#cite_note-PGE3C-150)</sup> Though conquered, High Rock's virulent sectarianism would remain intact.<sup>[[37]](#cite_note-PGE1High-40)</sup>

The distant shores of the Systres were also affected by Reman Cyrodiil's ambitions. In [1E 2704](Lore_First_Era.md#1E_2704), the Reman Empire reclaimed the archipelago and reinstalled Breton Coin-barons, which marked the end of the Green Years.<sup>[[143]](#cite_note-ONSHV6-151)</sup> The High Rock Coin-barons committed various injustices when they utilized their merchant fleet to move illicit goods. The Coin-barons were also involved in [slavery](Lore_Slavery.md), which was a part of Breton culture at that time, and established a slaver fort on Amenos.<sup>[[UOL 9]](#cite_note-HIDD-152)</sup><sup>[[144]](#cite_note-ESOEHI-153)</sup> Over time, the Spire of the Crimson Coin on High Isle, where many grim and debaucherous celebrations took place, became a sort of monument to the excesses of these rulers.<sup>[[145]](#cite_note-154)</sup><sup>[[146]](#cite_note-155)</sup>

As part of the Second Empire, High Rock's soldiers participated in the 80-year [Four Score War](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Four_Score_War) against [Morrowind](Lore_Morrowind.md). According to the historical fiction *[2920, The Last Year of the First Era](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:2920,_The_Last_Year_of_the_First_Era)*, a Breton man named [Cassyr Whitley](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Cassyr_Whitley) of [Dwynnen](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Dwynnen) defected from the Imperial army and spied on the Dunmer's behalf. After Whitley's mistake cost Morrowind the fortress of [Ald Marak](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Ald_Marak), he returned to High Rock, where he met the Dunmeri exile [Turala](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Turala). When Turala's coven and child were lost to an Orcish raid, Whitley deceived her into believing the attack was perpetrated by assassins employed by Duke [Brindisi Dorom](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Brindisi_Dorom) of [Mournhold](Lore_Mournhold.md), prompting her to summon [Mehrunes Dagon](Lore_Mehrunes_Dagon.md) for revenge.

### Second Era
[![](https://images.uesp.net/thumb/2/23/ON-place-Mages_Guild_%28Daggerfall%29.jpg/200px-ON-place-Mages_Guild_%28Daggerfall%29.jpg)](File_ON-place-Mages_Guild_(Daggerfall).jpg.md) [](File_ON-place-Mages_Guild_(Daggerfall).jpg.md) A Mages Guild building in High Rock High Rock had been possibly the most prosperous and stable province under the Reman Dynasty,<sup>[[1]](#cite_note-TBMOP-1)</sup> and continued to benefit under by the [Akaviri Potentates](Lore_Akaviri_Potentate.md). Concurrent with the rule of [Versidue-Shaie](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Versidue-Shaie), urban Bretons started systematically organizing themselves alongside the hierarchy the [Mages Guild](Lore_Mages_Guild.md) sometime after its founding in [2E 230](Lore_Second_Era.md#2E_230). The Mages Guild became a formidable force within High Rock,<sup>[[37]](#cite_note-PGE1High-40)</sup><sup>[[39]](#cite_note-TIEGTT-42)</sup> but it was not officially sanctioned within the Second Empire until the [Guild Act](Lore_Guild_Act.md) of [2E 321](Lore_Second_Era.md#2E_321). The Guild Act also standardized regulation of trade and transactions across the Empire, and was adopted as de facto law across Tamriel, including in High Rock.<sup>[[147]](#cite_note-HKEAYQ-156)</sup>

Circa [2E 312](Lore_Second_Era.md#2E_312), the Bretons on [Betony](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Betony) were attacked by War Chief Yzzgol and his [Seamount Clan](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Seamount_Clan). King [Renwic](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Renwic) attempted to defend his island with necromancy and an ancient Ayleid relic, but failed. Yzzgol exterminated the Bretons and renamed the island Betnikh.<sup>[[148]](#cite_note-ONKhazun-157)</sup><sup>[[149]](#cite_note-ONKing Renwic-158)</sup> King [Casimir II](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Casimir_II) of Wayrest formed an alliance with a [dragon](Lore_Dragon.md) named [Nahfahlaar](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Nahfahlaar) some time during the second century, which was ended by the [Dragonguard](Lore_Dragonguard.md) in [2E 369](Lore_Second_Era.md#2E_369).<sup>[[150]](#cite_note-159)</sup> Circa [2E 428](Lore_Second_Era.md#2E_428), High Rock was plagued by the Curse of the Crimson Moon, a [werewolf](Lore_Werewolf.md) crisis which prompted the creation of the [Order of the Silver Dawn](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Silver_Dawn) to hunt werebeasts.<sup>[[151]](#cite_note-ESOPJ-160)</sup>

#### The Interregnum and the Three Banners War
The Second Empire collapsed with the assassination of Akaviri Potentate [Savirien-Chorak](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Savirien-Chorak) in [2E 430](Lore_Second_Era.md#2E_430), marking the start of the [Interregnum](Lore_Interregnum.md). Left without a [Dragonborn](Lore_Dragonborn.md) Emperor, the [Empire of Cyrodiil](Lore_Empire_of_Cyrodiil_(Interregnum).md) was passed between petty warlords for centuries. High Rock fared much better than the other provinces at this time, despite being fractious in nature.<sup>[[53]](#cite_note-PGE3High-56)</sup> Another Orsinium was accepted as a territory of the Second Empire during Savirien-Chorak's reign,<sup>[[114]](#cite_note-PGE1WR-121)</sup><sup>[[152]](#cite_note-RM8TO-161)</sup><sup>[[147]](#cite_note-HKEAYQ-156)</sup> and [Frostbreak Fortress](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Frostbreak_Fortress) was built to help defend it.<sup>[[153]](#cite_note-162)</sup> With the Second Empire's fall, Orsinium lost its protection, and an assault spearheaded by the Bretons of [Shornhelm](Lore_Shornhelm.md) destroyed it once more in [2E 431](Lore_Second_Era.md#2E_431).<sup>[[114]](#cite_note-PGE1WR-121)</sup><sup>[[154]](#cite_note-TFo KR-163)</sup> The Bretons seized the land, and the Orcs scattered across northern Tamriel.<sup>[[155]](#cite_note-Gtt DC-164)</sup><sup>[[156]](#cite_note-OOS-165)</sup>

[![](https://images.uesp.net/thumb/1/1d/ON-concept-Daggerfall_Covenant-4500x2040.jpg/200px-ON-concept-Daggerfall_Covenant-4500x2040.jpg)](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:ON-concept-Daggerfall_Covenant-4500x2040.jpg) [](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:ON-concept-Daggerfall_Covenant-4500x2040.jpg) Races of the Daggerfall Covenant In [2E 542](Lore_Second_Era.md#2E_542), Reachmen under [Durcorach the Black Drake](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Durcorach) invaded High Rock, sacking Evermore and Camlorn. They were defeated at the gates of Daggerfall by [Emeric of Cumberland](Lore_Emeric.md), which led to the formation of the first [Daggerfall Covenant](Lore_Daggerfall_Covenant.md), signed by the kings of Daggerfall, Camlorn, Shornhelm, [Wayrest](Lore_Wayrest_(kingdom).md) and Evermore. In [2E 563](Lore_Second_Era.md#2E_563), Emeric became the king of Wayrest. Three years later, King [Ranser](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Ranser) of Shornhelm [invaded](Lore_Ranser%27s_War.md) Wayrest, angry at Emeric for rejecting his daughter's hand to instead wed [Maraya](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Maraya), daughter of King [Fahara'jad](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Fahara%27jad). The Covenant defeated him at Markwasten Moor with the help of the Orcs, who were promised the return of Orsinium for their aid.<sup>[[154]](#cite_note-TFo KR-163)</sup> Enraged by this, Ranser ordered his Spymaster to round up many Orcs in Rivenspire to be interrogated and executed. The Spymaster would end up murdering hundreds of innocent Orcs during the course of Ranser's War.<sup>[[157]](#cite_note-Marisette-166)</sup><sup>[[158]](#cite_note-Gerard-167)</sup>

[![](https://images.uesp.net/thumb/9/95/ON-render-House_Dufort_Banneret_Style.jpg/200px-ON-render-House_Dufort_Banneret_Style.jpg)](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:ON-render-House_Dufort_Banneret_Style.jpg) [](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:ON-render-House_Dufort_Banneret_Style.jpg) House Dufort knights in Cyrodiil during the Three Banners War These events led to the formation of the Greater Daggerfall Covenant, an alliance between Emeric, the Redguard King Fahara'jad, and King [Kurog gro-Orsinium](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Kurog_gro-Orsinium) of the Orcs.<sup>[[159]](#cite_note-Toa M-168)</sup> Kurog demanded restitution for the ivory Bretons looted during the Siege of Orsinium as part of his terms for joining the Covenant.<sup>[[120]](#cite_note-ESOIvory-127)</sup> The Covenant became an economic powerhouse as trade flourished.<sup>[[160]](#cite_note-THOTE-169)</sup> The Covenant later fought in the [Three Banners War](Lore_Three_Banners_War.md) during King Emeric's bid for the throne of Cyrodiil.<sup>[[159]](#cite_note-Toa M-168)</sup> The kings of the Daggerfall Covenant looked to Reman I as a model Emperor, and saw themselves as the spiritual heirs to the Second Empire.<sup>[[155]](#cite_note-Gtt DC-164)</sup> To promote their claim, the Covenant claimed it would restore "the glory of Reman's legacy" by promoting freedom, worship of the Divines, and trade.<sup>[[160]](#cite_note-THOTE-169)</sup> Race relations between the Bretons and Orcs generally improved,<sup>[[161]](#cite_note-170)</sup> despite persistent anti-Orc sentiment.<sup>[[162]](#cite_note-171)</sup> The Direnni elves were also accepted within the Covenant's borders.<sup>[[163]](#cite_note-172)</sup>

#### Fate of the Systres Archipelago
[![](https://images.uesp.net/thumb/b/b7/ON-misc-High_Isle_02.png/200px-ON-misc-High_Isle_02.png)](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:ON-misc-High_Isle_02.png) [](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:ON-misc-High_Isle_02.png) A clash with the Ascendant Order on High Isle With the destruction brought by the Three Banners War, the [Ascendant Order](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Ascendant_Order) gained traction as a pan-Tamrielic movement.<sup>[[UOL 10]](#cite_note-ESOGR-173)</sup> Many common folk were drawn in by leaders of the faction, the Ascendant Lord and his Ascendant Magus, who promised the downfall of the tyrants growing richer and powerful from misery and bloodshed.<sup>[[164]](#cite_note-MTCALM-174)</sup> Breton-influenced, the Ascendant Order likened themselves to a knightly order, though most other orders thought of them as nothing more than well-armed fanatics.<sup>[[UOL 10]](#cite_note-ESOGR-173)</sup> Nevertheless, they infiltrated nearly every level of Breton society,<sup>[[165]](#cite_note-ONU34-175)</sup> and established the Systres Archipelago as their main base of operations.

In truth, the leaders of the Ascendant Order were nobles. The Ascendant Magus was Count Damard of House Dufort, while the Ascendant Lord was [Lord Bacaro](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Bacaro_Volorus) of House Volorus from Cyrodiil. Bacaro's partner and children were killed during the [Colovian Revolt](Lore_Colovian_Revolt.md), and when the Three Banners War came around, he created the [Society of the Steadfast](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Society_of_the_Steadfast) as a humanitarian organization.<sup>[[166]](#cite_note-So ST-176)</sup> Lord Bacaro settled in his holdings on the Systres and over time built goodwill through his Steadfast Society. He then planned to leverage his reputation to lure the major players responsible for the Three Banners War to their deaths. The leaders accepted Bacaro's invitation to High Isle for peace talks, but the plot to assassinate them ultimately failed.<sup>[[167]](#cite_note-177)</sup><sup>[[67]](#cite_note-ESODR-73)</sup>

[![](https://images.uesp.net/thumb/9/95/ON-wallpaper-Firesong-2880x1620.jpg/200px-ON-wallpaper-Firesong-2880x1620.jpg)](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:ON-wallpaper-Firesong-2880x1620.jpg) [](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:ON-wallpaper-Firesong-2880x1620.jpg) Conflict on Galen Concurrently, the druids on Galen were involved in a civil war orchestrated by Bacaro's unwitting pawn, Archdruid Orlaith of the Firesong Circle. When Orlaith failed to become the Druid King and forcibly unify the druids under one banner, Bacaro took matters into his own hands. Bacaro was also a member of House Merchad through his mother's bloodline, a noble house with ties to the last Druid King, Kasorayn. As its last living descendant, he sought to claim the Ivy Throne of the Druid King as a step towards taking the [Ruby Throne](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Ruby_Throne).<sup>[[168]](#cite_note-ONLBJ-178)</sup> The Vestige confronted Bacaro at Mount Firesong, where he had ascended into a false Druid King. Utilizing his newfound power, Bacaro enslaved the dormant spirit of the volcano, which was capable of decimating Tamriel's armies.<sup>[[169]](#cite_note-ESODL-179)</sup> However, Volorus was defeated, saving the archipelago from destruction.<sup>[[170]](#cite_note-THLord-180)</sup><sup>[[171]](#cite_note-TIThrone-181)</sup>

What followed afterward was a more unified Systres Archipelago. The feudal Bretons and the druids that inhabited Galen began talks to build better relations, and the mending of wounds between the feuding noble houses of High Isle and Galen began.<sup>[[34]](#cite_note-ESOSSM-37)</sup>

#### The Third Empire
During the [Tiber War](Lore_Tiber_War.md), a Nord-Breton alliance captured [Sancre Tor](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Sancre_Tor) in [2E 852](Lore_Second_Era.md#2E_852). General Talos recaptured the city and integrated the Nordic forces, impressed by his [thu'um](Lore_Thu%27um.md), into his own army.<sup>[[112]](#cite_note-PGE1C-119)</sup> He executed the Breton leadership, and variously executed, enslaved, and sent the Breton forces back to High Rock.<sup>[[172]](#cite_note-Bo ST-182)</sup> Those Bretons who remained sought to counter Talos with Reach-magic, and in [2E 854](Lore_Second_Era.md#2E_854), entrusted a Reachman to assassinate [Cuhlecain](Lore_Cuhlecain.md) and his general. Talos survived the attack, and went on to found the [Third Empire](Lore_Third_Empire.md)<sup>[[112]](#cite_note-PGE1C-119)</sup> —though *[The Arcturian Heresy](Lore_The_Arcturian_Heresy.md)* claims Talos himself slew Cuhlecain, and placed the blame on his enemies.<sup>[[173]](#cite_note-TAH-183)</sup>

At some point in their history, the Bretons were ruled by witch-kings.<sup>[[174]](#cite_note-CP-184)</sup><sup>[[UOL 11]](#cite_note-DGP-185)</sup> Talos, now known as [Tiber Septim](Lore_Tiber_Septim.md), would easily conquer the squabbling Breton kingdoms, but would find it impossible to truly squash the sectarian conflicts between them that hampered trade and prosperity.<sup>[[37]](#cite_note-PGE1High-40)</sup><sup>[[53]](#cite_note-PGE3High-56)</sup> Septim opted to entrust a governor of his choosing to end the feud between High Rock's witch-kings, which was a successful endeavor.<sup>[[175]](#cite_note-186)</sup>

### Third Era
[![](https://images.uesp.net/thumb/d/d4/DF-misc-Death.jpg/200px-DF-misc-Death.jpg)](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:DF-misc-Death.jpg) [](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:DF-misc-Death.jpg) Druids carrying a coffin in the Iliac Bay circa 3E 417<sup>[[176]](#cite_note-DFDeath-187)</sup> The Dream of Kasorayn foretold of druids retaking their place on Tamriel, and a possible future where the druidic circles would unite under one banner and reestablish themselves as the Druids of Galen.<sup>[[UOL 12]](#cite_note-188)</sup><sup>[[UOL 13]](#cite_note-ESOYoutube Firesong Tour-189)</sup><sup>[[177]](#cite_note-ESOOrlaith-190)</sup><sup>[[169]](#cite_note-ESODL-179)</sup> As previous attempts to reinvigorate their ways had led to great bloodshed,<sup>[[62]](#cite_note-ESODruid King-67)</sup><sup>[[177]](#cite_note-ESOOrlaith-190)</sup> druids instead began to seek a future which would not depend on a king or a prophecy to improve the world.<sup>[[34]](#cite_note-ESOSSM-37)</sup> In this respect, Kasorayn's dream may simply be a metaphor, encouraging druids to live life as if the dream was close to fruition.<sup>[[169]](#cite_note-ESODL-179)</sup> It is unknown what parts of the prophecy came true, but by the fifth century of the Third Era, druids were once again present in the regions surrounding the Iliac Bay.<sup>[[176]](#cite_note-DFDeath-187)</sup><sup>[[UOL 14]](#cite_note-DFTDE-191)</sup> "By the Arch Druid" is a common exclamation by Bretons of this era.<sup>[[178]](#cite_note-ARExclamations-192)</sup><sup>[[179]](#cite_note-DFExclamations-193)</sup>

By the Third Era, there were eight major Breton powers in the province of High Rock: the kingdoms of Daggerfall, Camlorn, Wayrest, Shornhelm, [Northpoint](Lore_Northpoint.md), Evermore, [Farrun](Lore_Farrun.md), and [Jehanna](Lore_Jehanna.md).<sup>[[180]](#cite_note-EWR-194)</sup> Since most Emperors in the [Third Era](Lore_Third_Era.md) were Bretons or raised in High Rock, Bretons were generally supportive of [Imperial](Lore_Imperial.md) rule, but were often disgruntled by its ineffectual protection.<sup>[[181]](#cite_note-TFOTU-195)</sup> However, the decentralized nature of Breton society also fostered surprising resilience during times of upheaval.<sup>[[53]](#cite_note-PGE3High-56)</sup> One of the best examples of this was during the defeat of the [Camoran Usurper](Lore_Camoran_Usurper.md), when four of the smaller Breton city-states—Dwynnen, [Kambria](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Kambria), [Phrygias](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Phrygias), and [Ykalon](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Ykalon) —led a united force that halted the Usurper's long northward advance and finally defeated him in the [Battle of Firewaves](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Battle_of_Firewaves) in [3E 267](Lore_Third_Era.md#3E_267).<sup>[[181]](#cite_note-TFOTU-195)</sup> Baron Othro, who had already gained fame for his defeat of the Lich of Castle Wightmoor during the [Battle of Wightmoor](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Battle_of_Wightmoor) fourteen years prior, formed the modern barony of Dwynnen, which would eventually grow into of the more powerful city-states in western High Rock.<sup>[[181]](#cite_note-TFOTU-195)</sup>

[![](https://images.uesp.net/thumb/9/90/LO-misc-Daggerfall_History.gif/200px-LO-misc-Daggerfall_History.gif)](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:LO-misc-Daggerfall_History.gif) [](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:LO-misc-Daggerfall_History.gif) The Battle of Cryngaine Field Other wars which occurred in High Rock during this Era included the [War of the Bend'r-mahk](Lore_War_of_the_Bend%27r-mahk.md) in 3E 397, where Skyrim conquered land in the east which included the Kingdom of Jehanna. It later came to light that [Jagar Tharn](Lore_Jagar_Tharn.md) was behind Skyrim's aggression. When [Emperor Uriel Septim VII](Lore_Uriel_Septim_VII.md) regained his throne following the Imperial Simulacrum, great efforts were taken to revert the damage done by Tharn. At the other end of High Rock, the [War of Betony](Lore_War_of_Betony.md) was fought between Daggerfall and Sentinel over the eponymous island in 3E 405. The [Battle of Cryngaine Field](Lore_Wars.md#Battle_of_Cryngaine_Field) resulted in Daggerfall's victory, though at the cost of the life of their [King Lysandus](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Lysandus). His son and heir, [Gothryd](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Gothryd), was crowned the new king of Daggerfall after the war.<sup>[[53]](#cite_note-PGE3High-56)</sup>

[![](https://images.uesp.net/thumb/0/0a/LO-misc-Numidium_Wall.png/200px-LO-misc-Numidium_Wall.png)](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:LO-misc-Numidium_Wall.png) [](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:LO-misc-Numidium_Wall.png) The [Numidium](Lore_Numidium.md), responsible for the Warp in the West On the 7th of Frostfall in [3E 417](Lore_Third_Era.md#3E_417), the [Warp in the West](Lore_Warp_in_the_West.md) occurred. The roughly two dozen city-states comprising southwestern High Rock were suddenly, forcefully, and mysteriously united into two kingdoms: Daggerfall and Wayrest, with Orsinium taking control of part of the Wrothgarian Mountains in central High Rock.<sup>[[182]](#cite_note-196)</sup><sup>[[183]](#cite_note-TWINT-197)</sup> The amount of squabbling kingdoms in High Rock was reduced from about a hundred to five. According to Imperial sources, it was the most unified High Rock had ever been.<sup>[[53]](#cite_note-PGE3High-56)</sup>

The populace and culture of the Systres remained largely Breton by [3E 433](Lore_Third_Era.md#3E_433).<sup>[[5]](#cite_note-OBBR-5)</sup> Despite this, some maps presented the islands as part of Hammerfell's territory just years prior during [3E 427](Lore_Third_Era.md#3E_427).<sup>[[nb 1]](#intnote_Systres)</sup>

### Fourth Era
In the early [Fourth Era](Lore_Fourth_Era.md), following the [Oblivion Crisis](Lore_Oblivion_Crisis.md) and the destabilization of the Third Empire, the combined forces of Hammerfell and High Rock sacked Orsinium, leading many Orc refugees to flee east into Skyrim.<sup>[[184]](#cite_note-Lo S-198)</sup>

High Rock was still part of the Empire when [Titus Mede II](Lore_Titus_Mede_II.md) ascended the throne of Cyrodiil in [4E 168](Lore_Fourth_Era.md#4E_168), and assisted Hammerfell during the [Great War](Lore_Great_War.md). The [Third Aldmeri Dominion](Lore_Aldmeri_Dominion.md) took Hammerfell's southern coastline, leaving Hegathe the lone surviving state. Those who survived the March of Thirst joined Legion reinforcements from High Rock in northern Hammerfell in [4E 173](Lore_Fourth_Era.md#4E_173), and the Dominion suffered losses in the province soon after. The Dominion withdrew in [4E 174](Lore_Fourth_Era.md#4E_174). Bretons also participated in the climactic [Battle of the Red Ring](Lore_Battle_of_the_Red_Ring.md) in [4E 175](Lore_Fourth_Era.md#4E_175).<sup>[[185]](#cite_note-199)</sup>

[![](https://images.uesp.net/thumb/6/6c/LG-quest-Regicide_02.jpg/200px-LG-quest-Regicide_02.jpg)](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:LG-quest-Regicide_02.jpg) [](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:LG-quest-Regicide_02.jpg) Corsairs sack Wayrest (Legends) In [4E 188](Lore_Fourth_Era.md#4E_188), King Barynia of Wayrest was overcome by paranoia when rumors of conspiracy reached his ears. He purposely left his city vulnerable to outside attacks, hoping his enemies would be killed in the chaos. His actions led to the sack of Wayrest by Breton corsairs. The city's nobles hired an [assassin](Lore_Forgotten_Hero.md) from the [Dark Brotherhood](Lore_Dark_Brotherhood.md) amid the conflict, though Barynia's fate is ultimately unknown.<sup>[[186]](#cite_note-LTFDB-200)</sup> The corsairs raided and destroyed the Dark Brotherhood sanctuary hidden in Wayrest before they departed.<sup>[[186]](#cite_note-LTFDB-200)</sup><sup>[[187]](#cite_note-CJ2-201)</sup> Piracy would remain an issue by [4E 197](Lore_Fourth_Era.md#4E_197) around the Wayrest area.<sup>[[27]](#cite_note-Cookbook2-29)</sup>

Circa [4E 201](Lore_Fourth_Era.md#4E_201), the [Stormcloaks](Lore_Stormcloaks.md) looked to their neighbors in High Rock for aid in the midst of the [Skyrim Civil War](Lore_Skyrim_Civil_War.md). The Bretons, who had good relations with the Empire, refused to respond to the Stormcloaks.<sup>[[188]](#cite_note-SRUlfric Galmar-202)</sup>

## Culture
[![](https://images.uesp.net/thumb/8/8e/LO-misc-highrock1.jpg/150px-LO-misc-highrock1.jpg)](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:LO-misc-highrock1.jpg) [](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:LO-misc-highrock1.jpg) A sketch of a northern guardsman by '[¥R](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:%C2%A5R)'Bretons are an intelligent, individualistic, energetic, pragmatic, and humorous people.<sup>[[UOL 15]](#cite_note-Mara Wasserman-203)</sup><sup>[[122]](#cite_note-TRB5-129)</sup><sup>[[94]](#cite_note-WJOTB-100)</sup> They are said to enjoy intellectual pursuits; they often have an affinity for anything related to logic and ordered complexity.<sup>[[19]](#cite_note-KE9-21)</sup> Their love of knowledge and affinity for commerce drives them into a host of careers, including trading, the military, sailing, medicine, textiles, manufacturing, writing, theology, philosophy, banking, all kinds of artistry, and other scholarly pursuits.<sup>[[94]](#cite_note-WJOTB-100)</sup><sup>[[76]](#cite_note-FOA-82)</sup><sup>[[189]](#cite_note-BB-204)</sup><sup>[[190]](#cite_note-16AOM-205)</sup><sup>[[191]](#cite_note-TR-206)</sup> Their scholarly institutions include the [Invisible College of Daggerfall](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Invisible_College_of_Daggerfall) and [Schools of Julianos](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:School_of_Julianos).<sup>[[192]](#cite_note-CS-207)</sup><sup>[[193]](#cite_note-DFJ-208)</sup> Espionage has also proven to be one of their strong suits; Breton double agents, assassins, and spies have turned the tide of wars throughout recorded history.<sup>[[112]](#cite_note-PGE1C-119)</sup><sup>[[194]](#cite_note-BOST-209)</sup><sup>[[195]](#cite_note-2920FS-210)</sup><sup>[[196]](#cite_note-WAP-211)</sup><sup>[[197]](#cite_note-CF-212)</sup> Bretons value the principles of freedom, praising it in their tavern songs and propaganda,<sup>[[97]](#cite_note-TBo GM-103)</sup><sup>[[198]](#cite_note-THot E-213)</sup> but this only extends so far in practice.<sup>[[198]](#cite_note-THot E-213)</sup> In [2E 582](Lore_Second_Era.md#2E_582), the people of Evermore were allowed to freely criticize Queen Arzhela and the royal family,<sup>[[199]](#cite_note-214)</sup><sup>[[200]](#cite_note-ARE-215)</sup> while using excessive profanity in the presence of nobility in High Isle was criminal.<sup>[[201]](#cite_note-216)</sup> In the Third Era, a prolific bard and poet Darius Shano is also said to have criticized nobility, commoners and the Divines alike, receiving much scorn, but was only executed after ridiculing Tiber Septim.<sup>[[202]](#cite_note-16AOM9-217)</sup>

### Sex, Marriage, and Family
