→ *For more detailed information, see: Breton section in the [Sex](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Sex#Bretons) and [Marriage](Lore_Marriage.md#Breton) articles* [![](https://images.uesp.net/thumb/2/24/ON-quest-The_Sea_Runs_Restless_08.jpg/200px-ON-quest-The_Sea_Runs_Restless_08.jpg)](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:ON-quest-The_Sea_Runs_Restless_08.jpg) [](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:ON-quest-The_Sea_Runs_Restless_08.jpg) A Druidic arousal-inducing artifact (ESO) Arranging fortuitous marriages are the norm among Breton noble families,<sup>[[203]](#cite_note-218)</sup><sup>[[UOL 16]](#cite_note-ONHCP-219)</sup> but having courtships before choosing a partner is another option. Suitors may woo the person they are courting with various gifts,<sup>[[204]](#cite_note-220)</sup> such as a bouquet of rare flowers, a serenade, or something more extravagant.<sup>[[205]](#cite_note-221)</sup> The practice of dowries exists in Breton marriages.<sup>[[206]](#cite_note-MTCAlga-222)</sup> There is some societal expectations in your partner. A noble lady in a relation with her manservant would be considered forbidden love, for example.<sup>[[207]](#cite_note-223)</sup> Love charms are popular among Breton nobles and merchant lords who seek to improve their love lives.<sup>[[208]](#cite_note-224)</sup> Woman seeking to marry into the nobility may style their hair into a traditional updo.<sup>[[209]](#cite_note-ONBBBB-225)</sup>

It is a tradition for Breton parents to keep their childrens' bronzed baby teeth in a jar as remembrances.<sup>[[210]](#cite_note-226)</sup> Some Breton families have retained heirlooms from their Nedic ancestors,<sup>[[211]](#cite_note-227)</sup> and tea sets are common family heirlooms.<sup>[[212]](#cite_note-228)</sup> Breton families host annual summer reunions, where they gather [candleflies](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Candlefly) to illuminate their dinner, then release them into the evening sky after dessert.<sup>[[213]](#cite_note-ONTCL-229)</sup> Quilting and sewing circles are examples of hobby groups one might find in High Rock.<sup>[[214]](#cite_note-230)</sup><sup>[[215]](#cite_note-231)</sup> A quilt of "lost hope" may be crafted by a Breton mother and daughter to work through past regrets and sorrows.<sup>[[216]](#cite_note-232)</sup> Using [malachite](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Malachite) to make needles is popular among the Bretons of eastern High Rock.<sup>[[217]](#cite_note-233)</sup>

A Third Era joke book poked fun at Breton promiscuity.<sup>[[218]](#cite_note-Lore Jokes-234)</sup> The [Prostitutes Guild](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Prostitutes_Guild) has a large, almost palatial guildhouse located in an affluent part of Camlorn.<sup>[[219]](#cite_note-MOT4-235)</sup> Some Bretons utilize [drugs](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Drugs) to enhance their bedchamber activities.<sup>[[220]](#cite_note-AIOM-236)</sup> [Waking Day](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Waking_Day) is a Breton holiday originally invented to wake the spirits of nature which evolved into an orgiastic celebration of winter's end.<sup>[[221]](#cite_note-237)</sup> The druids of the settlement of Llanshara on the Systres isle of Galen possessed an artifact which caused extreme arousal to those in its vicinity.<sup>[[222]](#cite_note-TSRR-238)</sup><sup>[[223]](#cite_note-Mina N-239)</sup> This same settlement had a 'Ritual of Life's Commencement', an ancient tradition celebrating the creation of life through the sexual union of druids.<sup>[[224]](#cite_note-Ro LC-240)</sup> The Bretons of High Isle idolized [mermaids](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Mermaid) as fertility icons.<sup>[[225]](#cite_note-High Idol-241)</sup>

Bretons have the Law of Consanguinity, which bans marriage between close relatives,<sup>[[226]](#cite_note-TSo PE-242)</sup> though Breton nobility are often rumored to practice incest. Prominent Bretons like King Ranser allegedly slept with every sibling in his royal line; rumors even implied that his daughter [Rayelle](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Rayelle) was a product of one such coupling. Other tales speak of pagan rituals, paint-slick bodies and mind-altering concoctions as having their places in "blood purity" customs. However, these stories are typically considered just that — stories — and most historians disregard them as poor grist and sensationalism.<sup>[[68]](#cite_note-LABHI-74)</sup>

The [Laumont](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Laumont) line is rumored to have originated from a union of a Breton and a [flame atronach](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Flame_Atronach), though this is dismissed by some members of the family as exaggeration or embellishment.<sup>[[227]](#cite_note-Lud Lau Hireling-243)</sup> Though most sources claim [Haymon Camoran](Lore_Haymon_Camoran.md) was of Bosmeri Camoran lineage, a legend that he was the son of [Molag Bal](Lore_Molag_Bal.md) and a Breton woman has nonetheless persisted through the years.<sup>[[228]](#cite_note-DCSG-244)</sup> The Breton Galthis was the lover of [Vaermina](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Vaermina), and became her [Omen](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Omen) of a Hundred Prophecies.<sup>[[229]](#cite_note-245)</sup><sup>[[230]](#cite_note-246)</sup>

### Death
→ *For more detailed information, see: [Breton Death Beliefs](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Breton_Death_Beliefs)* [![](https://images.uesp.net/thumb/5/57/ON-place-Pelin_Graveyard.jpg/200px-ON-place-Pelin_Graveyard.jpg)](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:ON-place-Pelin_Graveyard.jpg) [](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:ON-place-Pelin_Graveyard.jpg) A Breton graveyard [![](https://images.uesp.net/thumb/6/63/ON-misc-Noble_Knight%27s_Rest.png/200px-ON-misc-Noble_Knight%27s_Rest.png)](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:ON-misc-Noble_Knight%27s_Rest.png) [](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:ON-misc-Noble_Knight%27s_Rest.png) A Knight's Carved Sarcophagus People of the northern regions of High Rock cremate their dead without exception, while burial remains common in the south. The Breton tradition of cremating the dead dates back to the days of High Rock's witch kings,<sup>[[174]](#cite_note-CP-184)</sup> with cremains commonly being stored in urns.<sup>[[231]](#cite_note-247)</sup>

The Bretons of the south build stone cemeteries to house their dead, and the nobility has always been interred in ornate mausoleums. Many Breton cemeteries are designed to provide direct sunlight on certain graves on highly specific high holy days on the Breton calendar. The ancient cemetery of Cath Bedraud, home to the corpses of many generations of Breton royalty, is constructed in a series of concentric bands atop a hill, with the oldest, most prestigious graves positioned in the high center of the graveyard.<sup>[[39]](#cite_note-TIEGTT-42)</sup> Southern Bretons also sometimes practice [mummification](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Mummy).<sup>[[232]](#cite_note-DF-248)</sup><sup>[[233]](#cite_note-249)</sup>

### Language
→ *For more detailed information, see: [Bretic](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Bretic)* The language of the Bretons is called Bretic.<sup>[[234]](#cite_note-KEPI-250)</sup> It is not widely spoken anymore, but the Sephavre (sung during the observance of [Broken Diamonds](Lore_Broken_Diamonds.md)) is written in Old Bretic.<sup>[[235]](#cite_note-BD-251)</sup> Before High Rock's integration into the Alessian Empire circa 1E 1029,<sup>[[93]](#cite_note-BSOHR-99)</sup> some Breton nobility were known to write in [Aldmeris](Lore_Aldmeris_(language).md) as a sign of their pride for their elvish heritage.<sup>[[236]](#cite_note-ONHTOS-252)</sup>

Druids speak in their own language; Bretons from the Systres Archipelago have some loan words from them.<sup>[[237]](#cite_note-Isobel-253)</sup><sup>[[68]](#cite_note-LABHI-74)</sup> Druidic runes are referred to as draoifoglyphs.<sup>[[238]](#cite_note-OSRCodex-254)</sup>

### Names
→ *For more detailed information, see: [Breton Names](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Breton_Names)* Bretons names follow a first and last name structure. The earliest recorded Breton from the Merethic Era had a surname.<sup>[[75]](#cite_note-LAIA-81)</sup>

### Holidays
→ *For more detailed information, see: [Breton Holidays](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Breton_Holidays)* [![](https://images.uesp.net/thumb/5/5a/ON-crown_store-Day_of_Release_Roisterer.jpg/200px-ON-crown_store-Day_of_Release_Roisterer.jpg)](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:ON-crown_store-Day_of_Release_Roisterer.jpg) [](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:ON-crown_store-Day_of_Release_Roisterer.jpg) Two Bretons dressed for the Day of Release in Daggerfall (right) The Bretons have been in Tamriel since before recorded history. Their holidays have remained almost unchanged since primitive times, though new holidays have been created to replace those which have lost popularity.<sup>[[18]](#cite_note-HOTIB-20)</sup> An example of a holiday is their celebration of [Saturalia](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Saturalia), which heralds the [New Life Festival](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:New_Life_Festival).<sup>[[239]](#cite_note-BLST-255)</sup> Originally a holiday held to celebrate a forgotten god of debauchery, Saturalia has transformed into a day where gifts are given, parades are held, and feasts are had.<sup>[[240]](#cite_note-256)</sup> Region specific holiday examples are [Waking Day](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Waking_Day), invented by the people of the [Yeorth Burrowland](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Yeorth_Burrowland) in prehistoric times to wake the spirits of nature after a long and cold winter, but has evolved into a sort of orgiastic celebration of the end of winter.<sup>[[241]](#cite_note-257)</sup> The celebration of [Gardtide](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Gardtide) hearkens back to the old cult of the flower,<sup>[[18]](#cite_note-HOTIB-20)</sup> as this festival in [Tamarilyn Point](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Tamarilyn_Point) was originally meant to honor [Druagaa](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Druagaa), the goddess of flowers. Worship of the goddess is all but dead, but the celebration is always lively.<sup>[[242]](#cite_note-258)</sup>

### Food
→ *For more detailed information, see: [Breton Cuisine](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Breton_Cuisine)* [![](https://images.uesp.net/thumb/7/72/ON-npc-Chef_Donolon_02.jpg/200px-ON-npc-Chef_Donolon_02.jpg)](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:ON-npc-Chef_Donolon_02.jpg) [](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:ON-npc-Chef_Donolon_02.jpg) Donolon, a renowned Breton chef [![](https://images.uesp.net/thumb/f/f1/BK-misc-Official_Cookbook_Potage_le_Magnifique.png/200px-BK-misc-Official_Cookbook_Potage_le_Magnifique.png)](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:BK-misc-Official_Cookbook_Potage_le_Magnifique.png) [](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:BK-misc-Official_Cookbook_Potage_le_Magnifique.png) Potage le Magnifique, a Breton dish Breton cuisine is considered to be some of the very best in Tamriel, with many of Tamriel's greatest cooks having been Bretons.<sup>[[243]](#cite_note-259)</sup> Breton cuisine takes advantage of the effects of alchemy through cooking, with specific ingredients not mattering but the principles of composition, the balance of essences, flavors, oils, and herbs; the preparation of these meals can cause them to act as a potion might.<sup>[[244]](#cite_note-t IC28-260)</sup><sup>:28</sup> The complexity of certain recipes means that some Breton cooks use sundials to track cooking times.<sup>[[245]](#cite_note-261)</sup> Examples of a light Breton meal include grilled and deboned rock pigeons, combwort chutney, ballom pudding, and syllabub (milk and cider).<sup>[[246]](#cite_note-Pa P-262)</sup>

It is common practice for Breton families to store and serve cows' milk in porcelain pitchers.<sup>[[247]](#cite_note-263)</sup> [Goat](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Goat)'s milk is used to make cheese by the inhabitants of Stormhaven, which Bretons prize for its moistness.<sup>[[248]](#cite_note-264)</sup> Large ornate platters are used to present and serve beef roasts prepared in wine and spices for holidays.<sup>[[249]](#cite_note-265)</sup>

The chef [Donolon](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Donolon) was a legendary confectioner whose clientele included nobles and even [Daedric Princes](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Daedric_Prince). Regardless of a person or entity's status, they might have to wait years to taste his most coveted creation, the Jubilee Cake.<sup>[[250]](#cite_note-ONCD-266)</sup><sup>[[251]](#cite_note-ONAFC-267)</sup> The [Surilie](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Surilie) family are Bretonic vintners whose history stretches through at least three eras.<sup>[[UOL 17]](#cite_note-ESOAMA-268)</sup><sup>[[252]](#cite_note-SRSBW-269)</sup> They produce some of the best wines in Tamriel, with it being particularly popular in Cyrodiil, where they established their vineyards at Skingrad, the wine-producing capital of Tamriel.<sup>[[253]](#cite_note-OBGS-270)</sup><sup>[[254]](#cite_note-OBRCS-271)</sup>

### Architecture
Construction of Breton villages and towns vary depending on their location. For example, buildings in mountainous regions such as Kambria are fully stone. In southwestern High Rock, buildings are comprised of wood or stone with thatched roofs. Breton cities are described as having an austere grandeur.<sup>[[53]](#cite_note-PGE3High-56)</sup><sup>[[255]](#cite_note-CKL1-272)</sup> According to Imperial sources, function is valued over form, resulting in earthen, hand-crafted dwellings free from ornament.<sup>[[39]](#cite_note-TIEGTT-42)</sup> In reality, Breton architecture often features patternwork, sometimes exceptionally ornate; basic patterns include common Breton motifs such as the trefoil and basic knotwork. More ornate examples on buildings such as castles, cathedrals, and guild buildings feature detailed friezes, bas reliefs, and intricate stained glass windows. The triquetra motif was particularly common during the mid-Second Era, and was featured on numerous Breton buildings, furniture and other crafts. Breton architecture features heavy use of the pointed arch, evident in their walls, doors, windows, and towers.<sup>[[256]](#cite_note-273)</sup> Pointed arches in Breton architecture are speculated to be a remnant of Direnni influence.<sup>[[257]](#cite_note-274)</sup>

Breton class stratification is reflected in their architecture, however, even the lower classes might have spaces that are fancy when compared to elsewhere.<sup>[[UOL 16]](#cite_note-ONHCP-219)</sup> Most people in High Rock live in small cottages in the countryside or townhouses in the cities; only the nobility and their servants live in large castles. Despite efforts under Tiber Septim to demilitarize the province by demolishing defensive structures, many villages are still surrounded by high walls, and fortresses dot the landscape.<sup>[[37]](#cite_note-PGE1High-40)</sup><sup>[[255]](#cite_note-CKL1-272)</sup> In the Systres Archipelago, the norm is that medium end homes have red clay tile flooring, while high end homes have elegant parquet flooring.<sup>[[UOL 18]](#cite_note-275)</sup>

Breton architecture shares similarities to the "Western Imperial Style", a style synonymous with villages throughout the western Empire, but which also features prominently in Imperial centers in the east, such as [Pelagiad](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Pelagiad) and [Caldera](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Caldera).<sup>[[258]](#cite_note-276)</sup><sup>[[259]](#cite_note-277)</sup> Both Imperials and Bretons have influenced Redguard cosmopolitan architectural styles.<sup>[[260]](#cite_note-PGE1Hammerfell-278)</sup>

The druids create settlements where manmade constructions intertwine with and honor nature,<sup>[[261]](#cite_note-ONGTSC-279)</sup><sup>[[262]](#cite_note-280)</sup> echoing the old druidic belief that civilization should develop alongside nature and not tame it.<sup>[[67]](#cite_note-ESODR-73)</sup><sup>[[nb 6]](#intnote_Architecture)</sup>

[Dutheil, the Mad Architect](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Mad_Architect), was a Breton architect from the mid- [Second Era](Lore_Second_Era.md) whose talents led him to work for multiple Daedric Princes across the various planes of Oblivion, in exchange for the opportunity to commit vengeance against those that wronged him. He was known for his black-spired castles, with some being built on Nirn, such as the Crypt of Hearts.<sup>[[263]](#cite_note-TAWPT-281)</sup><sup>[[264]](#cite_note-End Sta-282)</sup><sup>[[265]](#cite_note-ESOTubidan_the_Alarmist-283)</sup><sup>[[266]](#cite_note-Req-284)</sup>

- [![](https://images.uesp.net/thumb/e/e2/ON-concept-High_Isle_Architecture.jpg/200px-ON-concept-High_Isle_Architecture.jpg)](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:ON-concept-High_Isle_Architecture.jpg) Systrean Breton Architecture
- [![](https://images.uesp.net/thumb/2/26/ON-render-Gonfalon_Bay.jpg/200px-ON-render-Gonfalon_Bay.jpg)](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:ON-render-Gonfalon_Bay.jpg) Systrean Breton Skyline
- [![](https://images.uesp.net/thumb/3/33/ON-place-Red_Petal_Bastion_Keep.jpg/200px-ON-place-Red_Petal_Bastion_Keep.jpg)](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:ON-place-Red_Petal_Bastion_Keep.jpg) A fortress
- [![](https://images.uesp.net/thumb/a/a1/ON-place-Dusklight_Inn.jpg/200px-ON-place-Dusklight_Inn.jpg)](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:ON-place-Dusklight_Inn.jpg) A tavern
- [![](https://images.uesp.net/thumb/8/84/ON-load-Apartment_Inn.jpg/200px-ON-load-Apartment_Inn.jpg)](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:ON-load-Apartment_Inn.jpg) Breton Inn interior
- [![](https://images.uesp.net/thumb/f/f0/ON-load-Breton_House.jpg/200px-ON-load-Breton_House.jpg)](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:ON-load-Breton_House.jpg) Breton house interior
- [![](https://images.uesp.net/thumb/2/2c/ON-load-Daggerfall_Manor.jpg/200px-ON-load-Daggerfall_Manor.jpg)](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:ON-load-Daggerfall_Manor.jpg) Breton manor interior
- [![](https://images.uesp.net/thumb/6/6f/ON-load-Highhallow_Hold.png/200px-ON-load-Highhallow_Hold.png)](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:ON-load-Highhallow_Hold.png) Systrean Breton manor interior
- [![](https://images.uesp.net/thumb/8/86/ON-misc-High_Isle_Furniture.png/200px-ON-misc-High_Isle_Furniture.png)](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:ON-misc-High_Isle_Furniture.png) Systrean Breton Chest knotwork
- [![](https://images.uesp.net/thumb/6/6c/ON-misc-High_Isle_Furniture_02.png/200px-ON-misc-High_Isle_Furniture_02.png)](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:ON-misc-High_Isle_Furniture_02.png) High End Systrean Breton Furniture
- [![](https://images.uesp.net/thumb/5/53/ON-concept-Druidic_Architecture.png/200px-ON-concept-Druidic_Architecture.png)](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:ON-concept-Druidic_Architecture.png) Druid Architecture and Symbols
- [![](https://images.uesp.net/thumb/c/c9/ON-load-Gladesong_Arboretum.png/200px-ON-load-Gladesong_Arboretum.png)](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:ON-load-Gladesong_Arboretum.png) Druid Architecture Interior
- [![](https://images.uesp.net/thumb/5/50/CT-Castle Kit-Preview_Stone.png/200px-CT-Castle Kit-Preview_Stone.png)](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:CT-Castle Kit-Preview_Stone.png)"Classic Castle" theme, inspired by Breton and Western Imperial styles

### Fashion: Armaments, Cosmetics, etc.
[![](https://images.uesp.net/thumb/c/ca/ON-concept-Nobles%27_Fashionable_Attire.jpg/200px-ON-concept-Nobles%27_Fashionable_Attire.jpg)](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:ON-concept-Nobles%27_Fashionable_Attire.jpg) [](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:ON-concept-Nobles%27_Fashionable_Attire.jpg) Female Breton Fashion in [2E 582](Lore_Second_Era.md#2E_582) Influenced by constant warfare, Breton fashion is very utilitarian with various flairs,<sup>[[39]](#cite_note-TIEGTT-42)</sup> while Breton arts and crafts are influenced by their time under the Direnni.<sup>[[13]](#cite_note-ONBS-15)</sup> Examples of both together are Breton armor and weapons, which are ornate but practical,<sup>[[39]](#cite_note-TIEGTT-42)</sup> yet they also display a sophistication reminiscent of elven elegance.<sup>[[13]](#cite_note-ONBS-15)</sup> For clothing, Breton men like to look good in their everyday wear while they're at their trades,<sup>[[267]](#cite_note-285)</sup> while women may add a feminine flair to their clothing.<sup>[[268]](#cite_note-286)</sup> Those seeking to display their wealth do so through rich fabrics and glistening ornamentation.<sup>[[269]](#cite_note-287)</sup> The nobility prefers clothing that is elegant yet austere, which harkens back to High Rock's tradition of knightly orders.<sup>[[270]](#cite_note-288)</sup> Nobles typically wear simple yet elegant robes over their clothing when traveling to avoid sullying them, and display their wealth through the metal fastenings holding the robes together.<sup>[[271]](#cite_note-289)</sup> Nobles from Wayrest are known to throw dress-up parties utilizing suits of fur from various animals, including werewolves.<sup>[[272]](#cite_note-ONMenninia-290)</sup>

[![](https://images.uesp.net/thumb/8/8f/ON-concept-Breton_Heavy.jpg/200px-ON-concept-Breton_Heavy.jpg)](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:ON-concept-Breton_Heavy.jpg) [](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:ON-concept-Breton_Heavy.jpg) Breton plate armor Breton arms are described as standard fare, in that when one thinks of a sword, a Breton blade will typically appear. Despite this, Breton arms and armaments are not unvaried and have can have their own flair, such as that shields may be emblazoned with lion heads, or [staves](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Staves) can be carved and adorned with enchanted gems.<sup>[[273]](#cite_note-ILAABC-291)</sup> The mass-produced, one-handed, double-edged heavy broadsword commonly used by the Imperial Legions of the Third Empire were inspired by elaborate, decorated Breton broadsword designs. Broadswords are commonly used with shields, and Bretons favor the heavy tower shield. [Highland Bretons](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Highland_Bretons) were the first to use the heavy two-handed sword called the claymore, but their Redguard neighbors quickly adapted them to their own styles of fighting.<sup>[[274]](#cite_note-MWGaro-292)</sup> Breton bows tend to be longbows—weapons made of one piece of springy wood. Yew, elm, and ash are common in Breton longbows, as the wood is dense and strong, but flexible if tillered properly.<sup>[[275]](#cite_note-293)</sup> The Bretons of old were said to have put [skyshard](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Skyshard) silvers into the hilts of their swords, while early mages are believed to have built staves from roots of the [Wyrd Tree](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Wyrd_Tree).<sup>[[276]](#cite_note-ONABS-294)</sup>

[![](https://images.uesp.net/thumb/7/77/ON-misc-Breton_Outfits.jpg/200px-ON-misc-Breton_Outfits.jpg)](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:ON-misc-Breton_Outfits.jpg) [](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:ON-misc-Breton_Outfits.jpg) Male Breton Fashion in [2E 582](Lore_Second_Era.md#2E_582) Breton armor consists primarily of leathers, chainmail, scale mail, and plate armor, with tabards and heraldry added to the mix.<sup>[[UOL 1]](#cite_note-ON2022-9)</sup><sup>[[277]](#cite_note-295)</sup><sup>[[273]](#cite_note-ILAABC-291)</sup> The wealthy are known to add additional materials in the forging process of their plate armor to vary the color of their armor.<sup>[[273]](#cite_note-ILAABC-291)</sup> Bretons see tanning as a fine art. Quality pieces can use soft hides from animals such as [guars](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Guar) and cattle strategically placed at areas such as the joints of a gorget, or a [wolf](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Wolf)'s hide for vambraces.<sup>[[273]](#cite_note-ILAABC-291)</sup> Werewolf leather is prized by both armorsmiths and alchemists, and it is known to be utilized especially by Glenumbrans.<sup>[[272]](#cite_note-ONMenninia-290)</sup><sup>[[278]](#cite_note-296)</sup> For metals, Bretons are known to use a variety: [iron](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Iron) and [steel](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Steel) are common, with [ebony](Lore_Ebony.md) among the more exotic options.<sup>[[279]](#cite_note-SRSKA-297)</sup> [Paladins](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Paladins) from Daggerfall found a way to make armor stronger than ebony using [rubedite](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Rubedite), a red ore.<sup>[[280]](#cite_note-298)</sup> Enchanted armor created with metalworking tools blessed by Akatosh and Zenithar was coated with a rubedite metal enamel, then tempered with captured dragonflame.<sup>[[281]](#cite_note-299)</sup>

Tradition dictates that mages Tamriel-wide wear sturdy and practical robes, as magic itself is their armor.<sup>[[282]](#cite_note-300)</sup> Magic as armor is especially true for Breton mages, who are known for utilizing their natural magical talents to stand their ground against the fiercest opponents in battle by summoning fierce [daedra](Lore_Daedra.md) to aid them, or augmenting themselves with wards and bound armor.<sup>[[283]](#cite_note-301)</sup> Bretons utilize cloth to craft their light-weight armor, which may be structurally reinforced using bone, horn, or cartilage. The outer layer of jerkins and breeches may contain damask or ornamental silk. Underneath that is a layer or layers of durable fabrics such as cambric or burlap, which are often quilted or padded for protection from blows.<sup>[[284]](#cite_note-302)</sup> Distinct from mages are spell-knights, comparable to the Tamrielic tradition of battlemages, who may don heavy armor and wield melee weapons along with their spells in combat.<sup>[[29]](#cite_note-ONLOTB-32)</sup><sup>[[285]](#cite_note-303)</sup> Breton spell-knights are known for full plate armor of varying materials, and due to their combat style, their enemies who survive are left scarred from flame and sword.<sup>[[279]](#cite_note-SRSKA-297)</sup><sup>[[286]](#cite_note-COTH-304)</sup> The armor used by the Daggerfall Covenant, notably their helmets and shoulder cops, were influenced primarily by Breton knightly orders.<sup>[[287]](#cite_note-305)</sup>

[![](https://images.uesp.net/thumb/c/c3/ON-concept-IC_Concept_02.jpg/200px-ON-concept-IC_Concept_02.jpg)](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:ON-concept-IC_Concept_02.jpg) [](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:ON-concept-IC_Concept_02.jpg) The Daggerfall Covenant's primarily Breton-Knight and Second Empire influenced armor Druidic armorers, best described as plant-shapers, use their magic to improve their equipment's defensive and offensive traits. Their work is essentially vegetation carved and coaxed into intricate structures with a density nearly that of iron.<sup>[[288]](#cite_note-306)</sup><sup>[[289]](#cite_note-ONYWS-307)</sup> The wood used remains alive, aware, and unharmed. Druids also use leather for their armor, but with a sense of loss and respect for the animal it was harvested from.<sup>[[289]](#cite_note-ONYWS-307)</sup>

[![](https://images.uesp.net/thumb/3/38/ON-misc-Breton_Tattoos.jpg/200px-ON-misc-Breton_Tattoos.jpg)](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:ON-misc-Breton_Tattoos.jpg) [](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:ON-misc-Breton_Tattoos.jpg) Tattoos from various Bretonic subcultures In honor of their patron's sacrifice, its tradition for the Knights of St. Pelin to mix the blood of a new recruit into ink for tattoos featuring sword and wing iconography.<sup>[[290]](#cite_note-308)</sup> The [Glenmoril Wyrd](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Glenmoril_Wyrd) are thought to use [spriggan](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Spriggan) sap in their tattoo ink, so that the wearer may form a more intimate bond with nature.<sup>[[291]](#cite_note-309)</sup> Druidic tattoos, which can be quite colorful, have been made out of mystic ink, and these markings can serve to respect, give in to, or placate nature.<sup>[[292]](#cite_note-310)</sup><sup>[[293]](#cite_note-311)</sup><sup>[[294]](#cite_note-312)</sup><sup>[[295]](#cite_note-313)</sup>

Hair discs have been utilized by Breton nobility.<sup>[[296]](#cite_note-314)</sup> Boarbristle brushes and straight razors are common Breton tools.<sup>[[297]](#cite_note-315)</sup> The "Breton Tonsure" is a hairstyle in which a part of the hair around the scalp is shaved and left bare.<sup>[[298]](#cite_note-316)</sup> "Azure Ombre" is a blue hairstyle created through an alchemical process by the Breton Dabienne Geontene during the Interregnum, whose dyeing methods were also adopted by people of other races.<sup>[[299]](#cite_note-317)</sup> Blue-haired Breton women were still common into the late Third Era.<sup>[[300]](#cite_note-318)</sup> Mariner beard oil is used by Gonfalon Bay sailors to keep their facial hair lustrous.<sup>[[301]](#cite_note-319)</sup> Away from the waves, elaborate up-dos are traditional in Breton high society, with illustrated guides available for brides seeking to marry into Breton families.<sup>[[209]](#cite_note-ONBBBB-225)</sup> Seasalt spray is also used in these elaborate styles.<sup>[[302]](#cite_note-320)</sup> Breton nobles from High Isle use powdered [pearls](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Pearl) as an ingredient for mouthwash and also whiten the teeth.<sup>[[303]](#cite_note-321)</sup> Bretons employ manicure sets complete with nail clippers and more in fanciful shapes.<sup>[[304]](#cite_note-322)</sup>

Bretons utilize a variety of perfumes, colognes, and other scents. Aromatic scents of rain and smoke are popular,<sup>[[305]](#cite_note-323)</sup> and their bedchambers may smell of sweet smelling oil known as "[Mara](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Mara)'s bosom".<sup>[[306]](#cite_note-324)</sup> Some Bretons apply musk of [black bears](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Bear) behind the wrists and ears,<sup>[[307]](#cite_note-325)</sup> and Breton royalty like that of Cumberland employ alchemists to create colognes just for them.<sup>[[308]](#cite_note-326)</sup> Some wealthy Bretons favor "Orc sweat cologne" to "unleash their inner Orc."<sup>[[309]](#cite_note-327)</sup> Not every Breton fragrance is meant to please other Bretons. The sisters of the Glenmoril Wyrd apply an herbal fragrance along their legs, as the guardian wolves who they live alongside seem to enjoy it.<sup>[[310]](#cite_note-328)</sup><sup>[[311]](#cite_note-329)</sup>

- [![](https://images.uesp.net/thumb/8/88/ON-item-armor-Ancestral_Breton.jpg/200px-ON-item-armor-Ancestral_Breton.jpg)](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:ON-item-armor-Ancestral_Breton.jpg) Breton-stylized cloth, leather, and plate armors
- [![](https://images.uesp.net/thumb/d/d5/ON-item-armor-Breton_Armors.jpg/200px-ON-item-armor-Breton_Armors.jpg)](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:ON-item-armor-Breton_Armors.jpg) Various Breton Armors
- [![](https://images.uesp.net/thumb/4/49/ON-item-armor-House_Mornard.jpg/200px-ON-item-armor-House_Mornard.jpg)](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:ON-item-armor-House_Mornard.jpg) House Mornard Style armor
- [![](https://images.uesp.net/thumb/f/fd/SR-item-armor-Spell_Knight_Armor.jpg/200px-SR-item-armor-Spell_Knight_Armor.jpg)](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:SR-item-armor-Spell_Knight_Armor.jpg) Spell Knight Armor
(Left to Right: Iron, Steel, and Ebony)
- [![](https://images.uesp.net/thumb/f/fa/ON-concept-Silver_Rose_Style.jpg/200px-ON-concept-Silver_Rose_Style.jpg)](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:ON-concept-Silver_Rose_Style.jpg) Silver Rose Style, Breton Knightly Order
- [![](https://images.uesp.net/thumb/6/6f/ON-concept-Ascendant_Order_Style.jpg/200px-ON-concept-Ascendant_Order_Style.jpg)](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:ON-concept-Ascendant_Order_Style.jpg) The Breton-influenced rogue knights of the Ascendant Order
- [![](https://images.uesp.net/thumb/2/25/ON-misc-Y%27ffre%27s_Will.jpg/200px-ON-misc-Y%27ffre%27s_Will.jpg)](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:ON-misc-Y%27ffre%27s_Will.jpg) Druidic Robes and Weapons

### Domesticated Animals
Bretons raise a variety of domesticated animals for various purposes. Livestock such as [Cows](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Cow), [Horses](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Horse), [Sheep](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Sheep), [Pigs](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Pig), and pets such as [Dogs](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Dog) and [Cats](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Cat), can be found throughout High Rock.<sup>[[312]](#cite_note-330)</sup>

The Shornhelm Shepherd is a dog bred for sheep herding in Rivenspire's rugged terrain. They are known for their strength, speed, and their fierce loyalty, and they can be used as guard dogs.<sup>[[313]](#cite_note-331)</sup> The Great Daenian Hound are gentle giants bred by the Beldama Wyrd as protectors and companions. They were adopted as trackers by the werewolf-hunting Silver Dawn.<sup>[[314]](#cite_note-332)</sup><sup>[[315]](#cite_note-333)</sup> The Menevian Coachdog is known for its white coat with dark spots. They are perceptive and serve as deterrents to roadside hazards for the carts and coaches they often accompany.<sup>[[316]](#cite_note-334)</sup> The Breton Terrier, originally bred to kill rats around the Iliac Bay's docks, is known for its joyful disposition.<sup>[[317]](#cite_note-335)</sup> The Glenumbra Border Wolf resembles Breton dog breeds in coloration, and has been bred as a mount to carry couriers though harsh weather and the dark of night.<sup>[[318]](#cite_note-336)</sup>

Wealthy Bretons often let Piebald Cats wander the hidden passages of their manor homes. This tradition arose thanks to infestations of Sheogorath's never-there beetles, which the cats eventually purged.<sup>[[319]](#cite_note-337)</sup> The Indigo Senche-Panther, a [Senche](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Senche-Cat) originally bred to be mounts by a reclusive family in Rivenspire, is said to hunt werewolves for amusement.<sup>[[320]](#cite_note-338)</sup> The Senche-Serval mounts originating from the Summerset Isles<sup>[[321]](#cite_note-339)</sup> have also seen some use in High Rock and the Systres. The Ashgray Senche-Serval breed, once only possessed by nobles of House Mornard, became a more common mount throughout Tamriel after the house fell on hard times.<sup>[[322]](#cite_note-340)</sup> The [Knights of the Silver Rose](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Knights_of_the_Silver_Rose) utilized Senche-Servals to rid their fortress of pests and other troubles.<sup>[[323]](#cite_note-341)</sup>

The Evermore Painter's Moth, local to the eponymous city, is a moth whose natural pigments are utilized by artists for their paintings, a notable example being the portrait of Duke Blaise Guimard. Artists have domesticated and have even raised sanctuaries for these insects.<sup>[[324]](#cite_note-342)</sup> The ravens of Rivenspire, some of the smartest of Tamriel, have often served as companions.<sup>[[325]](#cite_note-343)</sup> The blue cockerals of Alcaire are known for their "noble duty" of screeching at daybreak which continues throughout the morning.<sup>[[326]](#cite_note-344)</sup> Two [Chub Loon](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Chub_Loon) breeds are kept for companionship in the Systres. The Hay-Crown breed are seen as omens of good harvests, and they were originally from Rivenspire where they were rendered extinct, but those that were taken to [High Isle](Lore_High_Isle.md) survived.<sup>[[327]](#cite_note-345)</sup> The Fellbraun Chub Loon is native to the island of Galen, and are seen as a blessing from Y'ffre.<sup>[[328]](#cite_note-346)</sup>

The Bretons are known to keep a variety of mounts. They are integral to the way of life of the Bjoulsae River Tribes, and the power and splendor of Breton mounted knights has been proven in battle.<sup>[[329]](#cite_note-ONWKC-347)</sup> The Daggerfall Dapple Horse, favored by long distance riders, comes from the Farwatch region in Glenumbra.<sup>[[330]](#cite_note-348)</sup> The Coalsmoke Forge Horse was bred by Breton blacksmiths for the strength to work long hours.<sup>[[331]](#cite_note-349)</sup> In the King's Guard region of Glenumbra, the superstitious believe species of ram bred as steeds bring good luck.<sup>[[332]](#cite_note-350)</sup> Over in the Systres, the [Oaken Order](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Oaken_Order) tamed green-hued mountain goats as mounts and companions.<sup>[[333]](#cite_note-351)</sup> Originally a Direnni creation,<sup>[[334]](#cite_note-352)</sup> [Quasigriffs](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Quasigriff) are cousins to [Gryphons](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Gryphon), and those of the Baysong breed are a colorful and flightless creatures adored by noble riders in the Systres.<sup>[[335]](#cite_note-353)</sup>

- [![](https://images.uesp.net/thumb/d/d0/ON-misc-Breton_Dogs.jpg/200px-ON-misc-Breton_Dogs.jpg)](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:ON-misc-Breton_Dogs.jpg) Breton Terrier, Menevian Coachdog, Shornhelm Sheperd, and Great Daenian Hound pets
- [![](https://images.uesp.net/thumb/a/ac/ON-misc-Breton_Cats.jpg/200px-ON-misc-Breton_Cats.jpg)](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:ON-misc-Breton_Cats.jpg) Piebald Cat, Indigo Senche-Panther, Ashgray Senche-Serval, and Silver Rose Senche-Serval felines
- [![](https://images.uesp.net/thumb/1/1c/ON-misc-Breton_Pets.jpg/200px-ON-misc-Breton_Pets.jpg)](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:ON-misc-Breton_Pets.jpg) Evermore Painter's Moth, Eyebright Raven, Alcaire Blue Cockeral, and Fellbraun Chub Loon pets
- [![](https://images.uesp.net/thumb/5/5d/ON-misc-Breton_Mounts.jpg/200px-ON-misc-Breton_Mounts.jpg)](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:ON-misc-Breton_Mounts.jpg) Daggerfall Dapple Horse, King's Guard Ram, Glenumbra Border Wolf, and Baysong Quasigriff mounts

### Maritime and Mercantile Industry
Bretons have a thriving and often intrepid merchant class that intersects with maritime activities.<sup>[[1]](#cite_note-TBMOP-1)</sup> "Merchant princes",<sup>[[336]](#cite_note-NAA-354)</sup> "warrior-merchants",<sup>[[39]](#cite_note-TIEGTT-42)</sup> and "merchant knights"<sup>[[42]](#cite_note-ONTKOHR-45)</sup> are some societal archetypes, and Bretons that are encountered outside High Rock are often merchants or mercenaries.<sup>[[12]](#cite_note-Adventure Game-14)</sup> Indeed, Bretons are often described as shrewd merchants, and as a race they are said to value prosperity over glory.<sup>[[15]](#cite_note-TCCAG-17)</sup> *The Improved Emperor's Guide to Tamriel* stereotypes Bretons as worshipping money over the Divines.<sup>[[39]](#cite_note-TIEGTT-42)</sup> Sometimes Breton's merchant-oriented side of society manifests in a darker way via illicit activities. Breton lackeys and merchant lords have been involved in cartels, [drugs](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Drugs), piracy, or at times even slavery.<sup>[[337]](#cite_note-ALML-355)</sup> High Rock's Coin-barons participated in slavery and other illicit practices during the First Era.<sup>[[UOL 9]](#cite_note-HIDD-152)</sup><sup>[[144]](#cite_note-ESOEHI-153)</sup>

[![](https://images.uesp.net/thumb/f/fd/ON-concept-High_Isle_Shipbuilders.jpg/500px-ON-concept-High_Isle_Shipbuilders.jpg)](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:ON-concept-High_Isle_Shipbuilders.jpg) [](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:ON-concept-High_Isle_Shipbuilders.jpg) Breton shipbuilders Some of the earliest known Breton-made vessels are contained in the oral histories of the druids. It is said that Y'ffre taught the last Druid King how to sing seaworthy vessels into existence, and he in turn taught the druids to do the same. The plants and trees of High Rock are said to had been altered to the exact specifications needed to be used as materials for this endeavor.<sup>[[59]](#cite_note-EOTD-63)</sup> Similarly, scholars theorize that the trees of the Systres island of High Isle were also influenced by the druids to be well suited for shipbuilding.<sup>[[338]](#cite_note-ONAHSB-356)</sup>

By the mid-Second Era, Bretons dominated in the naval shipbuilding industry, centering most operations along their prime trade routes. In the Systres Archipelago, the Bretons of House Dufort became perhaps the premier shipbuilders of Tamriel. Vessels from Dufort Shipyards, which entered every navy, were ranked among the finest. Due to "integrated business concerns", they shared a mutual reliance with their rivals House Mornard, as Dufort vessels transported and protected a great deal of Mornard trade goods.<sup>[[338]](#cite_note-ONAHSB-356)</sup><sup>[[339]](#cite_note-Dufort-357)</sup>

The Bretons of High Rock primarily utilize the waters of the Iliac Bay, the Eltheric Ocean,<sup>[[340]](#cite_note-GP-358)</sup> and the Bjoulsae River for trade. Strategic and economic concerns have led to a great deal of naval warfare over the years.<sup>[[114]](#cite_note-PGE1WR-121)</sup> The Masconian Trade Way was created as an anti-piracy measure.<sup>[[94]](#cite_note-WJOTB-100)</sup><sup>[[39]](#cite_note-TIEGTT-42)</sup> Not even the Bjoulsae River is safe, as its small islands often serve as bases for sea raiders.<sup>[[341]](#cite_note-Load-359)</sup> One notorious island was known as [Blackheart Haven](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Blackheart_Haven), after a pirate captain that secured a fearsome reputation among the locals.<sup>[[342]](#cite_note-Redbeard-360)</sup><sup>[[341]](#cite_note-Load-359)</sup>

A typical Breton merchant ship is a large wooden vessel rigged with square sails. These ships have also been utilized to carry troops.<sup>[[39]](#cite_note-TIEGTT-42)</sup> Systrean caravals have been seen in ports as far as [Solstice](Lore_Solstice_(island).md).<sup>[[343]](#cite_note-361)</sup> Warrior-sailors from High Isle often take on posts on escort ships to hone their martial prowess on the seas.<sup>[[344]](#cite_note-362)</sup> During the Second Era, Breton ship architect Jeromec Lemal sought to revolutionize naval warfare by including thicker masts, extra backstays, a narrower keel, lighter ballastas, reinforced hulls, and other improvements.<sup>[[345]](#cite_note-363)</sup>

The Bretons of the Systres Archipelago export many raw materials and trade goods.<sup>[[346]](#cite_note-Mot EA-364)</sup> Primary industries include logging, mining, and shipbuilding.<sup>[[143]](#cite_note-ONSHV6-151)</sup> An especially important commodity is [Eltheric Ammonite](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Eltheric_Ammonite), which washes up in the archipelago's shore. Collectors covet their beauty, while mages find them attractive as a perhaps more ethical raw source of magicka than [soul gems](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Soul_Gems).<sup>[[346]](#cite_note-Mot EA-364)</sup> [Larimar](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Larimar) is another important trade good, a milky-blue gemstone exclusive to the Systres, making it extremely rare and expensive.<sup>[[238]](#cite_note-OSRCodex-254)</sup><sup>[[143]](#cite_note-ONSHV6-151)</sup> Though it has become a highly coveted rarity over time,<sup>[[143]](#cite_note-ONSHV6-151)</sup> shipments of [Frog-Metal](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Frog-Metal) from the Systres isle of Amenos are still exported.<sup>[[347]](#cite_note-365)</sup> Druid-crafted volcanic jewelry has also been exported.<sup>[[238]](#cite_note-OSRCodex-254)</sup>

The biggest source of [Orichalcum](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Orichalcum) in history was found near Wayrest circa [2E 561](Lore_Second_Era.md#2E_561), which improved trade throughout High Rock.<sup>[[155]](#cite_note-Gtt DC-164)</sup><sup>[[348]](#cite_note-Toa M10-366)</sup> Feathers belonging to [Harpies](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Harpy), such as those from the Shrieking Scar in the Daggerfall highlands, are valued for use in quality calligraphy sets and kites.<sup>[[39]](#cite_note-TIEGTT-42)</sup><sup>[[349]](#cite_note-367)</sup> Earthenware is a common form of pottery in High Rock, and is used for goods such as chamber pots.<sup>[[350]](#cite_note-368)</sup> Bretons engage in a great deal of interprovincial trade. Under the Daggerfall Covenant, goods of Hammerfell reached a broader market in High Rock, including luxuries such as tapestries, embroidered throw pillows, and delicious pomegranate wine. As a downside, trade became restricted and less frequent with eastern Skyrim, which joined the enemy Ebonheart Pact, and some dependent on Nordic trade went out of business.<sup>[[351]](#cite_note-369)</sup> The Bretons of High Isle, though, greatly profited due to their neutrality in the conflict.<sup>[[4]](#cite_note-ONHIPTZ-4)</sup>

- [![](https://images.uesp.net/thumb/c/c6/ON-place-Dufort_Shipyards.jpg/200px-ON-place-Dufort_Shipyards.jpg)](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:ON-place-Dufort_Shipyards.jpg) House Dufort Shipyards
- [![](https://images.uesp.net/thumb/8/8f/ON-place-The_Fair_Winds.jpg/200px-ON-place-The_Fair_Winds.jpg)](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:ON-place-The_Fair_Winds.jpg) Systrean galleon exterior
- [![](https://images.uesp.net/thumb/4/47/ON-load-The_Fair_Winds.png/200px-ON-load-The_Fair_Winds.png)](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:ON-load-The_Fair_Winds.png) Systrean galleon interior
- [![](https://images.uesp.net/thumb/b/bd/ON-concept-Large_Ship.png/190px-ON-concept-Large_Ship.png)](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:ON-concept-Large_Ship.png) A square-rigged merchant ship
- [![](https://images.uesp.net/thumb/5/55/LG-cardart-Iliac_Sorcerer.png/200px-LG-cardart-Iliac_Sorcerer.png)](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:LG-cardart-Iliac_Sorcerer.png) A Breton sorcerer on a ship with cannons

### Recreation: Art, Sports, etc.
[![](https://images.uesp.net/thumb/c/ca/ON-crown_store-Key_Harp.jpg/200px-ON-crown_store-Key_Harp.jpg)](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:ON-crown_store-Key_Harp.jpg) [](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:ON-crown_store-Key_Harp.jpg) The Key Harp, favored in High Isle Bretons have a variety of recreational activities. Bardic traditions serve as a unifying legacy for the Bretons,<sup>[[38]](#cite_note-POT-41)</sup> with examples including works such as "The Gonfalon Maid" celebrating love, "Blessings of Y'ffre" for the eponymous god,<sup>[[352]](#cite_note-370)</sup> or "The Battle of Glenumbria Moors" for the historical and pivotal victory.<sup>[[97]](#cite_note-TBo GM-103)</sup> [Kieran the Bard](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Kieran), a noted literary figure, inspired shrines called Kieran Theatres throughout the Iliac Bay,<sup>[[353]](#cite_note-DFShrines-371)</sup> while the bard and poet [Darius Shano](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Darius_Shano) serves as a reminder to not deal with daedra.<sup>[[202]](#cite_note-16AOM9-217)</sup> Named the Poet-Champion by Potentate Savirien-Chorak, [Nynelle Dumaris](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Nynelle_Dumaris) rose to prominence with her famous sonnets *[A Lissome Sprite](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:A_Lissome_Sprite)* and *[Fearless as the Sun](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Fearless_as_the_Sun)* following her victory in a poetry tournament in the Imperial City in [2E 400](Lore_Second_Era.md#2E_400).<sup>[[354]](#cite_note-TPCOV-372)</sup><sup>[[355]](#cite_note-ALS-373)</sup><sup>[[356]](#cite_note-FATS-374)</sup> A painting called "Frolicking Trolls of [Eastmarch](Lore_Eastmarch.md)", which depicts smiling frost trolls dancing in the snow, is said to be how a Breton imagines the [frost trolls](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Frost_Troll) of Skyrim.<sup>[[357]](#cite_note-375)</sup>

Bretons play a variety of musical instruments. Lutes and drums are standard,<sup>[[358]](#cite_note-376)</sup> but they also play a variant of a lyre known as a talharpa,<sup>[[359]](#cite_note-377)</sup> and bugles often sound during war campaigns.<sup>[[360]](#cite_note-378)</sup> They have bellowing instruments known as concertinas,<sup>[[361]](#cite_note-379)</sup> while key harps are the favored instrument in High Isle.<sup>[[362]](#cite_note-380)</sup> Bagpipes in Galen were made from a [hoarvor](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Hoarvor)'s bloat-sac and proboscis, often adorned with [parrot](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Parrot) feathers.<sup>[[363]](#cite_note-TIGalen-381)</sup> Druids purportedly began using pan flutes after a group of [Fauns](Lore_Faun.md) proffered how to make them.<sup>[[364]](#cite_note-382)</sup> The Stonelore druids are known to wear a bracelet of bells during their ritual dances around fires.<sup>[[365]](#cite_note-383)</sup>

Bretons have a multitude of recreational activities, including a sport called "Bretonball", which is played with rackets.<sup>[[366]](#cite_note-384)</sup> Racing rowboats is a centuries old pasttime centered around the Bjoulsae River.<sup>[[367]](#cite_note-385)</sup> Shuttlecocks, traditionally used as a lure in falconry, were repurposed into a sport involving making it fly with wooden paddles.<sup>[[368]](#cite_note-386)</sup> Triangle Chess involves a three-sided board.<sup>[[369]](#cite_note-387)</sup> Khimera, themed around the Chimeras of legend, is a traditional Breton yard game played by children.<sup>[[45]](#cite_note-TBOG-48)</sup> The denizens of High Isle enjoy "Proof", a murder mystery role-playing card game based on the *[Investigator Vale](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Investigator_Vale)* book series.<sup>[[370]](#cite_note-388)</sup>

## Society

### Politics
*"You think politics here are something? Well, we Bretons invented politics."* — *Anton Virane*<sup>[[11]](#cite_note-SRAV-13)</sup> [![](https://images.uesp.net/thumb/9/99/ON-render-ESO_Tavern_Event_Announcement.jpg/200px-ON-render-ESO_Tavern_Event_Announcement.jpg)](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:ON-render-ESO_Tavern_Event_Announcement.jpg) [](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:ON-render-ESO_Tavern_Event_Announcement.jpg) Breton nobles at a social gathering High Rock is segmented into city-states, encouraging petty nationalism and infighting between the kingdoms. Most Breton cities are sprawling trade hubs with highly developed social strata. The poor peasantry lies at the bottom of the hierarchy, above them is a middle class of mostly merchants and artisans, and noble ruling families sit at the top. Additionally, there are the many autonomous knightly orders, as well as a small haughty magical elite.<sup>[[39]](#cite_note-TIEGTT-42)</sup> The jockeying for power among the various powers of the Iliac Bay region is a deeply ingrained and even cherished part of Breton culture.<sup>[[37]](#cite_note-PGE1High-40)</sup> Breton society is fractious and quarrelsome, but internal conflict seems to disappear when their way of life is threatened by outside forces.<sup>[[39]](#cite_note-TIEGTT-42)</sup>

Bretons' largely agrarian and feudal society, as well as their obsession with nobility, status, and lineage, was shaped by their days as vassals of Clan Direnni.<sup>[[13]](#cite_note-ONBS-15)</sup><sup>[[1]](#cite_note-TBMOP-1)</sup><sup>[[7]](#cite_note-MDBMM-7)</sup> Bretons borrowed and modified their elven ancestor's feudal system to suit their needs, removing the aspect that forced people to stay in the same social class for their rest of their lives.<sup>[[7]](#cite_note-MDBMM-7)</sup><sup>[[UOL 16]](#cite_note-ONHCP-219)</sup> Indeed, their outlook is shaped from breaking free from their elven masters and taking High Rock for themselves. Thus Bretons live lives of excess and believe in upwards mobility to the extent that even those at the very bottom of the social ladder feel like they can always aspire to become better and advance to the top of the social ladder.<sup>[[UOL 16]](#cite_note-ONHCP-219)</sup> Despite this, there is still however a sense of elitism and otherism in Breton society. Some nobles may look down at common folk as inferior to them.<sup>[[371]](#cite_note-ONAV-389)</sup><sup>[[372]](#cite_note-390)</sup>

Though Bretons of lower status have several paths to prosperity, becoming a nobleman by performing quests and services to curry favor with various rulers is considered the best way, which has created a cultural "quest obsession" among young Bretons.<sup>[[37]](#cite_note-PGE1High-40)</sup><sup>[[373]](#cite_note-FAOT-391)</sup> The desire to find some great opportunity for fortune and glory has made Bretons venture all over Tamriel, even to such remote locations as [Thirsk](Lore_Thirsk.md) on the island of [Solstheim](Lore_Solstheim.md), where one adventurous Breton once earned the position of chieftain.<sup>[[87]](#cite_note-PGE1S-93)</sup><sup>[[374]](#cite_note-TCATD-392)</sup><sup>[[375]](#cite_note-TAHR-393)</sup>

[![](https://images.uesp.net/thumb/e/ef/LO-misc-Daggerfall_Noble.jpg/130px-LO-misc-Daggerfall_Noble.jpg)](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:LO-misc-Daggerfall_Noble.jpg) [](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:LO-misc-Daggerfall_Noble.jpg) A noble from Daggerfall
### Peerage
*"Find a new hill, become a king"* — *Breton Proverb*<sup>[[37]](#cite_note-PGE1High-40)</sup> [![](https://images.uesp.net/thumb/c/c1/LG-cardart-High_King_Emeric.jpg/200px-LG-cardart-High_King_Emeric.jpg)](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:LG-cardart-High_King_Emeric.jpg) [](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:LG-cardart-High_King_Emeric.jpg) High King Emeric Cumberland, leader of the Daggerfall Covenant Across High Rock, traditions of the peerage differ slightly from region to region. The base rule of the eight kingdoms is that if a woman is ruling one of these areas, she is called the Queen. The husband of a Queen and the wife of a King is not necessarily of equal rank – they may not be Kings and Queens themselves. Their children are Princes and Princesses. Their grandchildren are also Princes and Princesses. If a male ruler dies, his wife takes the title Dowager Queen, providing there is not a Dowager Queen already. In the Kingdom of Daggerfall, it is permissible for there to be two persons with the same title. If a female ruler, who does not share rank with her husband, dies, there is no male equivalent to the word Dowager. Widowers of Queens usually take another title, either a lesser family title or one given by their children. There have been few men in the history of High Rock who have fallen from being addressed as King to being addressed as Mister at the death of their wife.<sup>[[180]](#cite_note-EWR-194)</sup>

Other regions in High Rock are ruled by Dukes and Duchesses, Marquises (or Marquesses) and Marquises (or Marchionesses), Counts and Countesses, Viscounts or Viscountesses, Barons or Baronesses, and Lords or Ladies. This is theoretically listed from highest to lowest rank, but the ruler of a territory outranks all other nobles, regardless of title.

Counts usually enjoy less autonomy than dukes and duchesses, as their territories are subservient to the duchies they are part of. However, they serve as vital links to guilds, churches, and scholastic organizations that might otherwise receive less attention from the duchy's rulers. Beneath counts and countesses, peerage hierarchy flattens considerably. Barons and baronesses stand above most, but these titles rarely carry robust land rights. Instead, they serve as titles of honor, granting the noble certain privileges at court. Dignitaries should address barons and baronesses as "my lord" and "my lady" respectively.<sup>[[376]](#cite_note-NRAT-394)</sup>

Dwynnen, for example, is a Barony, and the Baron or Baroness of Dwynnen outrank any other noble in that territory, even Dukes and Counts. In theory, (again, this may not be the case according to local custom) the eldest son or daughter of a noble takes their parent's highest family title below their parents. Thus, the Duke of Northmoor, who is also the Marquis of Calder, had a daughter who became the Marchioness of Calder.<sup>[[180]](#cite_note-EWR-194)</sup>

Kings and Queens are always addressed as "Your Majesty" in conversation; Dukes and Duchesses, "Your Grace". All other rulers may be addressed with their title and name, or Lord or Lady and their name.<sup>[[180]](#cite_note-EWR-194)</sup>

One way of telling who is in charge of a region is to pay some attention to the names of taverns and shops in a region. By tradition, many of these are called names such as "The Duke's Fox" or "The Lady's Provisions." This, more often than not, is the title of the ruler. If the shop's name is, for example, "Lady Annisa's Provisions" or "Lord Boxworth's Fox", that is probably the name of a local titled merchant, not the ruler. A store with an unnamed ruler's title has probably been around for some time, and does not bother to change its name with the new name of the ruler.<sup>[[180]](#cite_note-EWR-194)</sup>

Emeric of Cumberland, as a result of being the architect of the Daggerfall Covenant, became High King and the first to ever claim supreme leadership over all High Rock. All the city-states of northwest Tamriel swore loyalty to the Covenant's Royal Council.<sup>[[155]](#cite_note-Gtt DC-164)</sup> The various monarchs of High Rock were bound to him via trade agreements,<sup>[[39]](#cite_note-TIEGTT-42)</sup> which included "dozens of compromises and carefully negotiated provisions".<sup>[[155]](#cite_note-Gtt DC-164)</sup>

The following is a list of Breton Noble Houses or families whose names are known. Others exist, but have not been named and are therefore not included in the list.
