### The Role of Magic among Bretons
[![](https://images.uesp.net/thumb/b/b2/LG-cardart-Lion_Guard_Strategist.png/200px-LG-cardart-Lion_Guard_Strategist.png)](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:LG-cardart-Lion_Guard_Strategist.png) [](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:LG-cardart-Lion_Guard_Strategist.png) Breton Spell-Knights [![](https://images.uesp.net/thumb/9/92/LO-misc-Breton.jpg/200px-LO-misc-Breton.jpg)](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:LO-misc-Breton.jpg) [](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:LO-misc-Breton.jpg) Breton mage that dabbled in the dark arts *You Bretons have a reputation for mystical aptitude, but I would argue that the cost of that success has been a lack of lasting impact on the greater magical community. I could find numerous instances of Mage So-And-So making a splash with war magics for a few decades, and then dying. Or a great divinator prognosticating portentous events, and then dying. Breton mages burn brightly but briefly, I suppose, a sad commentary on the lifespan your uncaring gods have gifted your people.*
—Divayth Fyr<sup>[[25]](#cite_note-LAHT-27)</sup> Bretons are known to be inventive wizards.<sup>[[15]](#cite_note-TCCAG-17)</sup> Magic permeates throughout all of Breton society, from the serf all the way up to the king.<sup>[[UOL 3]](#cite_note-ESOLI-30)</sup> Though no two mages weave their spells in exactly the same way,<sup>[[377]](#cite_note-395)</sup> the average Breton mage is said to perform "flamboyant gesticulations" when spellcasting.<sup>[[378]](#cite_note-WAS-396)</sup> Some Bretons are born with innate gifts for unique kinds of magic, such as [thaumavocalism](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Thaumavocalism).<sup>[[379]](#cite_note-MBFP-397)</sup> Due to the innate magical ability of Bretons, children are tested for their magical potential at an early age, and those who pass enter apprenticeship programs funded by the Mages Guild or independent sponsorships.<sup>[[37]](#cite_note-PGE1High-40)</sup> Children are known to practice illusion spells on each other in the streets of cities such as Daggerfall.<sup>[[380]](#cite_note-398)</sup> In more remote regions, such as Glenpoint and the Wrothgarian Mountains, witches and medicine men, barely distinguishable from Orcish shamans, hold sway over the superstitious peasants with feats of untutored, but often impressive, magical ability.<sup>[[37]](#cite_note-PGE1High-40)</sup> Many use their magical talents to earn success,<sup>[[37]](#cite_note-PGE1High-40)</sup> such as undertaking an ancient traditional role of a court mage.<sup>[[35]](#cite_note-ONCDD-38)</sup> Not much is known about the magical elite that sit right below the ruling families in the social hierarchy, but these gifted see themselves as above the rest.<sup>[[37]](#cite_note-PGE1High-40)</sup><sup>[[39]](#cite_note-TIEGTT-42)</sup><sup>[[38]](#cite_note-POT-41)</sup>

## Subcultures
Breton culture, despite its seeming homogeneity, has many subcultures throughout the regions of High Rock. Many clans inhabit regions such as Greater Bretony, the [Dellese Isles](Lore_Dellese_Isles.md), the Bjoulsae River Tribes, and traditionally the [Western Reach](Lore_Western_Reach.md). They are, in fact, so culturally diverse that some have regarded "Breton" as a term of convenience.<sup>[[37]](#cite_note-PGE1High-40)</sup><sup>[[38]](#cite_note-POT-41)</sup>

### Bjoulsae River Tribes
[![](https://images.uesp.net/thumb/6/6a/LO-misc-Bjoulsae_River_Tribes_02.jpg/200px-LO-misc-Bjoulsae_River_Tribes_02.jpg)](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:LO-misc-Bjoulsae_River_Tribes_02.jpg) [](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:LO-misc-Bjoulsae_River_Tribes_02.jpg) Members of the Bjoulsae River Tribes → *For more detailed information, see: [Bjoulsae River Tribes](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Bjoulsae_River_Tribes)* The [Bjoulsae River Tribes](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Bjoulsae_River_Tribes) (also known as the **Horse-People of the Bjoulsae River**, the **River Horse Bretons**, or simply the **horsemen**) are the indigenous groups of tribal Bretons that live in the [Bjoulsae River](Lore_Bjoulsae_River.md) region. While information on them is scarce, the horsemen are a nomadic, primitive folk that wear fur armor, bone necklaces, and turbans. As the name suggests, they are known for their [horses](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Horse). Their battle strategies and tactics are described as straightforward, which is the "way of the horse men", in the book *[The Mirror](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:The_Mirror)*. Their greatest legacy is the modern-day Kingdom of Evermore, which was founded in [1E 983](Lore_First_Era.md#1E_983) after they helped suppress Orsinium, which opened trade through the Bjoulsae River region. Additionally, the Bjoulsaer folk are directly attributed to one of the two scholastically prominent creation myths associated with Bretons.<sup>[[TRL 1]](#cite_note-TMF-399)</sup>

### Druids
→ *For more detailed information, see: [Druids](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Druids)* [![](https://images.uesp.net/thumb/e/e3/ON-misc-Druid_Laurel.jpg/200px-ON-misc-Druid_Laurel.jpg)](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:ON-misc-Druid_Laurel.jpg) [](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:ON-misc-Druid_Laurel.jpg) Druids of the Stonelore Circle [Druids](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Druids) (also known as **vinebeards**) are children of the land whose kind have their origins in ancient [High Rock](Lore_High_Rock.md). They are practitioners of [Y'ffre](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Y%27ffre)'s True Way (also known as Druidism), in which one is to lead a life connecting with, valuing, and stewarding the growth of the natural world referred to as [the Green](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:The_Green). The eponymous god takes the forefront of their faith, with some reverence also being shown to the stars. The True Way is a promise made to the "groves, to the seas, to the sky", and under the Oak's Promise, druids are to "stand strong, stay true, and shelter all". Druids serve in accordance to Y'ffre's will in roles such as priests, arbiters, teachers, healers, and [soothsayers](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Sight). Druids have little interest in the quarrels of monarchies, often leading many to believe that they are pacifists. However, as champions of nature, they are not afraid to defend their ancient sites from the cruelty of civilization, as violence and death are natural.

Y'ffre and his [Earthbones](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Earthbones) sacrificed themselves during the [Dawn Era](Lore_Dawn_Era.md) to create the Green, an act which bound [Nirn](Lore_Nirn.md) to the laws of nature. Their voices are sought by druids so they may best be their advocate, and to ensure a life guided by natural principles and the willfulness of nature. Druidic spellcraft (which differs from the arcane) is said to be the first truly Breton creation, and its practitioners utilize the wellspring of primordial energy the Earthbones left behind, which flows via lines through the ground. Junctions where this resource intersects are known as "[bonelines](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Bonelines)", places where druidic spells exhibit strange properties, and where prayers carry deeper emphasis. It can be harnessed by druids to overcome their physical limitations, shapeshift into various animals, terraform the environment around them, or even invoke natural disasters to consume their foes. Druids are also known animists who can call upon [nature spirits](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Nature_Spirits) to aid them.

### Dellese
The [Dellese Isles](Lore_Dellese_Isles.md) are commonly cited among the most culturally relevant regions when describing the Bretons of High Rock.<sup>[[37]](#cite_note-PGE1High-40)</sup><sup>[[38]](#cite_note-POT-41)</sup><sup>[[381]](#cite_note-Morrowind Dialogue-400)</sup> Additionally, the Dellese are directly attributed to one of the two scholastically prominent creation myths associated with Bretons.<sup>[[TRL 1]](#cite_note-TMF-399)</sup>

### Glenumbrans
[![](https://images.uesp.net/thumb/7/74/ON-crown_store-Camlorn_Top_Hat_Pack.jpg/200px-ON-crown_store-Camlorn_Top_Hat_Pack.jpg)](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:ON-crown_store-Camlorn_Top_Hat_Pack.jpg) [](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:ON-crown_store-Camlorn_Top_Hat_Pack.jpg) Camlorn Top Hats In the mid-Second Era, the region of Glenumbra included Daenia, [King's Guard](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:King%27s_Guard) and the [Cambray Hills](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Cambray_Hills), each distinguishable by many unique elements. In southern Glenumbra, Daenia is the home of the Bretons' quest obsession: the practice by which young serfs or peasants perform great deeds to elevate their societal standing. Daenian tales commonly include lowly individuals going on great quests to attain respect, glory and status. Consequently, the people of Daenia have reputations as independent spirits. Daenia is also home to the Wyrd subculture, and nature-worshipping witches reside in the region's dense forests.<sup>[[340]](#cite_note-GP-358)</sup>

Glenumbra's Cambray Hills, most prominent in Camlorn, has been a melting pot with an aristocracy described as poets and artists.<sup>[[340]](#cite_note-GP-358)</sup> The region lends its name to the famed Cambray Hills Academy of Art.<sup>[[382]](#cite_note-401)</sup> The Cambray Hills are haunted, and ghost stories abound among the populace. Camlorn has served as an open market for goods coming in from the Iliac Bay and the waters west of High Rock, dealing peacefully with Daggerfall and Wayrest to its benefit. The swamp-dwellers of the eastern bogs are the Cambray Hills' largest subculture.<sup>[[340]](#cite_note-GP-358)</sup> Though apparently originally founded during the First Era,<sup>[[195]](#cite_note-2920FS-210)</sup> the modern iteration of the Barony of Dwynnen would be founded by the legendary [Baron Othrok](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Othrok) in [3E 253](Lore_Third_Era.md#3E_253) after the Battle of Wightmoor. It would go on to become cultural center of the region in the Third Era.<sup>[[181]](#cite_note-TFOTU-195)</sup>

The northermost reaches of Glenumbra became known as King's Guard, after the mountain range separating Glenumbra from Rivenspire and Stormhaven. Crosswych is the center of trade between Glenumbra and its neighboring regions, and another cultural melting pot of Bretonic city-states. The Red Rook bandit clan originated in King's Guard as a loose group of hunters and highwaymen that targeted caravans traveling across regional borders.<sup>[[340]](#cite_note-GP-358)</sup> Kambria is another notable city in this region, renowned for its picturesque nature and many libraries. Kambria rules over the windswept plateau in the north, which is still dotted with the fortresses that were ruined during the Tiber War.<sup>[[37]](#cite_note-PGE1High-40)</sup><sup>[[181]](#cite_note-TFOTU-195)</sup><sup>[[255]](#cite_note-CKL1-272)</sup>

### Highland Bretons
[![](https://images.uesp.net/thumb/5/57/MW-item-Claymores.jpg/200px-MW-item-Claymores.jpg)](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:MW-item-Claymores.jpg) [](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:MW-item-Claymores.jpg) Claymores (Morrowind) → *For more detailed information, see: [Highland Bretons](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Highland_Bretons)* The [Highland Bretons](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Highland_Bretons) are a Breton culture believed to inhabit highland strongholds, and renowned for the invention and usage of claymore. They were pioneers in employing these formidable two-handed swords. However, the [Redguards](Lore_Redguard.md) later would quickly incorporate these massive shock [weapons](Lore_Weapons.md) into their valiant melee tactics. Designed for use by solitary hero-adventurers rather than close-order troops, their claymores were favored in encounters with formidable beasts and otherworldly creatures.

There are a number of highland areas in High Rock, typically composed of woodland hills. The windswept plateau of North [Kambria](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Kambria) has many grim fortifications and small towns tucked into the folds and valleys that wind their way down to the northern coast. Remote highland regions include the [Glenpoint](Lore_Glenpoint.md) Foothills and the Dragon's Toe of the [Wrothgarian Mountains](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Wrothgarian_Mountains), near the border with [Hammerfell](Lore_Hammerfell.md). Witches and medicine men, barely distinguishable from [Orcish](Lore_Orc.md) shamans, hold sway over the superstitious peasants of these highlands with feats of untutored, but often impressive, magical ability. [Jehanna](Lore_Jehanna.md) is also found near a highland area of the province.

### Hillmen of Rivenspire
[![](https://images.uesp.net/thumb/5/59/ON-place-Rivenspire.jpg/200px-ON-place-Rivenspire.jpg)](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:ON-place-Rivenspire.jpg) [](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:ON-place-Rivenspire.jpg) Rivenspire shapes its people The [hillmen](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Hillmen) are the people of Rivenspire,<sup>[[154]](#cite_note-TFo KR-163)</sup><sup>[[nb 3]](#intnote_Hill_Giants)</sup> known as the backwater of High Rock.<sup>[[154]](#cite_note-TFo KR-163)</sup> The region's people are shaped by its tortured landscape.<sup>[[39]](#cite_note-TIEGTT-42)</sup> They've been described as "surly",<sup>[[154]](#cite_note-TFo KR-163)</sup> "gloomy", "laconic", and having "little to say to strangers".<sup>[[39]](#cite_note-TIEGTT-42)</sup> They are also known for their "overactive imaginations".<sup>[[56]](#cite_note-ONBF-59)</sup> Hillmen hunters can make a decent living off of the pelts of wolves and giant bats, as well as from spider venom, but must be wary of Rivenspire's many hostile creatures.<sup>[[383]](#cite_note-402)</sup> Restless spirits are known to haunt the region's forts,<sup>[[384]](#cite_note-ONOT-403)</sup> and rumors exist of "evil fog" where the souls of fallen sailors stir off the coast.<sup>[[385]](#cite_note-404)</sup>

Rivenspire's dark history has haunted the region's people.<sup>[[384]](#cite_note-ONOT-403)</sup> A number of atrocities and despots have made their mark, such as the violence against the Direnni under the orders of King Festrien Spenard I,<sup>[[101]](#cite_note-ROTPO-108)</sup> and the Purge of the Wyrd-Hags during [Sun's Death](Lore_Sun%27s_Death.md) under King Berthulic.<sup>[[386]](#cite_note-405)</sup><sup>[[387]](#cite_note-SCCOTN-406)</sup> Fighting broke out between the natives and Ayleids who migrated to the region, resulting in incalculable damage. These elves had attempted to transform what they called the "Land of Cold Rocks"<sup>[[388]](#cite_note-ROL-407)</sup> into a region full of life, but their method for doing so, the Light of Life was damaged in the conflict. It became the Lightless Remnant, a corrupting influence on Rivenspire. This influence was further amplified when it was touched by [vampires](Lore_Vampire.md) during the Second Era,<sup>[[389]](#cite_note-Wynaldia-408)</sup> leading to a vampire crisis perpetuated by one of Rivenspire's noble houses, the [Montclairs](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:House_Montclair).<sup>[[390]](#cite_note-BOR-409)</sup>

For all their differences, the noble houses of Rivenspire hold many of the same traditions. Each house keeps its own fighting force, though in times of war or other emergencies, it is not uncommon for house troops to join with the city guard to form a single fighting force in defense of the region.<sup>[[391]](#cite_note-HTARH-410)</sup> The nobility of Rivenspire are known for burying their dead beneath the gnarled trees of Westmark Moor (except for monarchs, who are all buried in the great cemetery of [Cath Bedraud](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Cath_Bedraud) in Glenumbra).<sup>[[392]](#cite_note-TBOWM-411)</sup>

### Knightly Orders
→ *For more detailed information, see: [Breton Knightly Orders](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Breton_Knightly_Orders)* [![](https://images.uesp.net/thumb/4/4e/ON-render-Castle_Navire.jpg/200px-ON-render-Castle_Navire.jpg)](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:ON-render-Castle_Navire.jpg) [](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:ON-render-Castle_Navire.jpg) A Knightly Tournament Breton society is famous for its knightly orders,<sup>[[42]](#cite_note-ONTKOHR-45)</sup> with notable examples including Daggerfall's Knights of the Dragon, the [Knights of the Rose](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Knights_of_the_Rose) of Wayrest, the [Knights of the Flame](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Knights_of_the_Flame) of [Anticlere](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Anticlere), and Dwynnen's [Order of the Raven](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Order_of_the_Raven). Some Bretons served as knights under Clan Direnni sometime before the fall of the Direnni Hegemony.<sup>[[40]](#cite_note-ONARCP-43)</sup><sup>[[41]](#cite_note-ONTNS-44)</sup> However, it is commonly accepted that Bretons established their militant orders of knights when they became independent from Direnni elves. High Rock's cultural history is founded on tales of such noble and chivalrous knights, which supposedly fought for Breton liberation and drove the Direnni back to Balfiera Isle. The knightly orders were founded to carry on the tradition of nobles-in-arms and to ensure the province would have defenders at the ready should invading armies come to their gates.<sup>[[42]](#cite_note-ONTKOHR-45)</sup> The [Lion Guard](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Lion_Guard) was one such order before the formation of the Daggerfall Covenant in the Second Era.<sup>[[39]](#cite_note-TIEGTT-42)</sup> Breton knights espouse traditional codes of chivalric principles and are among the most prominent questers of High Rock.<sup>[[43]](#cite_note-TL-46)</sup><sup>[[44]](#cite_note-ONDHQ-47)</sup>

[![](https://images.uesp.net/thumb/4/4c/BK-misc-Breton_Warrior.jpeg/200px-BK-misc-Breton_Warrior.jpeg)](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:BK-misc-Breton_Warrior.jpeg) [](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:BK-misc-Breton_Warrior.jpeg) A Breton warrior Historically, knightly orders were composed of the high-born, providing a place for excess nobility. As High Rock became more prosperous, the merchant classes increasingly joined.<sup>[[42]](#cite_note-ONTKOHR-45)</sup> It is more difficult for commoners,<sup>[[371]](#cite_note-ONAV-389)</sup> but not impossible. Lady Joslin Garick, a captain in the All Flags Navy, is but one commoner who became a renowned knight.<sup>[[134]](#cite_note-ONCG-142)</sup> Knighthood confers a measure of nobility, and can be rewarded to the lower classes for significant contributions to society. If the position was not achieved through conflict, the membership is nominal only, such as with the "merchant knights", great contributors to the economy who do not take up arms, but instead heavily contribute to a knightly order's finances.<sup>[[42]](#cite_note-ONTKOHR-45)</sup>

Most competent knightly orders require applicants to have some degree of martial knowledge or skill before they are considered for membership. Less reliable orders may grant promotions in rank over a knight's nobility, wealth, or charisma, but generally, a knightly order will require their members to be skilled warriors so as not to tarnish the group's reputation.<sup>[[393]](#cite_note-412)</sup> Etiquette, swordsmanship, archery, and medical skill are factors considered when assessing potential recruits.<sup>[[394]](#cite_note-413)</sup> The spell-knight is an archetype that encapsulates the Breton staples of knighthood and the arcane,<sup>[[29]](#cite_note-ONLOTB-32)</sup><sup>[[33]](#cite_note-MTCSSM-36)</sup><sup>[[286]](#cite_note-COTH-304)</sup> while the druid-knight brings the druidic arts into the lifestyle of a knightly order.<sup>[[34]](#cite_note-ESOSSM-37)</sup><sup>[[135]](#cite_note-ONSKO-143)</sup> The Reachmen were inspired to breed their own hardy steeds when they saw how mounted Bretonic knights fought during their invasion of High Rock.<sup>[[329]](#cite_note-ONWKC-347)</sup>

Knights are addressed with the honor of "sir" or "dame". Knights subscribe to their own hierarchies and customs as dictated by their order. In most cases, these orders are governed by a marshal or a knight-commander. Regardless of the marshal's high station, their honorific remains the same.<sup>[[376]](#cite_note-NRAT-394)</sup> In older chivalric orders, heavy rings served as a knight's symbol of membership.<sup>[[101]](#cite_note-ROTPO-108)</sup> Each of the Eight Divines have their own templar knightly order as the militant arm of their respective temples.<sup>[[395]](#cite_note-414)</sup> One of High Rock's most notable heroes was the Breton knight Eleidon, owner of the eponymous [shield](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Eleidon%27s_Ward).<sup>[[373]](#cite_note-FAOT-391)</sup>

### Systreans
[![](https://images.uesp.net/thumb/7/7f/ON-prerelease-Firesong_03.jpg/200px-ON-prerelease-Firesong_03.jpg)](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:ON-prerelease-Firesong_03.jpg) [](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:ON-prerelease-Firesong_03.jpg) Druids and knights of Vastyr uniting against Maormer pirates The Systreans are the inhabitants of the Systres Archipelago. Primarily the descendants of the Bretons who settled on High Isle following the All Flags Navy's raid on Thras,<sup>[[52]](#cite_note-ONSHV4-55)</sup> the Systreans are major maritime traders, have their own knightly orders, and mostly follow a feudal society.<sup>[[68]](#cite_note-LABHI-74)</sup><sup>[[396]](#cite_note-SHV-415)</sup> Of course, druids settled in the archipelago long before,<sup>[[68]](#cite_note-LABHI-74)</sup> and though they prefer life in the forest, they have at times influenced and intermingled with the feudal Bretons.<sup>[[140]](#cite_note-ONSHV5-148)</sup><sup>[[84]](#cite_note-ONSHADG-90)</sup>

The Systres is an established neutral ground from conflicts, which the Bretons of High Isle greatly profit from.<sup>[[4]](#cite_note-ONHIPTZ-4)</sup> [House Dufort](Lore_House_Dufort.md) sells respite to people looking to get away from mainland troubles.<sup>[[4]](#cite_note-ONHIPTZ-4)</sup> It is considered a home away from home for much of the Breton elite,<sup>[[4]](#cite_note-ONHIPTZ-4)</sup> who treat it like a playground and resort.<sup>[[UOL 16]](#cite_note-ONHCP-219)</sup><sup>[[UOL 1]](#cite_note-ON2022-9)</sup> High Isle elite always dress in their finest to project their status and their barely-hidden ambitions,<sup>[[UOL 1]](#cite_note-ON2022-9)</sup> and the settlement of [Gonfalon Bay](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Gonfalon_Bay) has been described as "pompous".<sup>[[UOL 6]](#cite_note-ESOLive Firesong-71)</sup>

The isle of Galen developed a more working class population, and they are the most accepting of Druidism.<sup>[[UOL 6]](#cite_note-ESOLive Firesong-71)</sup> Unlike High Isle, where mainland influence established a feudal society long ago, most of Galen remained an untamed wilderness, with city Bretons are limited to the southern part of the land, in the city of [Vastyr](Lore_Vastyr.md).<sup>[[396]](#cite_note-SHV-415)</sup><sup>[[UOL 6]](#cite_note-ESOLive Firesong-71)</sup> The city features a blend of druidic and city Breton architecture, thanks to the [House Mornard](Lore_House_Mornard.md)'s connections to Druidism.<sup>[[396]](#cite_note-SHV-415)</sup>

The undesirables of Systrean society are taken to the lawless prison island of [Amenos](Lore_Amenos.md), where history shows its prisoners are forced into mining its resources.<sup>[[143]](#cite_note-ONSHV6-151)</sup> At one point, some were taken to nearby [Whalefall](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Whalefall) to be used for sport.<sup>[[397]](#cite_note-ONLouna-416)</sup><sup>[[398]](#cite_note-ONLendanor-417)</sup>

### Wyrd Covens
→ *For more detailed information, see: [Wyrd Covens](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Wyrd_Covens)* [![](https://images.uesp.net/thumb/7/75/ON-prerelease-Glenmoril_Style.jpeg/200px-ON-prerelease-Glenmoril_Style.jpeg)](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:ON-prerelease-Glenmoril_Style.jpeg) [](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:ON-prerelease-Glenmoril_Style.jpeg) A Glenmoril Wyrd Sister [Wyrd Covens](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Wyrd_Covens) (also known as **Wyresses**, **Wyrd Women**, **Wyrd Sisters**, the **Wyrd**, **Ward-Sisters**, **Name-Daughters**, and **nature-witches**) are female-only, animistic [witch](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Witches) covens that serve as wardens of [the Green](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:The_Green). They draw their power from the Earthbones, and revere nature and the elements. The leader of a coven is referred to as a "beldam".

The Wyrd originated from the ancient people that dwelled in [High Rock](Lore_High_Rock.md) who are referred to by retroactive nomenclature as the [Druids of Galen](Lore_Druids_of_Galen.md). A religious schism brought about the Wyrd's separation from their [druid](Lore_Druid.md) brethren. The Wyrd abandoned civilization in favor of living in the wilds, and believe that they are nature itself: the forest, the plants and beasts within it, and even the weather. In contrast, while ancient druids revered nature, they were not keen to isolate themselves and worship the untamed wilds. The druids accepted what they interpreted as their "proper place" as people, and embraced the idea that civilization can coexist alongside nature.

Wyrd witches are primarily Breton, though membership also extends to outsiders, even those from other races. Once a singular entity, the Wyrd split into subgroups by the time of the [last Druid King](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Kasorayn)'s voyage to [the Systres](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:The_Systres). These sisterhoods remained behind on the mainland to safeguard the forests of [High Rock](Lore_High_Rock.md), with some of the dozen or so covens even spreading throughout [Tamriel](Lore_Tamriel.md).

## Religion
[![](https://images.uesp.net/thumb/6/64/ON-concept-High_Isle_Cathedral.jpg/200px-ON-concept-High_Isle_Cathedral.jpg)](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:ON-concept-High_Isle_Cathedral.jpg) [](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:ON-concept-High_Isle_Cathedral.jpg) Breton cathedral on High Isle [![](https://images.uesp.net/thumb/c/c2/ON-Statue-Breton_Statue%2C_Arkay.jpg/200px-ON-Statue-Breton_Statue%2C_Arkay.jpg)](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:ON-Statue-Breton_Statue,_Arkay.jpg) [](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:ON-Statue-Breton_Statue,_Arkay.jpg) A statue of Arkay (ESO) Bretons believe two opposing forces, called the [Light](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Anu) and the [Dark](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Padomay) by some, have existed since before the gods were born. There are different interpretations, but they are said to be antithetical to each other, and evenly matched, but defy mortal conceptions of good and evil. They are technically immortal, as they do not live, only exist. The Aedra and Daedra are seen as pale reflections of the eternal conflict between the Light and Dark. Their endless struggle creates energies that distort their surroundings, and those energies are so powerful that life can appear.<sup>[[399]](#cite_note-TLD-418)</sup>

The undead and the Daedra tend to align with the Dark, as their natures are more akin to it. Mortals and the creatures of Mundus are more aligned with the Light. The evils of mortalkind more attuned to the Dark are incredibly dangerous. Magic is believed to come directly from the impersonal, intermingling energies swirling about both entities. Black magic is more a matter of intent than effect: destruction spells on their own are not black magic, for example, but are black magic when cast upon innocent people. The defeat of Daedra strengthens the light just a little. Conversly, the destruction of a Tamrielic creature strengthens the Dark. The gods are believed to mostly align with the Light, save for an ambiguous few. Mortals and those that reside in [Aetherius](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Aetherius) can perceive traces of the Light and Dark; the Light inspires most mortals to behavior deemed good by human standards. What the denizens of Mundus can perceive of the Dark is utterly evil by human standards; those who have visions of the Dark are often driven mad. The Dark is described as an emptiness that draws the soul in to be twisted and destroyed.<sup>[[399]](#cite_note-TLD-418)</sup>

According to the forbidden texts of Stormhaven's Priory of the Golden Staff, Mehrunes Dagon was created by the [Magna Ge](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Magna_Ge) to unmake the flawed creation of Mundus in accordance to [Magnus](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Magnus)'s plans.<sup>[[400]](#cite_note-DCT-419)</sup><sup>[[401]](#cite_note-MTCSC-420)</sup> Some think Bretons are not disposed to "excessive religion",<sup>[[60]](#cite_note-AHOD-64)</sup> while others consider them nearly as devout as Colovian Imperials.<sup>[[39]](#cite_note-TIEGTT-42)</sup> Some rural lords of High Rock were known to practice patron spirit worship, and offending them was considered an ill omen by local shamans.<sup>[[402]](#cite_note-Arena Rumors-421)</sup>

### Religious History
[![](https://images.uesp.net/thumb/2/20/ON-load-Heart_of_the_Wyrd_Tree.jpg/200px-ON-load-Heart_of_the_Wyrd_Tree.jpg)](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:ON-load-Heart_of_the_Wyrd_Tree.jpg) [](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:ON-load-Heart_of_the_Wyrd_Tree.jpg) The Wyrd Tree The earliest Bretons, the Manmer, worshipped gods derived from the faiths of their Nedic and Aldmer ancestors, including [Sheor](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Sheor)<sup>[[403]](#cite_note-CN-422)</sup> and [Hircine](Lore_Hircine.md).<sup>[[9]](#cite_note-LADCG-11)</sup> These Manmer inherited a form of nature worship from the Nedes, but this faith split into two separate subcultures. The witches of the Wyrd became their own entity due to the elves, and these witches continue to worship "old gods of the ancient past".<sup>[[9]](#cite_note-LADCG-11)</sup> Druidism, on the other hand, arose shortly after the Bretons first came about,<sup>[[32]](#cite_note-ONWD-35)</sup><sup>[[29]](#cite_note-ONLOTB-32)</sup> and their Y'ffre-centric religion survived in the Systres Archipelago after their exodus.<sup>[[3]](#cite_note-ONSHV-3)</sup> Druidism would later be reintroduced to mainland Tamriel, specifically around the Iliac Bay.<sup>[[176]](#cite_note-DFDeath-187)</sup><sup>[[UOL 14]](#cite_note-DFTDE-191)</sup>

Details of Aldmeri religious influence among the earliest Bretons are sparse. Evidence of peaceful cultural diffusion of religion between men and mer exists in the form of unearthed ancient idols of Mara as depicted in the elven pantheon.<sup>[[74]](#cite_note-Manmer-80)</sup> Interestingly, Sheor is depicted positively in a lovers embrace with this elven Mara figure,<sup>[[74]](#cite_note-Manmer-80)</sup> when Sheor is demonized in modern Breton religion,<sup>[[36]](#cite_note-VOFB-39)</sup> just as the pantheon equivalent of Lorkhan was demonized by Aldmer.<sup>[[404]](#cite_note-VOFHE-423)</sup> Worship of elven gods still exists in modern Breton culture; Bretons that emphasize their elvish blood are often drawn towards Phynaster.<sup>[[36]](#cite_note-VOFB-39)</sup> The gods Magnus and Y'ffre are traditionally associated with elven pantheons.<sup>[[102]](#cite_note-VOF-109)</sup> Druids claim that though the Nedes did not know the name "Y'ffre" until the "daughters and sons of … Anuiel" introduced it, they still felt Y'ffre's presence in their hearts and channeled his power.<sup>[[32]](#cite_note-ONWD-35)</sup>

Most Bretons transitioned to the Eight [Divines](Lore_Divines.md) under the Alessian Empire. The Eight Divines are worshipped widely in mainstream Breton culture,<sup>[[39]](#cite_note-TIEGTT-42)</sup> but other traditional deities still persist nonetheless. Sheor, Phynaster, Y'ffre and Magnus have significant cults in High Rock.<sup>[[102]](#cite_note-VOF-109)</sup>

Daedra worship is often seen in a negative light among Bretons. During the time of the Three Banners War, it was described as something needing to be cleansed.<sup>[[160]](#cite_note-THOTE-169)</sup> Negative sentiments against it required intervention from King Kurog, who legitimized his people's religious worship among their Daggerfall Covenant allies by claiming that Mauloch wasn't a Daedric Prince like [Malacath](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Malacath).<sup>[[405]](#cite_note-AUADC1-424)</sup> High King Emeric and his counselors tolerated the Spirit Wardens of [Azura](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Azura) due to their charitable contributions, their ability to be inconspicuous, and their ability to produce potions capable of combating the nightmares inflicted by the [Vaermina](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Vaermina) cult known as the [Supernal Dreamers](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Supernal_Dreamers).<sup>[[406]](#cite_note-Altien-425)</sup> The Knights of the Silver Rose ousted a count of Daggerfall for his worship of Meridia during this time period.<sup>[[407]](#cite_note-OCESO-426)</sup>

### Major Gods

#### [Akatosh](Lore_Akatosh.md)
The Dragon God of Time is acknowledged as the first of the gods to emerge from the Beginning Place. He embodies endurance, invincibility, and everlasting legitimacy.<sup>[[102]](#cite_note-VOF-109)</sup> Akatosh is hailed by the [Akatosh Chantry](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Akatosh_Chantry) in the Iliac Bay, and the [Order of the Hour](Lore_Order_of_the_Hour.md) is his sword.<sup>[[408]](#cite_note-427)</sup><sup>[[409]](#cite_note-OOTH-428)</sup> He is the patron deity of Wayrest and the [Isle of Balfiera](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Isle_of_Balfiera).<sup>[[410]](#cite_note-429)</sup>

#### [Arkay](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Arkay)
Arkay (also spelled Ark'ay)<sup>[[411]](#cite_note-ATG-430)</sup> is the god of burials and funeral rites, and is associated with the seasons.<sup>[[102]](#cite_note-VOF-109)</sup> According to a [Breton story](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Ark%27ay_The_God), Arkay was originally a mortal who ascended to godhood. As the God of the Cycle of Birth and Death,<sup>[[79]](#cite_note-TDCP11-85)</sup> he is charged with keeping the balance of death and life in the universe.<sup>[[411]](#cite_note-ATG-430)</sup> In the Iliac Bay, the [Order of Arkay](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Order_of_Arkay) celebrates the Blessed Neutrality that Arkay stands for. They do not offer blessings, for to give favor or disfavor upon one would upset the eternal balance. Their libraries and sages are some of the finest in Tamriel.<sup>[[412]](#cite_note-431)</sup> The [Knights of the Circle](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Knights_of_the_Circle) are the military arm of the Order.<sup>[[413]](#cite_note-KOTC-432)</sup> Arkay is the patron deity of the [Ilessan Hills](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Ilessan_Hills) and [Shalgora](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Shalgora).<sup>[[414]](#cite_note-433)</sup> Arkay is also the patron of [House Tamrith](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:House_Tamrith), who are devout followers of the Light.<sup>[[415]](#cite_note-434)</sup><sup>[[416]](#cite_note-435)</sup> The scions of House Tamrith study the Way of the Light and obey Arkay's teachings.<sup>[[417]](#cite_note-436)</sup> Their holy symbols bear the crest of House Tamrith and the symbol of the Light of Arkay.<sup>[[418]](#cite_note-437)</sup> Arkay's holy relics can be used to combat the undead.<sup>[[419]](#cite_note-ESOAlvaren-438)</sup>

[![](https://images.uesp.net/thumb/1/12/DF-npc-Dibella_Statue.png/200px-DF-npc-Dibella_Statue.png)](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:DF-npc-Dibella_Statue.png) [](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:DF-npc-Dibella_Statue.png) A statue of Dibella, Goddess of Beauty (Daggerfall)
#### [Dibella](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Dibella)
The Goddess of Beauty is very popular. She has many different cults dedicated to different aspects of her worship: some are dedicated to women, some to aesthetics and art, and others to erotic instruction.<sup>[[102]](#cite_note-VOF-109)</sup> In the late Third Era, the [House of Dibella](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:House_of_Dibella) was responsible for the administration of temples dedicated to Dibella in the province of High Rock, and its militant branch, the [Order of the Lily](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Order_of_the_Lily), was also active in the province at this time.<sup>[[420]](#cite_note-HOD-439)</sup> Dibella is the patron deity of the regions of [Koegria](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Koegria) and [Menevia](Lore_Menevia_(county).md),<sup>[[421]](#cite_note-440)</sup> and is venerated as a member of the Breton pantheon.<sup>[[102]](#cite_note-VOF-109)</sup>

#### [Jephre](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Jephre)
Jephre (also known as Jeh Free)<sup>[[121]](#cite_note-KEII-128)</sup> is the God of the Forest and the spirit of the "now". Jephre is typically considered an elven god, and is understood to have turned himself into the Earth Bones and established the laws of nature.<sup>[[102]](#cite_note-VOF-109)</sup> He is still revered by some Breton hunters and farmers.<sup>[[39]](#cite_note-TIEGTT-42)</sup> The Beldama Wyrd also worship him.<sup>[[422]](#cite_note-WCONHR-441)</sup> Bretons respect the Vicars of Jephre, a group of his adherents who are known defenders of the natural world.<sup>[[423]](#cite_note-442)</sup> The druids recognize Jephre as Y'ffre, the Green-King, the Slumbering Father of Nirn, who is their primary deity.<sup>[[32]](#cite_note-ONWD-35)</sup>

#### [Julianos](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Julianos)
The God of Wisdom and Logic is a favorite of Breton mages. He is the god of history, literature, law and contradiction.<sup>[[102]](#cite_note-VOF-109)</sup> In the Iliac Bay, temples dedicated to him are known as [Schools of Julianos](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:School_of_Julianos).<sup>[[424]](#cite_note-443)</sup> As their name implies, these temples are considered educational institutions.<sup>[[425]](#cite_note-TROZ-444)</sup> They are believed to have spread the term "magicka" to describe the "power associated with performing magic".<sup>[[426]](#cite_note-KE12-445)</sup> The templar knightly order associated with the School of Julianos is the [Knights Mentor](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Knights_Mentor).<sup>[[427]](#cite_note-KM-446)</sup> Julianos is the patron deity of the regions of [Daenia](Lore_Daenia_(duchy).md), Dwynnen and [Tulune](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Tulune).<sup>[[428]](#cite_note-447)</sup>

[![](https://images.uesp.net/thumb/0/04/ON-misc-Kynareth.png/200px-ON-misc-Kynareth.png)](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:ON-misc-Kynareth.png) [](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:ON-misc-Kynareth.png) Systrean statue of Kynareth (ESO)
#### [Kynareth](Lore_Kynareth.md)
The Goddess of Air is a patron to sailors and travelers. Legend holds she was the first to agree to Lorkhan's idea to invent the mortal plane, and she provided a space for its creation. Kynareth is associated with rain.<sup>[[102]](#cite_note-VOF-109)</sup> The island of Betony is considered holy land of Kynareth. This was a factor for Daggerfall's involvement in the War of Betony. It was also the reason why the conflict escalated to the [Battle of Cryngaine Field](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Battle_of_Cryngaine_Field), which ended the war.<sup>[[429]](#cite_note-DFNarrative-448)</sup> The [Temple of Kynareth](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Temple_of_Kynareth) does her work in the Iliac Bay. In the Third Era, her Temple contained the greatest physicians in Tamriel; their ability to cure magical and mundane diseases was said to be unrivaled.<sup>[[430]](#cite_note-449)</sup> The [Kynaran Order](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Kynaran_Order) is the militant arm of the Temple.<sup>[[431]](#cite_note-Kyn Or-450)</sup> Kynareth is the patron deity of [Alcaire](Lore_Alcaire_(fiefdom).md), Daggerfall and the [Wrothgarian Mountains](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Wrothgarian_Mountains).<sup>[[432]](#cite_note-451)</sup> The air spirits Amaro, Pina, and Tallatha, are acknowledged as [the fingers of Kynareth](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:The_Fingers_of_Kynareth) by the Skeffington Coven.<sup>[[433]](#cite_note-452)</sup>

#### [Magnus](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Magnus)
Magnus is the god of sorcery, who withdrew from creation at the last second. He is represented by a golden eye, an astrolabe or a telescope, but a staff is his most common symbol. Legend holds that he can possess powerful wizards and lend them power.<sup>[[102]](#cite_note-VOF-109)</sup> Breton followers of Magnus sometimes use wicker effigies as stand-ins for themselves when performing certain rituals.<sup>[[434]](#cite_note-453)</sup>

One known Breton sect that worshipped Magnus is the Priory of the Golden Staff. The Priory believed in Magnus's grand design for the Mundus, and his disappointment at the flaws introduced into his creation. They also believed that some of the Magna Ge once sought a tool to unmake what had been made wrong, in order that it could be remade in accordance with the Architect's plan.<sup>[[400]](#cite_note-DCT-419)</sup>

#### [Mara](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Mara)
Mara is the Mother-Goddess, and is married to Akatosh in Breton lore.<sup>[[102]](#cite_note-VOF-109)</sup> She is the patron deity of several regions of High Rock, such as [Anticlere](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Anticlere), Betony, [Glenumbra Moors](Lore_Glenumbra_Moors_(barony).md), and [Northmoor](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Northmoor).<sup>[[435]](#cite_note-454)</sup> In Anticlere, the 21st of Last Seed is known as [Appreciation Day](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Daggerfall:Holidays#Last_Seed), an ancient holiday of thanksgiving for a bountiful harvest. It is considered a holy and contemplative day devoted to Mara, the goddess-protector of the region.<sup>[[436]](#cite_note-455)</sup> Temples dedicated to the Divine are administered by the [Benevolence of Mara](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Benevolence_of_Mara), a religious organization dedicated to Mara and her teachings, and can be found in major urban centers throughout the province.<sup>[[437]](#cite_note-DFBenevolence-456)</sup> The [Maran Knights](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Maran_Knights) are a controversial knightly order dedicated to Mara and the protection of her temples.<sup>[[438]](#cite_note-MK-457)</sup>

#### [Phynaster](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Phynaster)
Phynaster is an Altmer hero-god who is the patron deity and teacher of the Direnni. He is often worshipped by Breton mages who care about their elven blood.<sup>[[102]](#cite_note-VOF-109)</sup>

#### [Sheor](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Sheor)
Also known as the Bad Man, Sheor is the source of all strife. He originated as a god of crop failure, and is believed to be a demonized version of the Nordic Shor.<sup>[[102]](#cite_note-VOF-109)</sup> Some sculptings created by the Bretons' Nedic ancestors have been found in [Glenumbra](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Glenumbra), which portray what appears to be their version of Sheor before he was villianized, paired with Mara as an Aldmer.<sup>[[74]](#cite_note-Manmer-80)</sup>

[![](https://images.uesp.net/thumb/f/f3/ON-misc-Stendarr.jpg/200px-ON-misc-Stendarr.jpg)](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:ON-misc-Stendarr.jpg) [](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:ON-misc-Stendarr.jpg) Systrean statue of Stendarr (ESO)
#### [Stendarr](Lore_Stendarr.md)
Stendarr (also known as Shandar) is known as the God of Mercy, and is the patron of magistrates, rulers, and knights errant. He is a god of compassion and righteous rule.<sup>[[102]](#cite_note-VOF-109)</sup> Temples dedicated to the Divine can be found throughout the Iliac Bay. Administered by the [Temple of Stendarr](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Temple_of_Stendarr), a religious organization dedicated to Stendarr and his teachings, the temples offer healing and training to the population of the Iliac Bay. Some mock their compassion, calling them sentimental fools and tenderhearts; but everyone depends on Stendarr when Sai, the God of Luck, abandons them.<sup>[[439]](#cite_note-DFStendarr-458)</sup> The [Crusaders](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Crusaders), also known as the Knights of Stendarr, are a knightly order dedicated to him which protect his temples against its adversaries, such as the [Citadel of Ebonarm](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Citadel_of_Ebonarm).<sup>[[440]](#cite_note-DFCrusaders-459)</sup> Stendarr is the patron deity of [Bhoriane](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Bhoriane), Phrygias and [Urvaius](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Urvaius).<sup>[[441]](#cite_note-460)</sup>

#### [Zenithar](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Zenithar)
Zenithar (often shortened to Z'en) is the God of Work and Commerce, a cultivated god of merchants, artisans, and middle nobility. His faithful tout him as a god "that will always win".<sup>[[102]](#cite_note-VOF-109)</sup> He teaches Bretonkind that they will be rewarded if they work hard. He also teaches them to be wise in their spending, and to never steal from others. Many of his rewards are those of the spirit: being productive, whether farming, smithing, or creating, honors Zenithar. Zenithar wishes for his faithful to find joy in their work.<sup>[[442]](#cite_note-461)</sup> In the Iliac Bay, the [Resolution of Zenithar](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Resolution_of_Zenithar) pays heed to the god.<sup>[[443]](#cite_note-Reso Zen-462)</sup> Zenithar is not merely the God of Merchants and Commerce; he is also a warrior god. The militant arm of the Resolution, the [Knights of Iron](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Knights_of_Iron), represent this part of him.<sup>[[444]](#cite_note-463)</sup> Zenithar is the patron deity of [Gavaudon](Lore_Gavaudon_(fiefdom).md), Kambria and [Glenpoint](Lore_Glenpoint.md).<sup>[[445]](#cite_note-464)</sup>

### Minor Gods

#### [Baan Dar](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Baan_Dar)
Baan Dar (also known as "the Bandit")<sup>[[121]](#cite_note-KEII-128)</sup> is noted to be a considerable force within the lands of High Rock by [Arkan the Wise](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Arkan), a Second Era scribe of Daggerfall. *[The First Scroll of Baan Dar](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:The_First_Scroll_of_Baan_Dar)*, which Arkan transcribed, say Baan Dar manifests across Tamriel to aid people in times of need.<sup>[[446]](#cite_note-TFSOBD-465)</sup> This aspect to his character is explored in the historical-fiction novel, *King Edward*, when Queen Aliera praises him along with other gods for bringing her husband Moraelyn and son Edward back to her safely.<sup>[[121]](#cite_note-KEII-128)</sup> He is known to be revered by the [Thieves Guild](Lore_Thieves_Guild.md) branch in the Iliac Bay.<sup>[[447]](#cite_note-DFAND-466)</sup>

#### [Druagaa](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Druagaa)
**The Old Goddess of Flowers**. A festival named Gardtide is still held in her honor on the 1st of Rain's Hand every year by the people of Tamarilyn Point, a coastal region of Menevia in central High Rock.

#### [Ephen](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Ephen)
Ephen (also known as S'ephen)<sup>[[426]](#cite_note-KE12-445)</sup> is the center of a temple-cult who worships him as **The God of the Wild**<sup>[[UOL 19]](#cite_note-DFpreview-467)</sup>. He was a [Chimer](Lore_Chimer.md) noble that was active during the early First Era. In death, he was given the duty of safeguarding the Horn of Summoning and eventually the [Staff of Chaos](Lore_Staff_of_Chaos.md). Statues of Ephen depict him wielding a hammer, atop of an anvil of [adamantium](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Adamantium),<sup>[[123]](#cite_note-TRB4-131)</sup> and shrines dedicated to him can be found across the Iliac Bay.<sup>[[353]](#cite_note-DFShrines-371)</sup>

#### [Jhim Sei](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Jhim_Sei)
Jhim Sei is little known, though their sphere of influence may revolve around music, since in the historical fiction *King Edward*, they are compared to Jephre, the elven God of Song and Forest.<sup>[[121]](#cite_note-KEII-128)</sup> There are shrines dedicated to Jhim Sei across High Rock.<sup>[[353]](#cite_note-DFShrines-371)</sup>

[![](https://images.uesp.net/2/27/Mfull_Sfull.jpg)](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:Mfull_Sfull.jpg) [](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:Mfull_Sfull.jpg) Mara's Tear (left) and Shandar's Sorrow (right)
#### [Mara's Tear](Lore_Masser.md) and [Shandar's Sorrow/Stendarr's Sorrow](Lore_Secunda.md)
Mara's Tear and Shandar's Sorrow, originally mortal lovers in a forbidden relationship, are the ancient Bretonic interpretations of the moons. After Shandar suffered a mortal wound defending his lover, the goddess Mara took the two mortals and placed them in the heavens so they could always be together, and the light of their love could shine upon the world as moonlight.<sup>[[448]](#cite_note-MT-468)</sup> Ancient druids had Mara's Tear and Shandar's Sorrow as witnesses to sanctify rituals.<sup>[[62]](#cite_note-ESODruid King-67)</sup><sup>[[449]](#cite_note-ONEV-469)</sup>

#### [Notorgo](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Notorgo)
Notorgo is known as the Messenger God.<sup>[[UOL 19]](#cite_note-DFpreview-467)</sup> He is mentioned in the *King Edward* series of books, where Queen Aliera praises Notorgo along with other gods for bringing her husband Moraelyn and son Edward back to her safely.<sup>[[121]](#cite_note-KEII-128)</sup>

#### [Q'Olwen](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Q%27Olwen)
Little is known about this deity, except that it is associated with those in pursuit of lore.<sup>[[UOL 19]](#cite_note-DFpreview-467)</sup> Q'Olwen is worshipped in the Iliac Bay area, where shrines to him can be found.<sup>[[353]](#cite_note-DFShrines-371)</sup>

#### [Raen](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Raen)
Raen is the Breton God of Agriculture.<sup>[[UOL 19]](#cite_note-DFpreview-467)</sup> Reliquaries of Raen can be found across the Iliac Bay region.<sup>[[353]](#cite_note-DFShrines-371)</sup>

#### [Reymon Ebonarm](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Reymon_Ebonarm)
Reymon Ebonarm is the God of War, a deity of some significance to the Bretons.<sup>[[450]](#cite_note-ILTEA-470)</sup> He is featured in the Bretonic historical novel *King Edward*. He has shrines in the Alcaire, Daenia, Daggerfall, Dwynnen, Ilessan Hills, Kambria, Wayrest, and the Wrothgarian Mountain regions of High Rock.<sup>[[353]](#cite_note-DFShrines-371)</sup>

#### [Sai](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Sai)
Sai is the God of Luck. He was born a mortal and had the talent to spread luck to others, but not to himself. Legend says he was a soldier, struck down in his first battle just as it was won. [Ebonarm](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Ebonarm) appeared to him, and offered him immortality if he agreed to spread his luck around. He said the gods were overworked, and thought Sai's inborn talent would balance things out. He readily agreed, and he was told that he could keep his body for a time before it began to fade.<sup>[[451]](#cite_note-PIX-471)</sup> Excessive worship of Sai causes the disease known as [Sai's Affliction](Lore_Disease.md#Sai.27s_Affliction). Sufferers of the disease have been abandoned by Sai, and long for the god's presence. They are driven to incessant gambling, seeking proof of the god's favor. This usually leaves the victim in poverty or debt.<sup>[[451]](#cite_note-PIX-471)</sup> Followers of Sai sometimes convert to worshipping [Stendarr](Lore_Stendarr.md) when Sai abandons them.<sup>[[452]](#cite_note-472)</sup> Reliquaries dedicated to Sai can be found throughout the Iliac Bay region.<sup>[[353]](#cite_note-DFShrines-371)</sup>

#### [Sethiete](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Sethiete)
Sethiete (also called Seth)<sup>[[453]](#cite_note-ARGideon-473)</sup> is a deity that is worshipped across Tamriel. The nature of Sethiete is unknown, but what is known is his influence. His places of worship are known as the [Temples of Sethiete](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Temple_of_Sethiete), and one of his temples is a landmark in the city of Camlorn that anchors the main street with the Royal Palace.<sup>[[454]](#cite_note-MOT1-474)</sup>

#### [Vigryl](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Vigryl)
Vigryl (also called Vir Gil)<sup>[[121]](#cite_note-KEII-128)</sup> is the God of the Sea worshipped in the Iliac Bay region.<sup>[[353]](#cite_note-DFShrines-371)</sup><sup>[[UOL 19]](#cite_note-DFpreview-467)</sup> People pray to Vigryl to bring them better weather.<sup>[[UOL 19]](#cite_note-DFpreview-467)</sup>

### Saints
The Bretons have saints that are affiliated with a god, and have usually performed great deeds.

[![](https://images.uesp.net/thumb/c/c5/ON-statue-Saint_Stental.jpg/200px-ON-statue-Saint_Stental.jpg)](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:ON-statue-Saint_Stental.jpg) [](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:ON-statue-Saint_Stental.jpg) Statue of Saint Stental
#### [Ellenica](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Ellenica)
Saint Ellenica was a priestess of Arkay.<sup>[[419]](#cite_note-ESOAlvaren-438)</sup> Her prayer book is a holy relic, and contains passages that can be read to put the dead to rest.<sup>[[455]](#cite_note-475)</sup> She was buried in Flyleaf Catacombs with her prayer book, which was retrieved in [2E 582](Lore_Second_Era.md#2E_582).<sup>[[456]](#cite_note-476)</sup>

#### [Marben](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Marben)
Saint Marben is a saint of Arkay.<sup>[[419]](#cite_note-ESOAlvaren-438)</sup><sup>[[457]](#cite_note-477)</sup> Saint Marben's Fingerbone is a holy relic of Arkay, and was buried at [Sanguine Barrows](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Sanguine_Barrows) until it was retrieved from Saint Marben's grave in [2E 582](Lore_Second_Era.md#2E_582).<sup>[[458]](#cite_note-478)</sup><sup>[[459]](#cite_note-479)</sup>

#### [Octavien](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Octavien)
Saint Octavien was a Priest of Arkay who was slain with a scythe by Daedra worshippers.<sup>[[460]](#cite_note-480)</sup> The broken scythe blade that killed Octavien is a holy relic of Arkay. It was buried in a tomb near Lorkrata Hills until it was retrieved by a Knight of Arkay in [2E 582](Lore_Second_Era.md#2E_582).<sup>[[461]](#cite_note-481)</sup>

[![](https://images.uesp.net/thumb/0/08/ON-misc-Saint_Pelin.png/200px-ON-misc-Saint_Pelin.png)](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:ON-misc-Saint_Pelin.png) [](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:ON-misc-Saint_Pelin.png) Saint Pelin
#### [Pelin](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Pelin)
[Saint Pelin the Martyr](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Pelin) was a Breton priest of [Stendarr](Lore_Stendarr.md) who was canonized after sacrificing himself in defense of the [Bangkorai Garrison](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Bangkorai_Garrison) in [1E 1029](Lore_First_Era.md#1E_1029), which in turn, brought [High Rock](Lore_High_Rock.md) into the [First Empire](Lore_Alessian_Empire.md) of [Cyrodiil](Lore_Cyrodiil.md). He became a hero to the Bretons of [Evermore](Lore_Evermore.md) and [Bangkorai](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Bangkorai), memorialized by the chapel of St. Pelin in Evermore, the [Order of Saint Pelin](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Order_of_Saint_Pelin), the knightly order of the Kingdom of Evermore, and the great cemetery called Pelin Graveyard.

#### [Stental](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Stental)
Saint Stental slew the demon of Overlook Hill (also called "the Leaper"), rescuing the three Sisters of Kynareth from an untimely death.<sup>[[462]](#cite_note-482)</sup> A statue dedicated to him was built where the demon was slain.<sup>[[463]](#cite_note-483)</sup>

#### [Vitache](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Vitache)
Saint Vitache is the Patron of Millers, Scissor-Grinders, and Bathhouse Attendants. She was honored daily by the millers of Northglen in [2E 582](Lore_Second_Era.md#2E_582).<sup>[[464]](#cite_note-484)</sup>

### Revered Persons
[![](https://images.uesp.net/thumb/0/08/ON-misc-Druid_King.png/200px-ON-misc-Druid_King.png)](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:ON-misc-Druid_King.png) [](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:ON-misc-Druid_King.png) Kasorayn, the last Druid King
#### [Druid King](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Druid_King)
The [Druid King](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Druid_King) (or **Druid Queen** and **Archdruid**) is more accurately described as a title rather than a person. It is a position for the highest authority among the [druids](Lore_Druid.md), and a philosophical figure that is revered in [High Rock](Lore_High_Rock.md). The role of Druid King is not inherited, as titles among the druids are earned.

The Druid King has the authority to bind and command the nature spirits safely, entities that are as unpredictable as nature itself. The Druid King has dominion over nature in that they can bring prosperity or make nature run amok.

#### [Eleidon](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Eleidon)
[Eleidon](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Eleidon) was a renowned holy Breton [knight](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Breton_Knightly_Orders) of legend. He was recorded in Breton history as a highly esteemed individual, admired for his bravery and unwavering commitment to set all wrongs right and fight against any injustices. Many stories exist about Eleidon's gallant and brave deeds, including a particularly well-known tale in which he saved a baron's daughter from certain death at the hands of a warlord. In recognition of his noble acts, the baron expressed his gratitude by commissioning the creation of an enchanted shield, known as [Eleidon's Ward](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Eleidon%27s_Ward). This artifact was imbued with magical properties, allowing the wielder to heal wounds.

#### [Gyron Vardengroet](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Gyron_Vardengroet) (The Sage)
[Gyron Vardengroet](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Gyron_Vardengroet) is an immortal wizard of legend that was born in the early years of the [Second Era](Lore_Second_Era.md), and was prophesied by the [Gods](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Gods) as a champion that would be sent down to guide others and bring wisdom. His exploits would earn him the title of **the Sage**, and **Great Sage**. Physically, he is described as a tall, bald, and bearded Breton with dark eyes, an indigo robe trimmed with gold, a pointed wizard's hat, and an intricately carved staff. He is the primary figure in the books *[The Sage](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:The_Sage)*, *[Feyfolken](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Feyfolken)*, and *[The Final Lesson](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:The_Final_Lesson)*. Gyron has monuments erected in his reverence in both [High Rock](Lore_High_Rock.md) and [Hammerfell](Lore_Hammerfell.md). He was listed alongside [Voernet](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Voernet) and [Druid](Lore_Druid.md) [King](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Druid_King) [Kasorayn](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Kasorayn) as one of the most powerful Breton mages in history.

#### [I'ric Harad Egun](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:I%27ric_Harad_Egun)
[I'ric Harad Egun](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:I%27ric_Harad_Egun) (sometimes shortened to **I'ric**) was the [Altmer](Lore_Altmer.md) archmagister of the [Crystal Tower](Lore_Crystal_Tower.md), believed to be alive sometime in the early-mid [First Era](Lore_First_Era.md). His name is widely known and is comparable to the likes of [Moraelyn](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Moraelyn), the Witch-King of [Ebonheart](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Ebonheart), and [Ebonarm](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Ebonarm), the God of War. According to the historical fiction, *[King Edward](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:King_Edward)*, his name is implied to have significant weight, and so throughout the story, he is simply referred as the **Arch Magister**. He is worshipped at altars in [High Rock](Lore_High_Rock.md) and [Hammerfell](Lore_Hammerfell.md).

#### [Kieran](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Kieran)
[Kieran the Bard](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Kieran) is a figure that is shrouded in mystery. Some of his stories have been lost, while others were successfully documented. His recorded tales fall into three categories dubbed the Woodland Cycle, Castles and Kings, and an unnamed lustful category. Some stories have become mere shells of the original and are now simple bedtime stories, and it is unknown if his stories are based on true events, allegory, or if they were simply written to entertain. He has shrines called Kieran Theatres in [Hammerfell](Lore_Hammerfell.md) and [High Rock](Lore_High_Rock.md), and he is of significance to Bretons. A Bretonic ruler of a [kingdom](Lore_Hero.md#Dynasty_of_Odar_the_Brave) neighboring the [Bloodfall Kingdom](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Bloodfall_Kingdom) is rumored to have had a tale of Kieran staged for the [Old Life Festival](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Old_Life_Festival).

[![](https://images.uesp.net/thumb/8/88/ON-statue-Viridian_Woods_Statue.jpg/200px-ON-statue-Viridian_Woods_Statue.jpg)](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:ON-statue-Viridian_Woods_Statue.jpg) [](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:ON-statue-Viridian_Woods_Statue.jpg) A statue representing the Viridian Sentinel
#### [The Viridian Sentinel](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Viridian_Sentinel)
The [Viridian Sentinel](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Viridian_Sentinel) protects the human inhabitants of northern [Bangkorai](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Bangkorai) from the beasts and witches that live in the forest. According to the legend of the Viridian Sentinel, long ago the [Direnni](Lore_Direnni.md) forged a covenant with the [Earth Bones](Lore_Ehlnofey.md) to protect their settlements located throughout all of High Rock from the wild. The Bretons, who displaced the Direnni, had no such arrangement, and as a result their farms in Bangkorai were gradually overrun by the wilderness. The people were pushed to the brink of starvation, causing a young boy called [Greenward](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Greenward) to pray to [Stendarr](Lore_Stendarr.md) for salvation. Stendarr taught him to forge a new pact with the forest, giving him the power to restrain the natural creatures within. He thus became the first Viridian Sentinel.

The Viridian Sentinel has great power over the forest, and can use this power to perform potent feats of [magic](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Nature_Magic). When the [Glenmoril Wyrd](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Glenmoril_Wyrd) became bound to the forest, they also gave some deference to the Sentinel due to that connection (though they had not been a party to the original pact). Although Viridian Sentinels were known for their longevity, over time, the Sentinel ages like other mortals, and must pass on their power and title to a new mortal before death. Their eyes age at a normal rate, however, and therefore a Sentinel usually requires a monocle when reading to counteract deteriorating eyesight.

## Artifacts
[![](https://images.uesp.net/thumb/3/32/SR-item-Chrysamere.jpg/150px-SR-item-Chrysamere.jpg)](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:SR-item-Chrysamere.jpg) [](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:SR-item-Chrysamere.jpg) Chrysamere
#### [Chrysamere](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Chrysamere)
[Chrysamere](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Chrysamere) (also called the **Chrysamere Blade**, or **the Chrysamere**) is an ancient [adamantium](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Adamantium) claymore [artifact](Lore_Artifacts.md) with offensive capabilities only surpassed by its defenses. It has [magical](Lore_Magic.md) properties which, unlike most weapons, are defensive in nature: it heals the wielder, grants them resistance to fire, and reflects hostile spells. It is unaligned, and is not a Daedric artifact. Chrysamere was forged in the late [Merethic Era](Lore_Merethic_Era.md) by the Breton swordsmith [Asterie Bedel](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Asterie_Bedel), who delighted in using the techniques of both [man](Lore_Men.md) and [mer](Lore_Mer.md) in her creations. In Chrysamere's case, this most clearly manifests in the placement of her maker's mark, a "mage's knot" within the heart of the sword that is said to harken back to the earliest days of Bretonic culture. Chrysamere is also said to have been influenced by the magic of Breton society's Elven forebears, and it gained further enchantments over time. Chrysamere does not typically stay with one swordsman for long, for it chooses not to favor one champion. It has earned the title of the **Sword of Heroes**, but it also goes by other names such as the **Sword of Kings** and the **Blade of Blades**. Chrysamere is considered a holy weapon, and in this context it is referred to as the **Sword of the [Paladin](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Paladins)**, or simply the **Paladin's Blade**.

[![](https://images.uesp.net/thumb/2/25/ON-misc-Druid_King_Vestments.png/150px-ON-misc-Druid_King_Vestments.png)](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:ON-misc-Druid_King_Vestments.png) [](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:ON-misc-Druid_King_Vestments.png) Druid King's Regalia
#### [Druid King's Regalia](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Druid_King%27s_Regalia)
The [Druid King's Regalia](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Druid_King%27s_Regalia) consists of a crown, a gauntlet, and a staff which were created by the [god](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Gods) [Y'ffre](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Y%27ffre). These gifts were worn with wisdom and mercy by the line of [Druid Kings](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Druid_King), and serve to legitimize one's ascension to the Ivy Throne. After the death of Kasorayn, the last Druid King, they remained dormant within sacred seeds entrusted to the three main Druidic Circles. The regalia supposedly has no innate power of their own, but after a pretender stole the Druid King's Regalia, they almost brought upon the Green Scourge which would have called forth the wrath of nature upon Tamriel but they were slain before being able to do so.

The Regalia serves to crown one as Druid King, said to be the only one who can safely invoke and command even the greater [spirits of nature](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Nature_Spirit). A wielder of the Regalia can also command a nature spirit to merge with them in order to gain its power. The Regalia can also be used to allow a nature spirit to bind itself to an area and take on a new role, replacing that region's prior spirit, such an event occurred when the spirit Frii became the new spirit of [Mount Firesong](Lore_Y%27ffelon.md) in order to prevent the volcano from erupting and destroying the [Systres](Lore_Systres.md) archipelago. Though the original Regalia was lost in the volcano and destroyed by the magma, the nature spirit Frii had foreseen that would occur and granted the [Vestige](Lore_The_Vestige.md) new sacred seeds to plant. It is said that from the tree grown from those sacred seeds, a new Regalia would one day grow.

[![](https://images.uesp.net/thumb/d/dc/MW-item-Eleidon%27s_Ward.jpg/150px-MW-item-Eleidon%27s_Ward.jpg)](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:MW-item-Eleidon%27s_Ward.jpg) [](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:MW-item-Eleidon%27s_Ward.jpg) Eleidon's Ward
#### [Eleidon's Ward](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Eleidon%27s_Ward)
[Eleidon's Ward](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Eleidon%27s_Ward) is an enchanted shield especially built for [Eleidon](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Eleidon), a renowned holy Breton knight of legend. One of the many stories about him is that he saved a baron's daughter from sure death at the hands of a warlord, and the baron spent all his riches on the creation of the shield to show his gratitude. Eleidon's eponymous shield grants the wielder the opportunity to heal wounds.

[![](https://images.uesp.net/thumb/3/3b/ON-item-Lady_Garick%27s_Sacred_Shield.png/150px-ON-item-Lady_Garick%27s_Sacred_Shield.png)](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:ON-item-Lady_Garick%27s_Sacred_Shield.png) [](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:ON-item-Lady_Garick%27s_Sacred_Shield.png) Lady Garick's Sacred Shield
#### [Lady Garick's Sacred Shield](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Lady_Garick%27s_Sacred_Shield)
[Lady Joslin Garick](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Joslin_Garick) was a premier Breton captain for the [All Flags Navy](Lore_All_Flags_Navy.md). Aside from her exploits, she was known for what she referred to as her ["Sacred Shield"](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Lady_Garick%27s_Sacred_Shield). She claimed her eponymous ward was blessed by a saint of [Arkay](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Arkay), though long after her passing, legends would paint it as Arkay himself that endowed his power into it. The shield was said to preserve the wielder's life, in that no injury would befall them. The legends seemed to have some merit, for her crew would always return safely. However, the one instance she left her shield behind for safe keeping was her last voyage, as she and her crew met their demise during the All Flags Navy's assault on [Thras](Lore_Thras.md).

[](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:ON-icon-armor-Ring_of_the_Pale_Order.png) [](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:ON-icon-armor-Ring_of_the_Pale_Order.png) Ring of the Pale Order
#### [Ring of the Pale Order](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Ring_of_the_Pale_Order)
The [Ring of the Pale Order](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Ring_of_the_Pale_Order) is a signet ring once belonging to a prominent member of the now-defunct Bretonic Knights of the Pale Order, who were notorious for their persecution of the [Direnni](Lore_Direnni.md) during the final stages of their flight to Balfiera, around or after the ninth century of the [First Era](Lore_First_Era.md).<sup>[[nb 7]](#intnote_Pale)</sup> Its enchantments shape the wearer’s behavior, driving them toward isolation and ritualized violence to draw out the ring’s full power. It is said to radiate a cold surge of energy and a deep, nagging paranoia, invigorating the wearer as they inflict damage in combat. The enchantment, however, weakens in the presence of allies, becoming less potent the more companions accompany the wearer. Consequently, members of the Pale Order were known for keeping their own company, and rumors persist that they and their associates were [vampires](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Vampires) or practitioners of dark magics. It was not uncommon to see knights of the Pale Order drenched in blood, their strength growing with each passing battle.

The artifact’s power derives from its intricate design. The band itself is broad, heavy, and golden, forming the ring’s sturdy base. A groove along the interior bears an elegy for all those slain by the wearer in unassisted triumphs, along with the engraving, “Killed at my hand,” reflecting the deeply personal and ritualized nature of violence within the Order. The gallery rail, a style dating to the fifth century of the First Era, carries the inscription, “Vigor through Blood,” suggesting that physical strength, endurance, or even vitality itself was believed to increase through killing. Polished onyx stones flank the ring’s signet, engraved with “Austerity, Autonomy, and Ferocity,” a behavioral mandate that explains why the knights neither [married](Lore_Marriage.md), traveled together, nor maintained close social bonds. The ring thus reinforced isolation and self-surveillance, turning its wearer inward and away from society. Though it is unknown whether the original owner of the Ring of the Pale Order was a vampire, the signet identifies them as a member of [House Aurmine](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:House_Aurmine), vassals to the despotic king of [Shornhelm](Lore_Shornhelm.md), Festrien Spenard I, who is believed to have been a vampire posing as all six rulers of the Spenard dynasty.

[![](https://images.uesp.net/thumb/5/54/ON-item-Shade_Sickle.jpg/150px-ON-item-Shade_Sickle.jpg)](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:ON-item-Shade_Sickle.jpg) [](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:ON-item-Shade_Sickle.jpg) Shade Sickle
#### [Shade Sickle](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Shade_Sickle)
The [Shade Sickle](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Shade_Sickle) is a Breton -made [weapon](Lore_Weapons.md) with the ability to separate the living from their [shadows](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Shadow). This leaves its victims fated to gradually become hapless beings akin to thralls. Though mortal in origin, it is now a daedric [artifact](Lore_Artifacts.md) associated with the [Daedric Prince](Lore_Daedric_Princes.md) [Nocturnal](Lore_Nocturnal.md), who was given the weapon at one point after its potential was realized. Nocturnal considers it a powerful instrument of her will. Despite its common appearance, the blade is preternaturally sharp, and those who gaze at it experience a deep sense of foreboding.

- [![](https://images.uesp.net/thumb/6/68/MW-race-Breton_03.jpg/200px-MW-race-Breton_03.jpg)](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:MW-race-Breton_03.jpg) A Breton warrior during the Third Era (Morrowind)
- [![](https://images.uesp.net/thumb/4/47/LO-misc-Port_of_Wayrest.jpg/67px-LO-misc-Port_of_Wayrest.jpg)](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:LO-misc-Port_of_Wayrest.jpg) Sketch of the Port of Wayrest by '[¥R](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:%C2%A5R)'
