(Oblivion Remastered)

## Concept and design
- Bretons traditionally occupy the role of the [European](https://www.wikipedia.org/wiki/European) [medieval](https://www.wikipedia.org/wiki/Middle_Ages) race in The Elder Scrolls universe.<sup>[[UOL 20]](#cite_note-ESOEGT-485)</sup> Their depiction draws primarily from the real-world [Bretons](https://www.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bretons), the [French](https://www.wikipedia.org/wiki/French),<sup>[[UOL 21]](#cite_note-DGI-486)</sup> [Celts](https://www.wikipedia.org/wiki/Celts), and overall [Western European](https://www.wikipedia.org/wiki/Western_Europe) imagery.<sup>[[UOL 22]](#cite_note-ESOCGM-487)</sup> - [Breton naming conventions](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Breton_Names) often match those of Western Europe, with examples including [*Mathieu*](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Oblivion:Mathieu_Bellamont), [*Louis*](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Online:Louis_Ervine), [*Emeric*](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Online:High_King_Emeric), [*Javier*](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Online:Javier_Viliane), [*Gabrielle*](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Online:Gabrielle_Benele), [*Sara*](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Online:Sara_Benele), and [*Isabelle*](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Online:Isabelle_Onis).
- Breton society likewise reflects medieval [Europe](https://www.wikipedia.org/wiki/Europe), particularly its kingdoms, [feudal](https://www.wikipedia.org/wiki/Feudalism) structures, knightly orders, and literary traditions such as the [Arthurian legend](https://www.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arthurian_literature), among others.<sup>[[UOL 1]](#cite_note-ON2022-9)</sup> Elements of [Thronesian](https://www.wikipedia.org/wiki/Game_of_Thrones) political intrigue have also served as an influence.<sup>[[UOL 3]](#cite_note-ESOLI-30)</sup>
- Breton culture on [High Isle](Lore_High_Isle.md) in the [Systres Archipelago](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Systres_Archipelago) also shows some medieval [Germanic](https://www.wikipedia.org/wiki/Germanic_peoples) influences,<sup>[[UOL 20]](#cite_note-ESOEGT-485)</sup> while the island itself is partly inspired by the [ancient Roman](https://www.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ancient_Rome) resort town of [Baiae](https://www.wikipedia.org/wiki/Baiae), particularly in its association with hedonism and nearby volcanic activity.<sup>[[UOL 22]](#cite_note-ESOCGM-487)</sup>
- The Druid subculture draws inspiration from the [Moai](https://www.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moai), [Olmecs](https://www.wikipedia.org/wiki/Olmecs), and [Stonehenge](https://www.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stonehenge) in its architecture. Its use of [rock-cut architecture](https://www.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rock-cut_architecture) was also influenced by sites in [Anatolia](https://www.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anatolia), including the [Lycian tombs in Dalyan](https://www.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lycia) and [Göreme Historical National Park](https://www.wikipedia.org/wiki/G%C3%B6reme_Historical_National_Park).<sup>[[465]](#cite_note-FDTZ-488)</sup>

## Notes
- | [^](#note_Systres) | The Morrowind Codex map denotes provinces by color, and has the Systres Archipelago with the same color as Hammerfell.<sup>[[466]](#cite_note-MCMap-489)</sup> |
| --- | --- |
- | [^](#note_Reachmen) | Although they are thought to share descent, Bretons do not consider themselves kin to the Reachmen, and the Reachmen do not see themselves as Bretons.<sup>[[467]](#cite_note-Lore Answers-490)</sup><sup>[[468]](#cite_note-ABAYQ-491)</sup> This sentiment is shared by other races.<sup>[[469]](#cite_note-ESOContraband OEEC-492)</sup> |
| --- | --- |
- | [^](#note_Hill_Giants) | Rivenspire in ESO was [originally planned](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Online:Cut_Content_Rivenspire#The_Hillmen_of_Rivenspire) to include the spirits of these race of giants that were called "hill giants". The region would have also had Bretons with hill giant heritage called hillmen that were larger than the average person, similar to the [half-giant](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Half-Giant) race. These hillmen would have also had some Nordic heritage. Only a loading screen hinting at these hill giant's existence remains in the final game, but the term hillmen still appears as a demonym for Rivenspire's people in the book *[The Fury of King Ranser](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:The_Fury_of_King_Ranser)* in reference to [Ranser](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Ranser). |
| --- | --- |
- | [^](#note_Chimer) | The time period of the book *[King Edward](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:King_Edward)* takes place after the founding of Wayrest, which is after the Chimer became the Dunmer. *[The Real Barenziah](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:The_Real_Barenziah)* places Edward and Moraelyn banishing the Nords long before this, when the Dunmer were still the Chimer. |
| --- | --- |
- | [^](#note_Desynan) | The book *[On the War of Righteousness](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:On_the_War_of_Righteousness)* states that the Alessian Order refrained from sending a military response to High Rock until after the marriage between the children of King Desynan of Skingrad and Queen Margert Gardner of Wayrest in [1E 2319](Lore_First_Era.md#1E_2319). |
| --- | --- |
- | [^](#note_Architecture) | In the Systres Archipelago, druidic architecture is intended to invoke the feeling of a culture that has embraced nature yet is not primitive.<sup>[[465]](#cite_note-FDTZ-488)</sup> |
| --- | --- |
- | [^](#note_Pale) | House Spenard ruled for 180 years before being dissolved by House Dorell, a house that did not emerge until the ninth century of the First Era.<sup>[[470]](#cite_note-ONRKT-493)</sup><sup>[[336]](#cite_note-NAA-354)</sup> |
| --- | --- |
- In *[A History of Daggerfall](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:A_History_of_Daggerfall)*, the Direnni were originally described as native Bretons. Although they are described to be predominantly Altmer in later content, they still have some [humans](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Chimere_Graegyn) in their ranks.
- Bretons have a higher tolerance to [alcohol](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Alcoholic_Beverages) but take longer to recover.<sup>[[471]](#cite_note-ARAlcoholic-494)</sup>
- Artist Dennis Mejillones, who created the NPC model art for *[Skyrim](Skyrim_Skyrim.md)*, mentioned this in regards to the aesthetic of Bretons: "I put all my [facial] features in the game, so I can make myself in the game, so I actually drew my eyebrows that's one of your options, and the facial hair -- all that stuff. So I even had screen capture somewhere of myself [as] my character the game, it was the Bretons." Jonah Lobe asks, "So basically the Bretons are Cubans?" to which Dennis responded, "Basically yeah, in my mind [laughs]!"<sup>[[UOL 23]](#cite_note-Jonah Lobe-495)</sup>
- [Julian Le Fay](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/General:Julian_Le Fay), the game director of *[Daggerfall](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Daggerfall:Daggerfall)*, has a thick Danish accent, and narrates the introduction and endings of *[Daggerfall](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Daggerfall:Daggerfall)* himself. He also voices the Ghost of King [Lysandus](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Lysandus), which would mean the Bretons, at least those of [Daggerfall](Lore_Daggerfall_(kingdom).md) possessed the real world Danish accent of Le Fay. However, this was obviously not carried forward for later games.<sup>[[472]](#cite_note-Daggerfall Cinematics-496)</sup>

## See Also
- For a list of notable Bretons, see [here](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Category:Lore-People-Breton).
- For game-specific information, see the [*Arena*](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Arena:Breton), [*Daggerfall*](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Daggerfall:Breton), [*Battlespire*](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Battlespire:Breton), [*Morrowind*](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Morrowind:Breton), [*Shadowkey*](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Shadowkey:Breton), [*Oblivion*](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Oblivion:Breton), [*Skyrim*](Skyrim_Breton.md), [*Elder Scrolls Online*](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Online:Breton), [*Legends*](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Legends:Breton), [*Blades*](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Blades:Breton), and [*Castles*](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Castles:Breton) articles. Also see the [*Redguard* category](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Category:Redguard-Breton).

### Books
- ***[A History of Daggerfall](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:A_History_of_Daggerfall)*** by [Odiva Gallwood](Lore_Books_by_Author.md#Odiva_Gallwood) — A relatively unbiased analysis of Daggerfall and the Iliac Bay
- ***[Ark'ay The God](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Ark%27ay_The_God)*** by [Mymophonus the Scribe](Lore_Books_by_Author.md#Mymophonus) — How Ark'ay was transformed from a shopkeeper into the God of Birth and Death
- ***[Bangkorai, Shield of High Rock](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Bangkorai,_Shield_of_High_Rock)*** by King [Eamond](Lore_Books_by_Author.md#Eamond) — King Eamond's address to his troops at Bangkorai Garrison
- ***[Banker's Bet](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Banker%27s_Bet)*** by [Porbert Lyttumly](Lore_Books_by_Author.md#Porbert_Lyttumly) — A humorous story of what people will do for money
- ***[Crafting Motif 5: Breton Style](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Crafting_Motif_5__Breton_Style)*** by [Doctor Alfidia Lupus](Lore_Books_by_Author.md#Doctor_Alfidia_Lupus) — Notes on materials and motifs used in Breton armor
- ***[Etiquette With Rulers](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Etiquette_With_Rulers)*** by [Erystera Ligen](Lore_Books_by_Author.md#Erystera_Ligen) — The etiquette of speaking with nobles
- ***[Fahamal, Trader](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Fahamal,_Trader)*** by [Fahamal](Lore_Books_by_Author.md#Fahamal) — A Redguard's thoughts on the Breton use of magic
- ***[Holidays of the Iliac Bay](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Holidays_of_the_Iliac_Bay)*** by [Theth-i](Lore_Books_by_Author.md#Theth-i) — An overview of Breton and Redguard holidays commonly celebrated in the Iliac Bay region
- ***[Legacy of the Bretons](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Legacy_of_the_Bretons)*** A series of musings by [Stefan Mornard](Lore_Books_by_Author.md#Stefan_Mornard) — A look at the cultural dual-nature of the Breton people
- ***[Mara's Tear](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Mara%27s_Tear)*** by [Zhen](Lore_Books_by_Author.md#Zhen) — An origin myth for the two moons, Mara's Tear and Shandar's Sorrow
- ***[Modern Day Bretons: Man or Mer?](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Modern_Day_Bretons__Man_or_Mer%3F)*** by Vastyr Historian [Filibert Beauchamp](Lore_Books_by_Author.md#Filibert_Beauchamp) — A historian's treatise on why Bretons are more Mer than Man
- **[*Pocket Guide to the Empire, 1st Edition: High Rock*](Lore_Pocket_Guide_to_the_Empire,_1st_Edition_High_Rock.md) — [Imperial Geographical Society](Lore_Imperial_Geographical_Society.md), [2E 864](Lore_Second_Era.md#2E_864)**
- **[*Pocket Guide to the Empire, 3rd Edition: The Sons and Daughter of the Direnni West: High Rock*](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Pocket_Guide_to_the_Empire,_3rd_Edition_High_Rock) — [Imperial Geographical Society](Lore_Imperial_Geographical_Society.md), [3E 432](Lore_Third_Era.md#3E_432)**
- ***[Systres History](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Systres_History)*** by [Trilam Heladren](Lore_Books_by_Author.md#Trilam_Heladren), Associate Dean of Eltheric History, [University of Gwylim](Lore_University_of_Gwylim.md) — A history of the Systres archipelago
- ***[The Bretons: Mongrels or Paragons?](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:The_Bretons__Mongrels_or_Paragons%3F)*** by [Phrastus of Elinhir](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Phrastus_of_Elinhir) — An essay surrounding the ancestral roots of the Bretons
- ***[The Light and the Dark](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:The_Light_and_the_Dark)*** by [Irek Unterge](Lore_Books_by_Author.md#Irek_Unterge) — A Breton man describes the Light and the Dark to his two grandchildren
- ***[The Viridian Sentinel](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:The_Viridian_Sentinel)*** — A children's story surrounding the legend of the Viridian Sentinel
- ***[Uncommon Taste](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Uncommon_Taste)*** by [The Gourmet](Lore_Books_by_Author.md#Balagog_gro-Nolob) — A cook book containing recipes of a Breton origin
- ***[Wayrest, Jewel of the Bay](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Wayrest,_Jewel_of_the_Bay)*** by [Sathyr Longleat](Lore_Books_by_Author.md#Sathyr_Longleat) — A history of the city Wayrest, circa 3E 405
- ***[Wyrd and Druid](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Lore:Wyrd_and_Druid)*** Transcribed from [Archdruid Barnabe](Lore_Books_by_Author.md#Archdruid_Barnabe)'s Discourse with Mainlanders, 2E 553 — The druidic origins of the Bretons, as told by a Stonelore archdruid
